might no wayes escape; his God from
the heauens sent horses and fierie chariots,
filling the mountaines round about Elisha,
                     2. King. 6. 14. 15. 16. 17.
so that there was moe with him then
there was with his enemies.Act. 5. 16. The Apostles
found this, when being imprisoned for
preaching in the name of Iesus, they had
the Angel of the Lord by night readie to
open the prison doore, and to bring them
forth. Secondly when death shall approach
the child of God by sea, by land,
in companie, and alone, in the hands of
friends, in the hands of foes; albeit the
husband be absent from his wife, and the
wife from the husband: the child from the
parent, or the parent from the child, and
so forth: yet the poorest distressed loathsome
Lazarus being Gods child,Luk. 16. 22. shall
haue these blessed Angels to attend him,
who shall not be wearie night and day
to stand by his bed till his soule leaue his
body, to the effect by them it may be conueyed
to his fathers house. Thirdly, in the
end of the world these blessed spirits, shall
not refuse to gather the verie dead bones
of the dead bodies of Gods children to
the end that their bodies being ioyned
with their soules; they may in bodie and

soule raigne and rest with these Angels
before God for euermore; according to
that, sweetly sounded by our Maister:
The sonne of man shall come in the cloudes of
heauen with power and great glorie,
                     Mat. 24. 30. 31. 
                     and he
shall send his Angels with a great sound of a
trumpet, and they shall gather together his
elect from the foure winds, and from the one
end of the heauen to the other. Oh, ô my
soule, when shall my heart begin to separate
it selfe from earthly and sensuall
thoughts, and meditate a little vpon these
things? Surely, surely, couldst thou, ô my
soule, consider rightly that thy God
would offer by them to thy consideration,
sure I am thou wouldst draw foure seueral
& soueraigne lessons out of this discourse
hath bene brought to thy eares, by him
who made thee, and loueth thee deerely.
And first, thou wilt see that great care the
Lord thy God hath of thee, out of that
great loue wherewith he loued thee,
which moued him to make and appoint
so heauenly a hoast to attend thee, for the
gaurding and keeping of thee. Secondly,
this would stirre thee vp iointly to feare
and loue this God, to feare him, who alwayes
hath in readinesse such a great

armie of spirits to execute his will and to
take his part against all such dare abuse
him or his children in any sort. Knowest
thou not, ô my soule, that thy God in
one night, by an Angel, smote in the
the campe of Ashur an hundredth fourescore
and fiue thousand,Esay 37. 36. who durst rise vp
against him and against his people? Let
this stirre thee vp, ô my soule, 
                        •
                     o loue this
God who hath them all in his hands readie
to be imployed to saue, to comfort,
and to deliuer thee. Thirdly, let the sense
hereof make vs ashamed to speake that,
to do that, either priuately out of companie,
or publickely before others, which is
repugnant to the good will of God, and
which thou wilt be ashamed to speake
before any religious honest man: seeing
thy words, speake them where thou canst;
thy deedes, do them where thou wilt; are
heard or seene by those Angels who alwayes
attends thee. It were good that
both men and women did hearken to that
watch-word vsed by the Apostle.1. Cor. 11. 16. 
                     Therefore
ought the woman to haue power on her
head, because of the Angels. For as these
Angels, being beholders and markers of
our carriage, and actions, are reioyced

and incouraged as it were by our good
behauiour; so are they greeued by our
leud life, and prophane carriage. Finally
and lastly, this would comfort thee, ô my
soule, vnder, and against all our troubles,
considering that our Father, redeemer,
and comforter; hath appointed these heauenly
spirits his messengers, to be our
painfull nurses, and faithfull pedagogues,
whatsoeuer our estate be here to the
iudgement of blind men; but specially
this should strengthen vs against that
fearefull day of death, in the which this
dustie tabernacle must be layed downe,
making thee, ô my soule, thus triumphing
ouer death, to speake to thy selfe; let me
not be cast downe, because death approacheth
me, because these my eares
shall be closed from hearing any more among
men here, because my eyes shall be
stopped, frō seeing any more among men
here, from henceforth neuer shall I heare
that, see that, or do that which may offend
my God, and beside that I shall heare
such things (in that palace to the which
I am going) see such things, feele, and
possesse such things; which in sweetnesse
and excellence, shall farre surmount all

heretofore seene, felt, and possessed by me;
yea, let it not trouble me, that this my
clay bodie, which lieth here vnder sicknesse,
pined sore in euerie member of it,
destitute of father, mother, husband, wife,
brother, sister, or any liuing whatsoeuer,
to care for it; seeing that blessed Spirit
the comforter of Gods elect lodgeth
within me, assuring me that God is mine,
and I am his; and considering these heauenly
spirits, attendeth my sicke and
pained bodie which they shall not
forsake, till breath forsake it; for
howbeit these spirits my attendants, be
nor seene by these my corporall dimme
eyes, yet I am clearely seene of them, and
assuredly granted by them, acorrding to
that charge they haue receiued of that
great Angel of the couenant who
gaue himselfe for me, and who
hath ordained to attend me,
till they bring me
where he is.
               
            
         
         
            
               
                  
                  SIXE
CVNNING
AND CRVELL
Robbers, hauing the heads of
Doues, but the tailes of Scorpions:
sent from the bottomlesse pit, by the
arch-enemie of Gods babes, to withdraw
them from the path-way which
leadeth to the paradise of God; and
for drawing them towards and holding
them on, in that by-way which
tendeth downewards vnto that
lake, out of the which there
is no redemption.
                  MAT. 10. 16.
                  Behold I send you as sheepe in the midst of woolues, be
ye therefore wise as serpents, and simple as doues.
                  REVEL. 12. 7. 8.
                  And there was a battell in heauen, Michael and his
Angels fought against the Dragon; and the Dragon
and his Angels fought, but they preuailed not.
                  BERN.
                  
                     Hic mundus, non est nisi nemus, plenum latronibus,
ideo per illud est cautè ambulandum. This world,
is nothing but a wood, layed full of Robbers; and
therefore it is needfull that we walke circumspectly
through it.
               
               
                  
                  
                  TO THE SINCERELY
RELIGIOVS
and truly vpright, Sir GEORGE
HAY of Kinphains Knight; great
Chancellar of Scotland; Counseller
to his most excellent Maiestie in
both the kingdomes.
                  
                     LVke the Euāgelist,Luke 1. 1. 2. 3. knowing
that that most Noble
Theophilus was wel instructed
in that misterie of
Christ; dedicated to him,
First, that sacred Historie of the Incarnation,
life, death, buriall, Resurrection,
and Ascension of that God-man,Acts. 1. 1.
and man-God Iesus blessed for
euermore; and thereafter that heauenly
Historie of the holy Acts of
his faithfull Apostles. And shall anie
thing be able to dash me (treading

the cleane pathes of so wise a leader,
of so holy a Maister) my verie religious
Noble good Lord, in dedicating
this part of my Heauenly Chariot vnto
your Lordship, if it shall please my
blessed good God by his Spirit to
moue your good Lordship to daigne
your selfe to accept of it? Certaine it
is, that since that lamed souldier Ignatius
Layola of abominable memory,
had his orderles bloudie order, first
confirmed at Rome by Paulus the
third,Anno. 1540. by the meanes of Cardinall
Conteran: that these Robbers, his lying
cruell broode, (here offered vnto
your Lordships view) compassed
neuer this kingdome (with Satan that
lier, that murtherer from the beginning
their Maister) so frequently, so
busily, so boldly as they do now at
this present, for the surprising of the
soules, and ouerthrowing of the bodies
of Gods Saints among vs. Alwayes
when I thinke vpon that light
of God which shineth cleerely in

your Lordships vnderstanding, I see
(to the great comfort of all such louers
of Christ among vs) one able to
take them vp a far off, and to discerne
them. When I thinke vpon that loue
and zeale of God (which burneth
strongly in your Lordships heart) I
meet one, readily willing, seeing them
and discouering them, to pursue them
till they be apprehended. And when
I cast my eyes vpon that high chaire
(in the which not mortal weake man,
but that immortall strong Monarch,
hath euen at such a time placed your
Lordship) I lay hold on one, carying
an armed hand, able exemplarlie
to punish them being apprehended,
and who knoweth whither your
Lordship be come to this chaire,Esth. 4. 14. at
such a time for this end? These Robbers
being that Goliah, your Lordships
good and wise guide hath most
wisely cast in your Lordships way,
to reuile your Lordship, to defie your
Lordship, yea to reuile, and to defie

to your Lordships hearing, the host
of the Lord: to the end that your
Lordship as his Dauid, sent out by
him against them, may haue them
falling downe dead at your Lordships
feete: and thereafter haue their heads
carried in triumph before your Lordship,
as a manifest euidence to the
world, that that God of hosts, euen
the God of the host of Israel (vpon
whom they haue too long railed) is
with your Lordship. The by-gone
proofes of your Lordships carriage,
and vpright dealing in euery thing,
hath bred such hopes in the hearts of
all feares God, that they expect this:
hath brought such astonishment to
the contrarie minded, that they looke
for this. My good Lord, let not your
Lordships sincere true friends be disappointed,
let not your Lordships
periured, lying, aduersaries be frustrated.
Cleon the Lacedaemonian being
set ouer the Commonwealth to gouerne
it, sent for all his friends, and

discharged himselfe of their friendship,
knowing that friendship hath
made many men oftentimes to erre
in iudgement: and shall your Lordships
kinsmen and acquaintances offend
(if your Lordship resembling in
your happie gouernment, that holy
one who gaue himselfe for you) shall
say to these who shall come to your
Lordship in chamber, in counsell, or
in Session:Mat. 12. 49. 50. 
                     Behold my mother, and my
brother, for whosoeuer shall do the will
of God (and so haue a good action) the
same shall be my brother, my mother, and
my sister. The Emperour Vitellus hauing
refused the petition of one of his
speciall friends which was vnreasonable,
and hearing him (waxing angry)
said to him: What auaileth thy friendship
to me, since I cannot obtaine that
which I craue? did answer religiously,
prudently, and calmely. And what
auaileth thy friendship to me, if for thee
I must do that which is vnlawfull? And
shall your Lordship hold these for

your Lordships friends, or account
these worthie of your Lordships fauor,
who shall attempt to desire your
Lordship to speake or to do that for
them which may prouoke your Lordships
good God to wrath? My deare
Lord, if diuels shall afterward assault
your Lordship, if men shall be bold,
either by faire promises to allure your
Lordship from good vnto euill, or by
sharpe threatenings to menace your
Lordship to refuse good, and to embrace
euill? let that holily & happily
spoken by Iosaphat to these Iudges
deputed by him, be alwayes remembred
by your Lordship:2. Chron. 19. 6. 7. 
                     Take heede
what ye do, for ye execute not the iudgement
of men, but of the Lord, and he will
be with you in the cause and iudgement.
Wherefore now let the feare of the Lord
be vpon you. Take heede and do it, for
there is no iniquitie with the Lord your
God, neither respect of persons, nor receiuing
of rewards. Suffer me, my verie
Noble good Lord, here to present my

blessed Lord and loue, euen that great
Angell of the couenant before your
Lordship, setting your Lordship to
this his worke, strengthening your
Lordship for this his worke, and fully
incouraging your Lordship against
all difficulties your Lordship possibly
can meete with, in vndergoing
and vnderlying this his worke. The
Lord is with thee thou valiant man.
                     Iud. 6. 12. 14. 16. 
                     Go
in this thy might, and thou shalt saue
my Israel, in Scotland out of the
hāds of these bloudy robbing Midianites,
the Iesuites: haue not I sent thee,
I will be with thee, and thou shalt smite
them as one man. He who made an
house to the midwiues of Egypt, shal
not forget to build an house to your
Lordship. He who iustly made the
names of Doeg, Sanballat, Tobiah, and
Haman to stinke, and who mercifully
made the names of Nehemiah, Esdrah,
and Mordecai to smell sweetly, shall in
despight of all hellish and earthly
powers, keepe your Lordships name

from all infection, and made it to be
sweet and fragrant to all future ages;
yea, shall write it in the Lambes book
of life, that after your Lordship hath
serued your King and Soueraigne
Lord here for a while, your Lordship
may be hereafter, for euer, where that
your Lordships Lord & Soueraigne
is:Ioh. 13. 16. for the which till I breathe, I shall
not ceasse heartily and humbly to
draw vp my simple prayers to God.
                  
                     Your Lordships most
humbly deuoted,
D. L.
                  
               
            
            
               
                  
                     
                     THE FIRST ROBBER IS
the Popish Seminarie obscuring from
the child of God, that shining Lanterne
of Gods written word (presented
before him for leading of him towards
the heauens his Fathers house)
vnder an vnknowne language.
                     
                        HE is not sensible of God
who reading that third of
Genesis, ô my soule, laments
not that Euah
hearkening vnto the Serpent,
should haue so easily
condescended to neglect, and forget
that vndoubted true solid lesson brought
to her eares by the louing voice of God,
her gracious maker, and onely true friend;
and contented her selfe, first to haue hearkened
vnto a lying lesson, and thereafter
to embrace it, brought from his deceitfull
lippes who prooued her deadly foe; first
betraying her, and then destroying her.

When we reade the 13. and 16. Chapters
of Iudges, we all cōdemne Samson of folly
& rashnesse, who knowing that Almighty
God had ordained no rasor to come
on his head (but that he should remaine a
Nazareth to the Lord) was moued by the
importunate dealing of his deceiuing Dalilah,
to shew her, that if he were shauen
his strength would go from him, and that
he would be weake and like vnto other
men. And yet when shall we begin, ô my
soule, to pitie not one Euah, but a world
of Euahs: not one Samson, but a very world
of Samsons: who content themselues in
these our dayes, alas, to passe by and neglect,
yea, to despise and reuile those onely
wholsome, and onely true sauing lessons
which flowes from the mouth of yt their
Father, which neither can deceiue, nor
lie; hearkening in the meane time 
                           •
                        o those
poysoned and poysoning lessons, inuented
by the deceitfull heart of that man of sin,
and his followers, and vented by the treacherous,
smooth, yet slaying lippes of his
busie agents; yea, not onely hearkening
to them when they come towards them,
but longing for them, yea, waiting for
them, if they appeare to stay for any space

from them, and which is more, heartily
contented to begger their children, and
ruine their houses, to the end they may
feed and nourish them Knowest thou not,
ô my soule, that Satan by that serpent the
Pope, and his agents, by that Dalilah the
Pope, and his suffragants (knowing what
fruite is able to feed the child of God, and
what fruite doth slay him; what wil make
the child of God strong and able to withstand
him, and his vncircumcised confederates,
and what will make the child of
God first weake, and then a prey to him
that in the end he may mocke him) these
many yeares by-past, hath bene withdrawing
the world from the mouth of
God, and the mouth of God from the
world,The light of the word couched by the Papists vnder an vnknowne language. speaking to it by holy written
Scripture, by couching this cleare Lanterne
of Gods word vnder an vncouth
and vnknowne language: and yet he hath
so farre preuailed by this his busie double
dealing, that now our Euahs, that is, our
women who would be reputed noble and
wise; that now our Samsons, that is, our
men who would be accounted valorous;
cannot be moued to looke vpon that sacred
Booke of God, being translated in

their mother tongue, but abhorre to see it,
to reade it, or to heare it read vnto them,
as if it were the inditement of some infernall
spirit: for do these men or women abhorre
so much any vaine or profane pamphlet,
as they do the Bible in the vulgar
tongue? But will our God, informing vs
by Scripture, subscribe with the Pope his
aduersarie (exalting himselfe against all
that is called God,
                           
                              •
                           . Thes. 2. 4. or is worshipped, so that
he doth sit as God in the Temple of God,
shewing himselfe that he is God) in this
point?Our God speaketh to the Iewes in the Iewish language. no, no, our God, saith Scripture, is
to speake to his people the Iewes, & hath
them to instruct and direct about his worship,
and their saluation: alwayes in what
language will he speake vnto them? by
what language will he instruct them?
those who haue read the writings of Moses,
the Psalmes and the Prophets, yea, in a
word that whole volume of the old Testament,
do know and must confesse that our
wise God spake to the Iewes in the Iewish
language, and instructed the Iewes by the
Iewish language; for tell me, ô effronted
Seminarie, in what language were these
oracles of God,Rom. 3. 2. committed by God, vnto
the circumcised Iewes sounded, yea put

in Register. When the fulnesse of time
comes, our God hath not onely the Iewes
to speake vnto, and to instruct, but the
Gentiles also. Alwayes will he speake to
them in the Hebrew & Greeke language.
O robbing Seminarie, readest thou euer,
considerest thou euer, that direction
with the warrant thereof giuen by our
Maister vnto his disciples, Act. 1. 4. Considerest
thou euer that which according
to this promise befell the disciples▪ Act. 2.
1. 2. 3. 4? Iesus (blessed for euermore) who
came into the world to saue Jew and
Gentile, and so who by perswading Iaphet
to dwell in the tents of Sem, to make of
both one, must haue some men to be witnesses
both in Ierusalem, and in all Iudaea,
and Samaria, and vnto the vttermost part
of the earth. But must these men speake
one language or two? or onely these three
canonized by the Pope, Hebrew, Greeke,
and Latine, which the lying Papist doth
hold that our God hath separate for his
sacred and heauenly things? Not so, not
so, ô my soule, I trow, for in the day of
Pentecost not onely were the Apostles
heard by the Iewes in the Iewish tongue,
by the Grecians in their tongue, by the

Romanes in their tongue, but by the Parthians,
Medes, Elemites, Inhabitants of
Mesopotamia, Cappadocia, Pontus, Asia,
Phrygia,Act. 2. 9. 10. 11. Pamphilia, Egypt, Lybia, Cyren,
Cretes, and Arabians: all these, saith Scripture,
heard the Apostles speake the wonderous
workes of God in their owne
tongues.Wherefore were the Apostles gifted with the gift of tongues. And so it pleased our God that
day miraculously (yet most graciously) to
gift the Apostles his seruants with the gift
of tongues, to the end that they by speaking
euery language, might be able to discouer
the hid mysteries of Gods blessed
word to all people of euerie language, to
the end they might be saued.Obiect. But I know
that here the robbing cunning Seminarie
will alledge, that we do him great wrong,
and lye vpon him grosly, saying: We neither
condemne the vulgar translations of
Scripture, neither debarre we men from
the reading of them. Remember thy selfe,
ô tricking Seminarie,Answer. so shalt thou finde
that while thou appearest by the one hand
slowly to put holy Scripture in the hands
of Gods children, translated in their own
mother tongue; thou forgettest not
with both thy hands subtilly to pull it
from them againe. Know I not, ô Seminarie,

that these blind leaders of that troubled
conuenticle at Trent,The decree of the Cō

& can reade thē. And who be these I pray
thee? The parts of the ordinance of Trent
about this matter be foure, ô my soule:
first, that it is lawfull to none to reade the
Scriptures in the vulgar tongue, but vnto
them who haue liberty gra
                           •

                         Secondly,

Thirdly, that the Bishops suffer

them not to reade indifferently all vulgar
translations, but those onely which Catholicke
Romanes haue set forth. Fourthly,
that libertie be not granted to all men
to reade those, but to such as by the
iudgement of their confessor will receiue
no hurt by them, that is, to be plaine with
the cunning Seminarie, but to such whom
they hold as obstinate Papists, bond slaues
to the Pope, and auowed aduersaries to
the sauing truth of God, as they themselues
be. Now of these foure grounds
layed by the Tridentine councellers, two
things do follow: first, that these blind
leaders of the Romish Synagogue admit
verie few to reade the vulgar translations
of the holy Scripture. Secondly, that those
whom they admit to reade them, are none
beside their owne sworne men, who refusing
to heare the voice of that true shepheard
Iesus, haue sold themselues to depend
vpon these mercenary cruell wolues,
in the verie matter of their saluation. O
ancient Iewes, were you thus limited and
bounded by that doctrine which Moses
learned of God in the mountaine of God,The papists conditions are not by Scripture.
and which he brought from the mountaine
to you? O you sometimes the auditors

Iesus, were you thus marked by that great

of God, his sauing counsell, were you thus
tyed? I know that Philip heard the Eunuch
alacke, as the Papists speake reading a
portion of the Prophet Isaiah, but I heare
not Philip either magnifying him by what
Bishop and confessors aduice did he that,
or reprouing him for doing of it. Yea,

                        The Iesuite is a Iebusite. Be ashamed ô Iesuite
of thy proud blasphemous lying title, and
be content hereafter to call thy selfe a Iebusite,
for whilst thou banishest men and
women from Scripture, thou hearest blessed
Iesus, sending men and women to

                        Search the Scriptures, for in them
you thinke to haue eternall life, and they are

faithfull seruant charging the Colossians
thus: Let the word of God dwell in you plentiously.
Where the Spirit of God will haue
the whole elect of God, men, women,
old, and yong, learned, and vnlearned, to
be as it were as so many buildings; & this

blessed word of God contained in Scripture
to be as a guest not lodging for one
night but dwelling alwayes to the end in
them. That famous Bishop Chrysostome
handling this text at Constantinople,
tooke occasion thereupon to deale with
his people, to prouide themselues of Bibles,
at the least of the new Testament, to
the end that the husband with the wife,
and the parents with the children might
conferre at home vpon the misteries of
their saluation, praying them not to lay
the whole burthen therof vpon his shoulders.
For Chrysostome had not learned to
blindfold the babes of God so, that they
could thinke themselues sufficient certified
of life eternall, if they could beleeue
as the Church beleeued, albeit in the
meane time they knew not what the
Church beleeued.Theod lib. 5. de cor. grec. affec. 
                        Theodoretus hath a
worthy place to this purpose. Ye may
cōmonly see that our doctrine is knowne
not onely of them that are doctors of the
Church, and ministers of the people, but
also euen of the Taylors, and Smithes,
and Weauers, and of women, and that
not onely of learned, but of vnlearned,
and labouring women, and sempsters and

seruants, and hand-maids, neither onely
the citizenes, but also the countrie folkes
do verie well vnderstand the same. Ye
may find euen the verie diggers, and the
neat-heards, and the gardeners, disputing
of the holy Trinitie, and of the creation
of all things. Were these holy Fathers,
(who sometimes sed the babes of God
with the holy truth of God) liuing now?
I thinke they would condemne these hellish
foxes, who by their cruell hands slay
the bodies of the babes of God, and
by their lying lippes murther their
soules.Hieron. ad dem. I heare Hierom saying, ô my soule,

                        The hurt cometh by the ignorance of Scripture.

The ignorance of the Scripture, is the ignorance
of Christ; loue holy Scriptures, and
wisdome shall loue thee: as it is a greater thing
to do the will of God, then to know it, so it
must be first knowne before it be done. I
wonder how the Iesuite taketh that
speech of Augustine. Si Scripturas diuinas
aut non legimus ipsi, aut legentes alios libenter
non audimus, ipsa nobis medicamenta conuertantur
in vulnera, & inde habemus iudicium

vnde potuimus habere remedium. If either
we our selues reade not holy Scripture, or
gladly heare not others reading them vnto vs,
our verie medicine shall be turned vnto
woundes vnto vs: and of that we shall reape
condemnation, of the which we might haue
found health and saluation.
                        Obiection. I am not ignorant,
ô my soule, that the Popish seminarie
keeping vp holy Scripture from the
common people,That alledged benefit of ignorance & hurt, of reading Scripture remoued. and thereby detaining
them within the darke schoole of ignorance,
alledgeth most clearely (euen against
his conscience, albeit with a brasen
countenance) that he doth this for the
singular spirituall benefite of the common
people: for is not ignorance (if we may
tell the Seminarie) the mother of Deuotion?
and doth not the reading of Scripture
bring simple people vnder fearefull
heresies? Hearken neuer, ô my soule, vnto
the deceiuing and male-pert, lying Priest
making this allegation.
                           Answer. Iohn 4. Ignorance a fearefull mother of vile superstion & vncouth be resi
                              •
                           . For I assure
thee, being clearely taught of God, that
howbeit ignorance hath bene the onely
mother of abominable idolatrie, and superstitious
deuotion, making poore
soules with the deceiued Samaritans to
worship that which they know not, and

with the superstitious Athenians to set vp
an altar vnto an vnknowne God, yet ignorance
was neuer, neither euer shall be
the mother of that true religious deuotion
commanded by God, allowed of
God, and comfortable for the soule of
man. Ignorance hath bene, and euer shall
proue the mother of heresie, drawing
men from the true God, yea making
men (who professe themselues to know
the true God) to worship and to seeke
him falsly.Esay 8. 19. 20. O Isaiah was this doctrine vented
by thy cleane lips which were touched
with that coale which was taken of ye altar
of God, which now the vncleane lips
of the foule Seminarie toucheth, who hath
his conscience feared with a hot iron heat
in the fire of the bottomles pit. No, no, for
I heare Isaiah speaking thus to me: Should
not a people inquire at their God; from the liuing
to the dead, to the Law and the testimonie,
if they speake not according to this word,
it is because there is no light in them. And so
Isaiah here, ô my soule, maketh ignorance
to be the manifest and direct mother of
vile heresie. Doth blessed Iesus that true
teacher of the truth of God speake of ignorance
as the false Iesuite speaketh of

it? not I thinke: for heare I him not thus
speaking to the Saduces: You erre not
knowing the Scriptures and the power of God.
Teaching them therby that the ignorance
of the Scripture made them to denie that
rarest article of the beleefe, euen the resurrection
of our bodies; and consequently
that ignorance is the vile mother of vile
heresie. Yea hearest thou not, ô my soule,
that holy one thy Sauiour crying thus on
the Crosse:Mat. 22. 19. 
                        Father forgiue them, for they
know not what they are doing:
                        Lact. lib. 5. resoluing vs
hereby, that Ignorance is the fierce mother
of bloudie persecution. Lactantius
was not of the Papists opinion, albeit he
writ that with his penne which the Seminaries

for giuing his reason wherefore so few of

be two most mischieuous daughters of that
mischieuous mother, Ignorance; Falsitie, and
Doubting, that more miserable, this more to

When the spirit speaketh, they both do fall

& carefully, to haue that sacred volume of
holy Scripture kept vp from the babes of
God. Hearken, hearken, ô my soule, well
know they what holy Scripture is, and
what is to be found in it: and therefore
therefore they cannot suffer, they will not
suffer the babes of God to haue it, lest

they (led by Scripture) should be made
to know that which they know, Scripture
cannot but leade them vnto. What thefe
approaching a house of purpose to breake
it, desires to heare the crow of the cocke,
or the barke of the dogge, to see any
candle, or to be brought before any gallous?
for well knowes he that the crow
of the cocke, or the barke of the dogge
may waken some one within, and so hinder
him of his intent: and he cannot be
ignorant that the candle will deceiue
him, & the gallous destroy him. Now no
lesse clearely knowes the Papist, Scripture
to be that to him (in case it were knowne
by the common people) which the crow
of the cocke, the barke of the dogge, the
light of the candle, aud sight of the gallous
is to these. This moued Chrysostome
long ago thus to write touching Heretickes.Chrysost op. imp. Hom. 44.
                        Heretici sacerdotes, claudunt ianuas
veritatis. Sciunt enim si manifesta esset
veritas quod ipsorum ecclesia esset relinquenda,
& ipsi de sacerdotali dignitate ad
humilitatem venirent popularem. Hereticall
Priests do close vp the gates of the truth of
God: for they know that if that truth were
made manifest, and cleare to the world; that

their Church would be forsaken, and that
they themselues would be cast downe from
their priestly dignitie vnto the meanest estate
of the basest people.
                        Hireom. in Esa. lib. 9. cap. 30. This moued Hierome also
thus to write touching Heretickes. Sagittant
in obscuro rectos corde, istitantam sibi
assumunt authoritatem, vt siue dextra doceant,
siue sinistra, id est siue bona, siue mal
                              •
                           ,
nolunt discipulos ratione discutere, sed se praeceptores
sequi; tunc hi qui prius decipiebant
nequaquam vltro ad eos volebant accedere,
postquam se senferint intellectos. They shoote
their darts in secret at the vpright in heart.
These men challenge so great authoritie to
themselues, that whither they teach right, or
wrong, that is, good or euill; they will no wayes
haue their disciples to trie, or examine that
they teach but to follow their maisters
blindnesse: then these who first deceiued the
people, would not afterwards come to them
knowing that they were vnderstood and taken
vp. I perswade my selfe, ô my soule, were
that worthy man Petrus Ferrariensis liuing
to day, he would (directing his
speech to the Princes of the world and
specially of Europe) crie out as he did of
old. O miseros imperatores & seculares
Principes! qui haec & alia sustinetis, & vos

seruos ecclesiae facitis, & mundum per eos infinit
is modis vsurpari videtis, nec de remedio
cogitatis, & quia prudētiae & sapientiae non attēditis.
O miserable Emperours and Princes of
the world! who suffer these & other things, &
make your selues seruants of the Church,
and see the world innumerable wayes abused
by them, and yet do thinke vpon no remedie,
because you hearken not vnto prudence and
wisedome. For sure it is if the Princes and
people (misled this day by the Papists)
knew what God offers to them by Scripture,
what God craues of them by Scripture,
and how their leaders should carrie
themselues towards him, they would not
be misled any longer by them. No, no,
Iehu was neuer more forward in destroying
the altars of Baal,
                        2. King. 10. then they would
be readie to pull downe all their idolatrous
monuments.Acts 16. Those men of Ephesus
were not more willing to burne their
costly curious bookes, after they hard
and beleeued, then the Kings, the Princes
and the men, the women; now blindnesse
followes the blind Papists, would be to
burne all those pamphlets and monuments
of poperie put in their hands by
thē. And to conclude this point, sure I am

were Augustine liuing this day,Aug. Epist. 167. he would
direct his speech, against the Popish Seminaries
as he directed it long ago against
the Donatists. Puto quod ipse diabolus, si authoritate
Iudicis quem ipse eligeret, toties
vinceretur, non esset tam impudens vt in ea
causa persisteret. In my iudgement if the diuell
himselfe were so often ouercome by the authoritie
of the Iudge whom he had chosen to
himselfe, he would not be so impudent as to
persist in that cause.
                        The Papist is bewitched by foure intising Dalilaes so that he cannot be reclaimed. But alas, but alas, ô
my soule, these sonnes of that sonne of
perdition, be so bewitched by these foure
entycing and perswading Dalilaes to the
which by fearefull oathes they haue married
themselues the onely builders and
vpholders of that their Babel, (Auaritia,
Superbia, Ignoratio Scripturae, falsorum
Prophetarum admiratio. Couetousnes, Pride,
Ignorance of the Scripture, admiration of
false teachers) that nothing can reclaime
them. For my owne part, I pray God for
the sonne of his loues sake,Lact. lib. 4. cap. 30. when it shall
please him to enlighten the eyes of the
Papist Seminaries to see that, and to open
their mouthes to confesse that euen before
the simplest of the babes of God
which Chrysostome confessed to be most

true touching holy Scripture.Chrysost, hom. 3. de Lazaro. 
                        Magna aduersus
peccatum munitio est Scripturarum
lectio, magnum praecipitium, profundum barathrum
scripturarum ignoratio: magna salutis
perditio de diuinis legibus nihil sc
                              •
                           re, eares
haereses peperit, ea vitam corruptaminuexit,
hoc sursum deorsum miscuit omnia. The
reading of holy Scripture is a great fortresse
against sinne. The ignorance of holy Scripture
is a verie fearefull downefall to the deepest and
most dangerous dungeon. It is a great losse of
saluation to know nothing of the Lawes of
God: this hath bred heresie; this hath brought
in corrupt life, and vile manners; yea, this hath
turned all things vp and downe.
                     
                  
                  
                     THE SECOND ROBBER
is the Popish Seminarie, without conscience,
and with ashameles countenance,
blotting cleane, perfect
written Scripture; with the foule
blot of imperfection and subtiltie, obtruding
to the babes of God 
                           •
                        ound
Traditions.
                     THat euill one Satan,Satan ha
                           
                              •
                           eth Scripture deadly being neuer able
to forget that sensible foyle he receiued

at the hands of yt great Sauiour of the
world Iesus (drawing that two edged
sword of holy Scripture,Mat. 4. ouer, and ouer,
against him, euen while Satan cunningly
peruerting Scripture, pressed by bringing
of it against him, to abuse it to his
ouerthrow) hath alwayes kept in his
heart, a deadly vnrecouerable hatred
against holy Scripture; and therefore he
hath not contented himselfe by the crafty
and cruell trauels of the Popish Seminarie
onely, to hide vp that cleare light
which shineth in holy Scripture, from
the eyes of Gods babes. But besides this
he hath not bene affraid (so shameles is
that great enemie the god of this world,
so forward are these his agents first blinded
and then sent forth by him) euen to
accuse holy Scripture of a most grosse
fault, and blast it with a monstrous blemish,
holding and affirming, that euen
Scripture (the verie inditement of truth)
onely louing, onely pitifull, onely towards
the babes of God; louing them
with a loue vnspeakable and glorious: pitying
them with incomparable compassion:
and well knowing what they stand
in neede of, for keeping of them from

Satan and sinnes snare, and for leading
them straightly towards their expected
home) is no perfect booke containing in
it all things necessarie for mans saluation,
but imperfect, which must be supplied (as
they alledge) by their traditions and vnwritten
verities (as they call them) which
they affirme to be worthy of no lesse reuerence,
and authoritie then the verie
written word of God deliuered by the
Prophets of blessed Iesus, and his Apostles:
as that shamelesse first decree pronounced
from the deceiued and deceiuing
hearts, by the foule and defyling lips
of those apostat fathers of yt Councell of
Trent in that 4. Session plainely speaketh.
Now (which thou canst not but iustly
admire) ô my soule, the Popish Seminarie
hath so farre preuailed in this point also,
with the Euahes of this time, with the
Sampsons of this time, that as they will
not looke, vpon any condition almost, vpon
a Bible translated in their mother
tongue, so they will euen with greedinesse
lend both their eares vnto the found traditions
of the Popish Seminaries, albeit
they be the corrupt birth of his owne
brutish braine. Pitie ô God the Euahes of

this our time, hearkening vnto the Serpent,
but not to the Sauiour. Pitie ô God
that Sampsons of this time, hearkening
vnto the agents of that trecherous great
Dalilah, but not vnto that true glorious
Messias. Oh, ô my soule, what a world of
auditors and followers, found those blind
leaders of the blind Scribes and Pharises,
while thy Lord and Maister teaching in
the world, was forsaken of all? and therefore
wonder not while he is not teaching
in his owne person, but by his base
seruants, lying flatterers be honoured and
maintained, and that the onely true fathers
of the Church be condemned, and
murthered.The Pope and his be possessed by a strange spirit. This must be a strang Spirit,
ô my soule, which possesseth the Pope,
which possesseth his agents, yea, which
possesseth those who do follow him and
them, that he with them hath taken vpon
them to perfect holy Scripture as if in it
selfe it were maimed, and not onely to
darken it as if it were not cleare, but besides
this that they haue found credit in
these points with the Euahes and Sampsons
of this world. The written word of
God my Father I may not reade, I may
not heare in my mother tongue. And yet

the vnwritten inuentions of man I my
reade, I must reade in any tongue I can
vnderstand. That Scripture which leades
men thus, ô my soule, cannot possibly be
the spirit of the Father, the spirit of the
Sonne who is from aboue, but must be
some spirit who is from beneath, drawing
men from the true Father and Sauiour
of their soules, to some bastard father and
Sauiour, who in the end will proue an vnnaturall
Saul, seeking the life of his owne
Ionathan, and a cruell Herod murthering
those infants he should haue maintained.
Scripture condemnes, and all ages since
that time sensible of God, haue abhorred
Ieroboam the sonne of Nebat, for attempting
(contrarie to the will of God) to erect
an altar at Bethel, and another at Dan,
lest the people resorting to Ierusalem
(where God had appointed sacrifice onely
to be offered) should haue fallen away
from him to the house of Dauid: and shall
not God condemne, and should not all
men sensible of God abhorre these peart
Popish Seminaries who haue taken vpon
them to set vp in euery corner where they
can be heard, the calfes of their owne traditions,
drawing away men thereby from

the true oracles of Gods written word,
lest that they ceassing to dote after these
calfes, and hearkening to Gods oracles,
should giue themselues to seeke and serue
the liuing God, according to his commandement?
Now to the effect that the
Seminarie may make the calfes of his traditions
to shine the more brightly, and to
smile the more sweetly on such towards
whom they are drawne, they haue not
bene afraid to lay a most fearefull imputation
vpon our blessed God, and his sacred
truth; most lyingly (and yet most boldly)
affirming that all things requisite for
mans saluation be not contained in holy
Scripture. What, ô my soule, if the eyes of
men were enlightened with the eyes of
Dauid, to see the wonders of the Law of
God, and seeing these wonders to perceiue,
not that little drop, but that huge
quantitie of sweetest honie, the hungrie
child of God hath presented to his soule
by the Spirit, speaking vnto him by that 4.
verse of the 15. Chapter of that Epistle
written to the Romans, and by the 15. and
16. verses of the 3. Chapter of that second
Epistle written to Timothie? Beleeue me,
ô my soule, couldst thou weigh and consider

those two Scriptures aright, thou
shouldest find thy selfe euen by fiue words
(which I may iustly stile fiue bright
diamonds Almightie God will haue alwayes
to shine vpon the fiue fingers of his
owne, to direct their way wheresoeuer
they walke) shortly (yet most substantially)
acquainting thee so with the whole
vses of that blessed written word of God,
that thou shouldst be able to find that nothing
requisite to mans saluation is deficient
in it,Scripture containes all things requisite for mans saluation. that all things needfull to mans
saluation be fully & clearly contained in
it. Wilt thou not confesse, ô my soule, that
whatsomeeuer can concerne mans saluation
possibly, must either looke to doctrine
or to manners, or to comfort. If it
looke to doctrine, that doctrine is either
true which the child of God must seeke
after, and embrace, as he would seeke after
that meate which is onely able to feede
him, and after that medicine which is only
able to cure him; or false, which the
child of God must flie from, as he would
flie from poyson, slaying not his bodie
onely, but his soule also. If the doctrine be
true, that is abundantly and clearly taught
by holy Scripture, and therefore it is said

to be profitable to Teach. If the doctrine
be false, that holy Scripture discouers
clearly and ouerthrowes fully, and therefore
it is said to be profitable to Improue.
If it looke to manners, these manners be
either good, commanded and commended
of God: or euill, forbidden and condemned
by him. If they be good manners,
Scripture instructs them abundantly concerning
them: and therefore it is said to
be profitable to Instruct in righteousnesse.
If the manners be euill, this Scripture reproues
and condemnes, and therefore it
is said to be profitable to Correct. And
lastly, if thou, ô my soule, shalt finde thy
selfe cast downe at any time, or weakened
by the force of any tentation or crosse lying
on thee, or approaching neare thee,
shalt thou not find holy Scripture sufficiently
able to furnish thee with Patience,Rom. 25. 4.
with Comfort, and with Hope, as Paul
tels thee? ô my soule, when shall the blind
Papist begin to lend his eare vnto holy
Scripture, which is that onely old and
true antiquitie, which hath God that
glorious Ancient of dayes for the author
of it, to the end that he may first see that
there is no suspition of imperfection of

insufficiencie in holy Scripture, and therefore
be moued to confesse, that all things,
and euerie thing requisite for mans saluation
is onely to be sought out of it, is onely
to be found in it. Shall thy God, ô my
soule, be so carefull about the building of
that outward tabernacle, which he appointed
onely to stand for a while, that euen
after he had called and fitted Bezaliel
& Aholiah for the building of it, he will
haue it, and euerie thing belonging to it,
to be made after that fashion which was
shewed by his Maiestie vnto Moses in the
mount? And canst thou, ô my soule, or
any other soule with thee, be possibly
built (by these men called of God for the
worke of the Ministerie) vpon that onely
true foundation, and pretious corner stone
Iesus, otherwayes then Almightie God
hath taught these men to build them vppon
him, in and by that his mountaine of
holy Scripture? Are we not thus resolued
by that disciple whom Iesus loued, ô my
soule:Ioh. 20. 29. 30. 
                        Many other things also did Iesus in
the presence of his disciples, which are not
written in this Booke; but these things are
written that we might beleeue that Iesus is
that Christ the Sonne of God, and that in beleeuing

ye might haue life through his name.
Heare I not Paul crying with a loude
voice to the hearing of Angels and men?
Though that we or an Angell from heauen
preach vnto you otherwise then that which we
haue preached vnto you,
                        Gal. 1. 8. 
                        let him be accursed.
If any man teach otherwayes, and consenteth
not vnto the wholsome words of the Lord Iesus
Christ, and to the doctrine which is according
to godlinesse, he is puft vp and knoweth
nothing,
                        1. Tim. 6. 3. 4. 5. 
                        but doteth about questions, and
strife of words, whereof cometh enuie, strife,
raylings, euill surmisings, vaine disputations
of men of corrupt minds, and destitute of the
truth, which thinke that gaine is godlinesse,
from such separate thy selfe. Thinkest thou
that it was without cause, ô my soule,
that our God directed the Iewes thus by
the mouth of Moses, to whom the Law
was giuen?Deut. 4. 
                              •
                           . & 12. 32. 
                        Ye shall put nothing to the word
which I command you, neither shall ye take
ought therefrom that ye may keepe the commandements
of the Lord your God which I
command you. Was it without cause that
blessed Iesus by whom grace came to vs,
would speake thus to vs by the mouth of
his dearest seruant Iohn? For I protest vnto
euery man that heareth the words of the prophecie

of this booke: If any man shall adde vnto
these things, God shall adde vnto him the
plagues that are written in the booke.
                        Reuel. 22. 18. 19. 
                        And if
any man shall diminish of the words of this
prophecie, God shall take away his part out of
the booke of life, and out of the holy Citie, and
from these things written in this Booke. Oh,
ô my soule, when shall the blind Papist
proudly (albeit not onely vainely but falsly)
bragging of Antiquitie, countenance
that Antiquitie penned by men, led of
God by Scripture, and in Gods name leading
men to Scripture, to the end that
they with these men may see the sufficiencie
and perfection of Scripture, and with
this, the vanitie, the weaknesse, the vilenesse
of humane traditions. Origen who
was no Papist, albeit he wrote long ago,
wrote thus:Origen in Ierem. 
                        Nobis necesse est Scripturas
sanctas in testimonium vocare; sensus quippe
nostri, & enarrationes sine his testibus non
habent fidem. We must necessarily call holy
Scripture to beare witnesse to vs, for without
them neither can our conceptions nor expositions
haue any faith. Chrysostome seeing no
imperfection in Scripture could say: Si
quid dicitur absque Scriptura,
                        Chrysost. 
                        auditorum cogitatio
claudicat. Whatsoeuer is deliuered or

spoken without the warrant of Scripture maketh
the mindes of the herers to halt. Damascene
agreeing herewith, can say: Cuncta
quae tradita sunt per legem,
                        Damas. 
                        per Prophetas,
per Apostolos, & Euangelistas suscipimus,
cognoscimus, veneramur, nihil vltro perquirentes.
We receiue and admit, we acknowledge
and reuerence whatsoeuer is deliuered
to vs by the Law, by the Prophets, and by the
Euangelists, searching out nothing beside.
Augustine subscribing hereto could say:
Quod è Scriptura authoritatem non habet,
                        August.
                        eadem facilitate contemnitur quae probatur.
Whatsoeuer hath not authoritie from Scripture,
is as easily contemned as it is allowed.
O would to God that those kings and
subiects, parents and children, husbands
and wiues, maisters and seruants, who superstitiously
dote after the Pope and his

of the furie of man, to the end that the
ordinance of God may be ouerthrowne, that is
adulterous, impious, sacrilegious; take your
selues farre from the infection of such men, by
flying, eschewing their speeches as ye would
eschue the canker, and the pest; being forewarned
and taught by our Lord and Maister
saying vnto you, they be blind leaders of the

man pull you Christians from the Gospell of
Christ? Let no man take the sonnes of the
Church out of the Church; let them perish to
themselues who will perish; let those be strongly
and constantly reiected and cast off by you,
who do cast off the commandements of God,
to establish their owne traditions; flie farre

from the diuell his poysoned tongue, who from
the beginning of the world hath euer bene a
deceiuer, and a lyer; he lies, to the end he may
deceiue; he flatters, to the end he may hurt;
he promises good things, to the end he may
giue thee euill things: yea, he binds himselfe
to giue life, to the end he may slay. O when
shall the blind Papist hearken to that of
Clemens Alexandrinus.
                        In or. ad gent. 
                        Quoniam ipsum
verbum ad nos venit de coelo, non est amplius
eundum, ad hominum doctrinam. Because the
very word of God is now come to vs from the
heauens, we must not hereafter take our selues
to the doctrine of men. This is that the Spirit
would cleare vnto vs, when he saith: At
sundrie times,
                        Heb. 1. 2.

spake in the old time to our fathers by the

vs by his Sonne, by whom also he made the
