                        Sola Christiana Philosophia
eiusmodi est, ex qua rerum diuinarum
haurienda est cognitio, cuius authores
fuerunt homines iusti, Dei amantes, Deo
chari, neminem metuentes, gloriae non cupidi,
tantum Spiritus Dei afflatu loquuti. Christian
wisedome contained in holy Scripture is
onely such, out of the which knowledge of heauenly

things is onely to be drawne, the authors
whereof were men iust, louing God, dearely beloued
of God, fearing no man, no waies desirous
of glorie and honour, aud who did speake by
the inspiration of the holy Ghost onely.
                     
                  
                  
                     THE THIRD ROBBER IS
the Popish Seminarie, malitiously
stealing from the child of God that
perfect satisfaction made by blessed
Iesus, his sole and full Sauiour, vnto
God his Father for all his sinnes, and
for all punishment due to him for his
sinnes; and cunningly obtruding vnto
him his owne satisfaction for the
temporarie punishment of his sinnes,
either here before death, or after
death in Purgatorie.
                     O What a terrifying monster hath
that cunning foxe the Pope made of
his more then subtilly inuented,The Papist hath made a fearefull monster of his effectlesse fire of Purgatorie. and yet
more thē shamefully vented, of the effectlesse
fire of Purgatorie? Beleeue me, ô my
foule, those huge giants the sons of Anak,
bred neuer such dashing astonishment vnto
the faithlesse and murmuring spies, and

people of Israel, as these flames of the
fire of Purgatorie (kindled by the Pope
in the cold chimney of his fond imagination,
and without it to this day neuer
seene, neuer felt burning by any liuing, by
any dead) hath and doth procure to those
blind people, who turning their backes
vpon the word of God, (carried by Moses
and Aaron) haue lent their eares to his inuentions.
And yet the subtile Pope, to
make this his conceit the more plausible,
to that blind people led by him their blind
guide, can hold & maintaine most peartly,
(albeit more then lyingly) that howbeit
blessed Iesus hath by his death satisfied
God his Fathers wrath,The Popish forged ground of his forged Purgatory. for the guilt
of the sinnes of his chosen, and for the eternall
punishment due to them for those
their sinnes; yet he hath no wayes satisfied
for that temporarie punishment their sins
drawes after them, and so opening without
shame his shamelesse mouth, he dare
auow that all these who here do not sufficiently
satisfie by Penance (as he speaketh)
for their veniall and daily sinnes,
must remaine after death in Purgatorie,
and be there broyled, and sodden in the
flames thereof till they be haled out againe.

This fire the Pope hath taken vpon
him to make vp of coales and other matter,
neuer created by that great Creator
who made all things, but of a matter
knowne (I should haue said vnknowne
to himselfe.) And this strong fire he hath
kindled neither in the heauens, nor in the
aire, nor in the seas, nor in the earth, nor
in the hells; so that I must thinke, as the
Pope doth not know of what matter he
hath made vp that his fire of Purgatorie,The alledged extrem paines indured in the forged fire.
so he cannot know in what place it burneth.
And yet (if the Papist may be beleeued) ô what extreame intollerable
paines do poore soules sustaine there? Is
not this written by their Doctors for a
truth, ô my soule! There was a soule which
had bene thirtie yeares in Purgatorie, at
length there came an Angell asking his
soule whether it would tarrie yet one
short Winter day in Purgatorie,In the 160. sermon of the soules of the booke c
                              •
                           lled sermone
                                 •
                               discipuli de tempore & sanctis.
                         or if it
would returne to the world againe, and
do there a maruellous hard Penance; to
wit, for a long hundred yeares space go
barefooted, still treading vpon sharpe
iron nailes, eating nothing but browne
bread, drinking bitter gall mingled with
vineger, wearing a cloath made of camels

haire nearest his skin, and hauing a stone
vnder his head in place of a pillow. This
soule hearing this, chused rather to returne
to the earth to indure all this, then
to stay so much as one short Winter day
long in Purgatorie. But no wonder can it
be that the soule made her choyse thus, if
that fire be such a fire as the Papists make
it to be: for is it not written in their decrees,
that there is no earthly paine or
martyrdome to be compared to the
paines of Purgatorie? yea, is that great
schooleman Thomas ashamed to affirme?Cap. qui in aliud dist. 25.
that the fire of hell and the fire of Purgatorie
is all one, and that they differ nothing
at all, but that the one is temporall,
and the other is eternall. And yet is it not
a wonder, ô my soule, that the Papists can
write so resolutely touching this their
forged fire, and the extremitie of the
paines sustained in it, considering that our
blessed God (to whom all things are
knowne) to this day told vs neuer by
Scripture that there was such a fire, or
such paines sustained in it; yea, considering
that these very Papists by whom these
things be written, (as I thinke) will confesse
were neuer at Purgatorie, either to

see the flames of fire burning,What moued the Papists to write so freely about their forged fire of Purgatorie. or to heare
the cries of the soules tormented there,
or to be pained themselues therewith. But
ô my soule, it may be that I smell a farre
off (if I be not farre deceiued) that which
hath moued the Papists so freely thus to
speake, and to write about their Purgatorie.
The fire of Purgatorie they neuer
saw, the ho
                           •
                        e paining flames thereof
they neuer felt in their owne persons.
But yet they do daily see their owne
outward and naturall fire, and feele
the heate of it, to their great profit and
pleasure: And they know that this
their alledged forged fire of Purgatorie,
with the alledged fearefull, and forged
burning flames thereof, hath onely set vp
this their fire, and kept in this their fire;
that kings are onely in their hands who
are onely able to pull poore soules out
of these flames; yea that strongest fleshcrooke
is onely in their custodie, which
is able to hale them out of this boyling
caldron (for be they not the maisters of
all Masses, Pardons, and Indulgences, by
the which alone these poore soules (if the
Papists may be beleeued) are deliuered
from these flames? haue they not, non

sine commodo curiae, albeit cum damno conscientiae:
first forged that fire cunningly, and
to this day fostered it carefully, drawing
sharpe slaying swords, and kindling seene
deuouring flames of seene, felt fire, against
all such who hearing do not beleeue and
follow them. And, ô my soule, will
Scripture subscribe with the Papist? will
true Antiquitie founded on Scripture, and
not blinded by that filthie idoll Couetousnesse
foster him in this point?Scripture ouerthroweth Purgatorie & her pretended ground. No, no, ô my
soule, I assure thee; for if that blessed Spirit
of truth speaking by Scripture cleare
any point of sauing doctrine sensibly, for
the resolution and consolation of poore
sinners, against those euils which sinne
draweth vpon man, he cleares most sensibly
that which that cursed spirit of lyes
speaking by the Pope, and his suffraganes
obscures most grosly, yea controles and
denies most impudently: and yet most
heartily vnto the confusion and condemnation
of poore sinners. What hath the
Spirit of God cleared, ô my soule, if this
be not cleared by him? Blessed Iesus, that
Sonne of God and Sonne of man, is that sole
and onely Sauiour of man, is the full and perfect
Sauiour of man; who alone in his owne

person once hath satisfiedfully, and perfited
his fathers iustice, for all the sinnes of his elect
freeing them from all the guilt of their sinnes,
and from all their punishment due to them.
Cannot sweet Iesus (who neuer made any
foolish bragge, or vttered any apparent
vntruth, fastened to the Crosse, and there
suffering for thee,Christ alone in his owne person hath satisfied his Father for vs fully. ô my soule) crie out
with a loud voice. It is finished, it is finished?
by this one word, directing his speech to
God his Father who sent him to saue lost
men, and telling his Maiestie that he by
his death had payed the least farthing of
mans debt of sinne, and so satisfie his
iustice fully; directing his speech to man,
for whose sake he was sent, and telling
him that he was loosed from that band,
and hand writing, God the Father had
ouer his head because of sinne, he hauing
cancelled it, and rent it in peeces vpon the
tree, and so that he was freed from that
prison within the which he lay bound before
and set at libertie, henceforth to
serue God on earth, and to reigne with
him in heauen: & yet the couetous papists
alwayes crying (with Iudas) What will
you giue me and I will betray him to you? can
giue Christ the lie in his face, saying in

the hearing of his father to men, It is not
finished. That is, Christ hath not ransomed
man fully, and freed him from prison
wholely in respect he must go yet to
that prison of Purgatorie and by another
ransome (most vile indeed, yet
not so vile as the vile receiuer of it is) be
deliuered therefrom. Cannot Paul (subscribing
to the sweetest and most comfortable
words of his Maister) tell me that
Iefus is giuen me of my God to be my
Redeemer,1. Cor. 1. 30. albeit the Pope would send me
to Purgatorie, to the end he may be my
redeemer? Yea, that he gaue himselfe a
ransome for all men, albeit the Pope
would send me to Purgatorie,1. Tim. 2. 6. there to be
tormented by my selfe, by suffering of torments,
and by the liuing belonging to
me, by laying downe a ransome of gold,
for some masses to be sung for me. Isaiah
would make me beleeue (and I dare not
but beleeue him better then all the Popes
of the world) that I am healed by Christs
stripes,Esay 5. 
                              •
                           . and yet the Papist will haue me
yet to be whipped, for the healing of me,
with the burning scourges of the flames
of this Purgatorie. Yea, Isaiah in that
same place tels me that the chastisement

of my peace was vpon Christ alone, and
Paul would assure me that I being iustified
by faith haue peace with God through
Iesus Christ our Lord, albeit the fierce
Papist would send me backe to that
bloudie barres of his cruell Purgatorie,
there to vndergo a fearefull battell and
vndergo a bloudy warrefare: draw neare
me,A direct opposition betwixt that spirit which speaketh by Scripture and that spirit speaketh by the Pope. here, ô my soule, and consider I pray
thee, but that contradiction which is to
be found to be betwixt that spirit of truth
speaking to thee by Scripture about this
point, and that spirit of lies speaking to
thee by the Pope: Scripture tels me that
Christ hath fully satisfied his Father for
me: The Pope tels me that he hath satisfied
him onely in a part. Scripture tels me
that Christ satisfied once for me. The
Pope tels me that he must be satisfied
daily for me; Scripture tels me that he satisfied
his Father for me by himselfe in his
owne person, bearing our sinnes in his
flesh vpon the Crosse: the Pope tels me
that I must satisfie my God by suffering
in my owne person. Scripture tels me, that
he hath satisfied and doth satisfie his Father
in vs. No wonder that the Pope doth
this, for by this craft he liueth, and therefore

I must giue him leaue, ô my soule,
till God (being mercifull vnto him) open
his eyes to see that truth which shineth
in holy Scripture, to lie about this his
forged Purgatorie;Act. 20. as Demetrius the siluer
Smith at Ephesus lied about his dead
goddesse Diana.
                        True Antiquitie condemneth Purgatorie. But will true Antiquitie,
ô my soule, subscribe with the Papist about
this his Purgatorie? No, no, if it
could be hearkned vnto: for cannot old
Cyprian say.Cyprian. con. Deme. 
                        Quando istinc excessum fuerit,
nullus iam locus poenitentiae, nullus satisfactionis
effectus; hic vita, aut tenetur,
aut amittitur. So soone as we go hence
there remaineth no place of repentance any
more, no effect of satisfaction; life is either
lost or found here. Bernard could say, Tria
sunt loca: Coelum, Terra, Infernus; & habent
singula habitatores suos; coelum solos bonos,
terra mixtos, Infernus solos malos. There
be three places, the Heauens, the Earth, and
the Hels; and euerie one of them hath their
owne indwellers. The heauens keeping these
who be good onely: the earth possessing both
good and bad:
                        Bern. in sentent. fol. 117. 
                        the hels hauing the wicked
onely inclosed within them. And againe,
Tres sunt animae status, in corpore, posito corpore,
& recepto corpore; primus datus est ei

ad agendam poenitentiam, reliqui duo ad habendam
requiem vel poenam scilicet, prout
gessit in corpore, siue bonum, siue malum.
There be three conditions of the soule, one
while it is in the bodie; another when it layes
aside the bodie; the third when it takes vp the
bodie againe. The first estate is granted to her,
to the end she may repent, the other two, to
the end she may receiue rest or punishment, as
she hath behaued her selfe in her bodie, by doing
good or euill.
                        Aug. lib. 5. hypogr. 
                        Augustine long before
Bernard could write thus. Primum locum
fides catholica diuina authoritate regnum
credit esse coelorum, secundum gehennam, tertiam
ignoramus penitus, imo nec in scripturis
sanctis inueniemus: the faith of true Catholike
Christians leaning to the authoritie of
God, beleeues the first place after this life to
be the kingdome of heauen, the second to be
the hels, but the third we no wayes know,
neither shall find to be in holy Scripture. And
no wonder that Augustine writ so, for
he could not find that Purgatorie hath
that vse which the subtile greedie Papist
since his dayes hath fained it to haue; for
writes not Augustine thus againe:Aug de ver. Ser. 37. 
                        Christus
suscipiendo paenam, & non suscipiendo culpam,
& culpam & paenam deleuit. Christ by taking

on him the punishment due to vs for sinne, and
not the guilt of sinne, hath done away both
the guilt and the punishment. Yea, this moued
Bernard to bring in that saying, Oportuit
liberari in hoc saeculo vt liberos haberet
in futuro. It behoued the children of our
God to be freed and deliuered from all euill in
this life, to the end that God their Father
might haue free sonnes and daughters to
raigne with him in the world to come. Were
that ancient Doctor at Paris liuing now,Frater Michael. Menoti.
he would ioyne hands with vs against the
Papist in this point, for could he not write
thus: Peccator est mercator positus in hoc
mundo pro emendo regnum Paradisi, & tantum
durant nundinae quantum vita praesens. A
sinner is a merchant placed in this world to
buy the kingdome of Paradise, and the market
or faire in the which he must buy it, indures &
lasts as long as this present life shall indure.
                     
                  
                  
                     THE FOVRTH ROBBER
is the Popish Seminarie, malciously
stealing from the babes of God that
cleane bloudie and onely propitiatorie
sacrifice offered vnto God the Father
by that blessed hie Priest of our soules

Iesus; and subtiltie obtruding to
them that vncleane bloudie, and no
wayes purging, but alwayes defiling
sacrifice of the Masse, offered vp
(alas) not vnto God (as the Papist
alledgeth) but to the diuell (as he
should confesse) by his Masse-Priest.
                     SEing,Wherfore was this vile Masse forged by the Papist. ô my soule, that vile sacrifice of
the Masse was first inuented without
confidence, & then vented with a shamelesse
countenance, specially because of
this forged and fained fire of Purgatorie
to be a tongs or flesh-hooke, or rather
a theeuish Egyptian hand, to pull out money
of poore mens purses. Let vs trie if
Scripture will fauor the tonges, and flesh-hookes
of the Masse, more then it fauors
the fire of Purgatory. Sure I am, ô my soule
that the first inuenters of this vnbloudie
(albeit not vngreedie) sacrifice of that
mischeuous monstrous Masse, neuer dreamed
that holy Scripture should haue fauored
it, or furthered them in maintaining
of it, albeit the other venters of it,
(non efferentes verum sensum ex Scripturis
sed inferentes falsum sensum in Scriptur as: not

bringing forth a true interpretation and
meaning out of Scripture, but throwing forcible
a false interpretation, and meaning vpon
Scripture) haue (peruerting Scripture
to their owne condemnation,2. Epist. 3. cap. as Peter
speaketh) pressed to make Scripture sound
their, way. The name of the Masse the
Papist shall not find iu Scripture, and this
the most learned among them will not
deny, for I perswade my selfe that they are
long ago ashamed of that brutish conclusion,
gathered by the Doctros of Sarbon
at Paris, vpon the end of Pauls Epistles,
shewing whence they were written, and
sounding in the Latine tongue thus. Missa
est, and so forth; affirming that Paul did
thereby giue men to vnderstand that they
should go to heare Masse on Sunday. And
therefore I must pray thee, ô my soule, let
me here enquire of the Papist first, what
sacrifice this his sacrifice of the Masse is?
Secondly, what is that which he sacrificeth
when he offereth it vp? and these
two questions being answered by
him, I shall shew thee (God-willing)
what thy God speaketh to thee by his
owne mouth out of Scripture, and hath
deliuered for thy resolution and establishment

about this point. The Papist
will answer thee, ô my soule, that his sacrifice
of the Masse is an externall, reall,
vnbloudie, propitiatorie sacrifice, in the
which the true bodie and bloud of Iesus
Christ be offered vp to God his Father,
by the Masse priest, vnder the shape,
forme, and fashion of bread and wine, and
that for the sinnes of the liuing on earth
here, and for the dead in Purgatorie. I
know, ô my soule, that the Masse priest
knowes that he hath no conscience in extolling
and defending of this his sacrifice,
and yet I cannot but wonder how he
hath the face to offer it vp, and to
eate it when he hath done with it. Grants
he not, ô my soule, that it is an outward
sacrifice? now if it be an outward sacrifice,
it must necessarily be a visible sacrifice, all
outward things being visible? If it be a
visible sacrifice, then necessarily that
which is offered vp into it must be seene,
for how can an outward sacrifice be vnderstood,
vnlesse the sacrifice offered vp
into it be perceiued? Stoope forwards
here, ô my soule, and with courage demand
the Masse priest, what he offers vp
to God, and so what he vnderstands by

the sacrifice whilst he cals his Masse an
outward, reall sacrifice? Himselfe I thinke
he offers not vp, himselfe I thinke he vnderstands
not by that sacrifice which he
offers vp, nor his altar, nor the many ceremonies
vsed by him, nor those hundred
crosses ouer and ouer made by him. The
bodie of Christ, saith the priest, stands by
his sacrifice: that I heare, but is Christs
bodie in that sacrifice of the Masse outward
and visible? aduise with thy senses,
by the which outward things are perceiued,
ô Masse priest, most sensible of siluer,
but altogether senslesse of thy Sauiour,
and then if thou hast any conscience, answer
me as thou wilt be answerable to
God: seest thou the bodie of Christ in this
thy sacrifice of the Masse? smellest thou it?
tastest thou it? touchest thou it? But the
accidents of the bread are seene (alledgeth
the Masse priest) as the roundnesse of
it, the colour of it, yea the taste and smell
of it are also perceiued, and these be outward
and externall. That I grant to be
true. But alwayes, ô Masse priest, when all
this is done, either thou must offer these
accidents to God, and these must be thy
sacrifice, which thou deniest, or else thou

must offer vp to God an outward visible
sacrifice without an outward visible offering,
which cannot possibly be: or lastly,
that one and the same sacrifice must be
outward and inward, visible and inuisible.
But it may be, ô my soule, that the Masse
priest who hath learned his tongue so
grosly to contrarie God, can easily digest
these contrarieties. Forget not then, ô my
soule, that the Papist doth confesse that
Christs bodie is offered vp in the Masse,
and yet that it is inuisible in the Masse, and
therefore see that thou, throwing his
owne false doctrine in his owne soules
face, say to him, vpon his owne grounds,
that his Masse can be no visible sacrifice,
and if it be no visible, that it cannot be
outward as he affirmeth.No remission of sins without bloud. But will Scripture
agree with an vnbloudie sacrifice
promising remission of sinnes? I trow not,
ô my soule, for speakes not Scripture thus:Heb. 9. 22.
                        Without shedding of bloud there is no remission.
Will Scripture allow the offering vp
of Christ by a priest for the sinnes of any?
I trow not, ô my soule, 
                           •
                        or be not these
the speeches of the Spirit:Heb. 10. 10. 11. 12. 13. 
                        We are sanctified
by the offering vp of the bodie of Iesus Christ
once made. Euery Priest appeareth daily ministring,

and ofttimes offereth any manner of
offering, which can neuer take away sinnes.
But this man after he had offered one sacrifice
for sinnes, sitteth for euer at the right
hand of God, and from hence forth tarrieth
till his enemies be made his footstoole.
                        Heb. 9. 24, 25. 26. 27. 28. 
                        For
with one offering hath he consecrated for euer
them that are sanctified. Christ hath entered
into the verie heauen to appeare now in the
sight of God for vs, not that he should offer
himselfe often, as the high Priests entred into
the holy place euery yeare with other bloud,
(for then must he haue often suffered since
the foundation of the world) but now in the
end of the world, hath he appeared once to put
away sinne by the sacrificing of himselfe, and as
it is appointed to men that they shall once dye,
and after that commeth iudgement, so Christ
was once offered to take away the sinnes of
many, and vnto them that looke for him shall
he appeare the second time without sinne vnto
saluation. And in that fame place: Christ
being an hie Priest of good things to come,
                        Heb. 9. 11. 12. 
                        by
a greater and more perfect tabernacle, not
made with hands, that is not of this building,
neither by the bloud of goates, and calues, but
by his owne bloud, entred he in once into the
holy place, and obtained eternall redemption

for vs. And againe: For such an high Priest it
became vs to haue which is holy,
                        Heb. 7. 26. 27. 28. 
                        harmelesse,
and vndefiled, separate from sinners, and made
higher then the heauens, which needeth not
daily as these high Priests to offer vp sacrifice,
first for his owne sinnes, and then for the peoples;
for that did he once when he offered vp
himself, for the Law maketh men high priests
which haue infirmitie, but the word of the
oath which was since the Law maketh the
Sonne who is consecrate for euermore. Consider
these Scriptures, ô my soule, and
then calling to minde the fond conceites
of the false greedie priest about his Masse,
iudge, I pray thee, how these grounds can
possibly stand together: Christs offering
once made, and Christs offering not once
made; Christs offering once offered, and
Christs offering daily offered, yea daily to
be offered while the world lasts; Christ
once offered, and Christ not once offered,
but often to be offered; Christ offered
once by himselfe, and to be offered often
by the priest. But all these contrarieties be
easily digested by that man, ô my soule,
who can treade the pathes of the old
Scribes and Pharises: for ô how iustly
may that be spoken of the Masse priest

this day sacrificing his vnbloudie sacrifice
of the Masse, that holding in his forged
fire of Purgatorie, he may thereby kindle
vp to himselfe, and alwayes keepe in his
closet, an hote fire to warme himselfe)
which was spoken long ago of the Pharises,
of whom Chrysostome writeth thus:
Magis cupiebant vt lege manente in vsu essent
sacrificia quibus ipsi ditabantur,
                        Chrys. on Mat. 23. hom. 44. 
                        non
Deus; quam lege cessante, sacrificium iustitiae
veniret in vsum, quo Deus delectatur & homines
iustificantur. They desired rather, that
the Law, these sacrifices standing, might remaine
in vse, by the which they were inriched,
and not God; then that the Law ceassing that
sacrifice of righteousnesse should haue place,
with the which alone God is well pleased, and
by the which sinfull man is made righteous.
Now I appeale to thy conscience, ô Masse
priest, whither thou wishest that thy vnbloudie
sacrifice of the Masse, whereby
thou art inriched, and God is grieued,
should stand in constant vigor, as it hath
done with thee, or that it should ceasse
and be reiected of all men, as it was neuer
ordained of God, to the end that all men
euerie where might haue recourse onely
to that onely bloudie propitiatorie sacrifice

once offered vp by Christ, and neuer
to be offered vp againe, albeit it be that
onely sacrifice wherein God delighteth,
and whereby euerlasting righteousnesse
is attained by man. But while the
Masse priest finds himselfe thus by Scripture
to be straited, with Satan his maister
tempting my Sauiour, he dare flie to Scripture,
and presse euen by it to make all he
hath alledged good (about the retention
of the temporarie punishment due to sin)
after the guilt thereof and eternall punishment
belonging to man,The Popish alledgances for the retention of the temporarie punishmēt after that remission of the guilt and eternal punishmēt. for it is remitted.
Reade we not (will the Masse
priest say) by Moses, in the 3. of Genesis,
that howbeit Adam after his fall
was certified by that sweet Euangelicke
Sermon sounded i
                           •
                         his eares, that by faith
in the seed of the woman promised, he
should be freed from the guilt of his sin,
and eternall death due thereunto: yet we
find that Adam beside this must endure
the first death, be cast out of the earthly
paradise, and haue his bodie afflicted with
many troubles and miseries. Surely reade
we not that notwithstanding Dauid had
his adulterie and murther remitted, yet he
was sharpely punished with temporarie

scourges, for as Scripture tels vs the child
which was borne dyed according to
Gods threatning: Ammon his sonne defiled
Tamar his daughter, Absolon his sonne
slue Ammon his brother, yea Absolon his
sonne put first his old father out of the
doores, & after defiled his concubines before
the Sun, whereof it is manifest (saith
the Masse priest) that after God hath remitted
the great and eternall punishment
of sinne to his owne, that they themselues
must suffer for the temporarie, either here
before death, or after death in Purgatory.
Lift vp thine eares, ô my soule, and heare
I pray thee, he whom heresie hath once
blinded, can very hardly be enlightened
by veritie: yea, he who with Iudas seekes
the bagge, cannot be kept backe from betraying
Iesus, for any thing Iesus can
speake to him, Iesus can do to him. If thou
hast any conscience, ô Masse priest, tell
me as thou wilt answer to God, if no other
thing moues our wise God, after he
hath freely and fully forgiuen his children
for the merits of his dearest child Iesus,
to correct and afflict them, but that
thereby they may satisfie his iustice for
the temporarie punishment due to them

for sinne? If thou shalt suffer Scripture
to leade thee, and not thy owne greedie
heart to miscarrie thee, thou shalt find
that no wayes, for that cause, but for
maine other good deeds doth our God so
behaue himselfe towards his owne. First,
that the bodie of sinne in them may by
peece and peece be crucified,Wherfore corrects our God those whō he remitteth. and mortified,
least otherwayes they falling forth in
new sins should proue dogges returning
to their vomite, & swine to their puddle.
The sense hereof moued, Dauid to say: It is
good for me that I haue bene afflicted,
                        Psal. 119. 71. 
                        that I
may learne thy statutes. Secondly, this is
done by our wise God, to the end that
these his corrections may supply ye roome
of as many speaking, wise Maisters, alwayes
sounding in the eares of Gods children
that notable iewell receiued by
them, euen the remission of their sinnes,
together with the dutie they should discharge
vnto God for the same. This moued
Dauid in the place alledged to say:
Before I was afflicted I went astray,
                        Psal. 119. 67. 
                        but now
I keepe thy word. Chrysostome
                        Chrysost. seeing this
which the Papist cannot see, could say.
Deus imponit paenam non exigens supplicia
pro peccatis, sed ad futura nos corrigens. God

layes correction vpon his owne, not exacting any
punishment for sinnes, but correcting vs for
the time to come. Yea, this moued Augustine
to say. Res prosphera donum est Dei consolantis,
res aduersa donum Dei admonentis.
Prosperitie is the gift of God comforting men;
aduersitie is the gift of God admonishing men.
Thirdly, this is done least sinne (which is
both freely and fully remitted of God
with all punishment due thereto) should
be extenuate and accounted light, either
by the committers, or by others looking
on them, and in the end not onely excused,
but defended by them to their condemnation.
This moued the Apostle to
say,1. Cor. 11. 32. 
                        When we are iudged we are chastened of
the Lord, because we should not be condemned
with the world. Fourthly, that sinners
being thus recōciled to God through the
remission of their sinnes, and yet out of his
wonderfull, wise loue corrected by him,
might alwayes carrie about with them
some tokens of that sinne which lodgeth
within them, and doth sometime fully
burst out of them, leading them alwayes
with the sound, to the sight of
their blacke feete, and making them to
walke more holily, and humbly before

God, crying alwayes with that great Apostle,Rom. 7. 24.
                        O wretched man that I am who shall
deliuer me from this bodie of death. Fiftly, to
the end that th
                           •
                        se corrections wisely
layed vpon them by their God, might
haue a solid matter of spirituall exercise
to them, not onely acquainting them
with the great weaknesse and imperfection
of their faith and repentance, but
stirring them vp to haue them from day
to day, more and more increased and
strengthened.August. 
                        Augustine seeing this, could
write most prudently about this point
thus: Posset aliquis dicere, si propter peccatum
dixit Deus homini, in sudore vultus tui
edes panem tuum & spinas, & tribulos proferit
tibi terra; cur fideles post remissionem
peccatorum, eosdem dolores patiuntur? Respondet,
ante remissionem esse supplicia peccatorum,
post remissionem, esse certamina exercitationesque
iustorum, Some man might say,
if God said vnto man for his sinne, in the sweat
of thy face shalt thou eate thy bread, and the
earth shall bring forth thrones and thistles to
thee: wherefore doth the faithfull after the
remission of their sins suffer the like troubles,
He answers: before remission of sinnes these
things be punishments sinnes, but after remission

they are trials and exercises of the
iustified children of God. O when shall the
lying Seminaries hearken to that of the
Apostle.Heb. 12. 6. 7. 
                        Whom the Lord loueth he chasteneth,
If you indure chastening, God offereth
himselfe vnto you as to sonnes.
                        Reuel. 3. 19. 
                        As manie as I
loue I rebuke and chasten. Now if these corrections
which be layed by our blessed
God vpon his children, do not onely
flow from that sweetest well of that loue,
wherewith his Maiestie doth loue them
in his blessed Sonne, but also by euident
and sure pledges of that loue; can these
corrections suffered by Gods children be
possibly satisfactions for his iustice for sin?
I charge thee therefore, ô my soule, that
remaining within my bodie, thou countenance
no sacrifice, besides that onely
bloudie sacrifice, offered once onely vp by
thy great hie Priest Iesus God,Esay 53. and man
vpon the crosse vnto his Father for thee,2. Cor. 5.
as thou desirest to be freed of the burthen
of my sinnes, and of all punishment due
to me for them. I charge thee that thou
neuer lend thy eare to the sound of anie
Purgatorie,Iohn 1. besides that cleane and cleansing
pure bloud of that blessed Lambe of
God who takes away the sinnes of the

world,1. Iohn 1. and whose bloud cleanseth thee
from all sinne,Aug. in Epist. 171. euer crying with Augustine,
Passio Domini pretium est orbis terrarum:
The suffering of the Lord Iesus is the redemption
of the world; and neuer forget to solace
and cherish thy selfe in the middest of
all extremities with that of Bernard:
                        Bern. 
                        Passio
tua Domine vltimum refugium est, singulare
remedium; deficiente sapientia, iustitia non
sufficiente, sanctitatis succumbentibus meritis:
Thy passion ô Lord Iesus is my last refuge, my
singular remedie, when my wisedome failes,
when my righteousnesse is not sufficient; and
when the merites of my holinesse do succumbe
and are brought to nought, thy onely passion
doth helpe me.
                     
                     Oh, ô my soule, when shall the blindfold
Papists (who partly avow that they
do see, and who in this respect cannot but
sinne grossely, and go on in sinne fearefully)
beginne to perswade that they be
blinde; to the end that through the tender
mercies of God they may be freed
from their sins? Could the Popish Seminaries
(the sowers of Satans poyson, and
people with the proud Pharisees, and who
with,Esay 60 6. 3. the counterfet old idolatrous Iewes
do offer swines bloud, and blesse an Idol)

begin to learne to discerne betwixt that
great and onely Maiesticke high sacrificing
Priest, Iesus, and their greedie and
only mercenarie, slauish, sacrificing priest;
would they beginne now at length (hauing
stumbled so long at that lanterne of
the blessed word of God,Marke the opposition which is betwixt Christ and his sacrifice and the Popish priest and his sacrifice and sinned against
the light of their owne consciences,)
to make a difference betwixt that
bloudie sacrifice offered vp by Iesus, and
these vnbloudie sacrifices now authorised
and offered vp by them and their leaders,
the Iesuites? O how farre would they
adore the one, and abhorre the other! O
with how swift feete would they runne
towards the one, and flee from the other!
Yea, ô how often would they present the
one before the Lord their God, as that
onely ransome which is onely able to satisfie
his iustice for their monstrous debt
of sinne, and repent before God and man
thar euer they presented themselues before
the other, which is nothing else but
that odde abomination, wherby that debt
of sinne is not onely kept ouer the head
of man, but also fearefully augmented and
increased, swearing solemnely neuer to
countenance that Idoll. The heart of the

sacrificer Iesus, ô my soule, as Scripture
witnesseth was the heart of a Lambe beyond
all measure, gentle and pitifull,
which neuer deuised any crueltie, which
neuer consented to any crueltie. The
mouth of that sacrificer Iesus was the truest
mouth, the sweetest mouth that euer
man spake with, neuer vttering any falsehood,
neuer colouring, or couering anie
crueltie to the preiudice or hurt of anie.
The hand of that sacrificer Iesus, was the
cleanest hand that euer man carried, the
most liberall hand that euer man had,
helping thousands, but neuer hurting one;
sauing, and healing thousands, but neuer
slaying or harming so much as one; albeit
that sacrifice offred vp by this gentle, pitifull,
true, sweet, liberall, and euer helping
and sauing, but neuer harming or
slaying sacrifice, was bloudie, yea was as it
had bene nothing but all bloudie, his
head, his side, his hands, his feete, being
all couered therewith, so that not without
cause some of the ancients could apply
that of Isaiah to this blessed Sacrificer Iesus.
                        Esay 61. 1. 2. 3.
                        Who is this that cometh from Edom,
with red garments from Bozrah? he is glorious
in his apparell, and walketh in his great

strength, I speake in righteousnesse, and am
mightie to saue? wherefore is thine apparell
red, and thy garments like him that treadeth
in the wine presse? I haue tread the wine presse
alone, aud of all the people there was none
with me. But, ô my soule, will not the Papist
confesse (considering long and fearefull
experience will testifie against him)
that the heart of his sacrificing Priest is
the heart of a lion, beyond measure fierce
and false, deuising crueltie, approuing crueltie;
that the mouth of his sacrificing
Priest is the mouth of a diuell, hauing alwayes
deceite & falsehood vnder his lips,
and neuer so readily as when he bakes his
false speeches with fearefull oathes. That
the hand of his sacrificing Priest, is ye hand
of one Bontcher and Burrio, delighting in
nothing so much, as in the shedding of
the bloud of Kings, Princes, and people,
without any respect of sexe or age, albeit
his sacrifice in the meane time (as he
styles it) be vnbloudie. And here I would
pray thee, ô my soule, (if thou be any way
acquainted with the holy and iust God)
to tell me ot thy God can possibly take
vpon, or accept of that vnbloudie sacrifice
which is offered vp by him who

hath a bloudie false heart, deuising crueltie
and falshood? a bloudie tongue
councelling and concealing, as he hath
to do with God and his Saints, crueltie
and falshood? yea, an hand executing
crueltie and falshood? yea I must yet enquire
of thee another thing, ô my soule,
could that bloudie sacrifice offered vp by
Iesus to God his Father for thee, haue
possibly bene accepted of God, if his
heart, his mouth, and hands, had bene such
an heart, a mouth, and hands as the heart,
mouth, and hands of the Papish priests be?
No, no, ô my soule, had Christ heart bene
such an heart, had Christs mouth bene
such a mouth, had Christs hands bene such
hands, as the heart, mouth, and hands of
these Papish priests be, euen Christs sacrifice
should haue bene reiected by God
his Father. And therefore I heare Peter
(fully abused by the Pope and his followers)
telling me that I am not onely redeemed
by the bloud of that Lambe Iesus,1. Pet. 1. 19.
but of that Lambe Iesus; vndefiled,
and without spot, cleane hearted, cleane
tongued, cleane handed, and alwayes
cleane. When I begin to thinke vpon this
seriously, ô my soule, I cannot but wonder

who he is that hath conquired such a
great cracke to the Papist priests in this
our last age of the world, that an vnbloudie
sacrifice comming from his bloudie,
heart, mouth, and hands should be accepted
of God, at whose hāds the old Iewes,
Gods first borne, could finde no such fauour:
for whe
                           ••
                         reade that first of Isaiah,
I heare out God reiecting both the bloudie
and vnbloudie sacrifices of the Iewes,
to wit, their prayers and incest, and all because
their hands were defiled with
bloud, for speakes not our God by Isaiah
thus:Isa. 1. 15. 
                        When you shall stretch out your hands
I will hide my eyes from you, and though you
make many prayers, I will not heare you, for
your hands are full of bloud. Shall crueltie in
the heart and in the hand of the counterfeit
Iew, make that holy iust God of heauen
refuse to accept from the hands of the
Iewes these sacrifices, his Maiestie by his
Law hath commanded? and shall this holy
iust God accept of that sacrifice offered
vp by that cruell heart, and bloudie hand
of the Masse priest, which he neuer commanded,
but which hath bene, is, and shall
be, in despite of diuels and men, abhomination
before his Maiestie, albeit he dare

dreame that his vnbloudie sacrifice smelled
neuer so sweetly before God as when
he hath come from the deuising or approuing
of the slaughter of some few or
moe, who do worship the true God of
heauen, truly according to his will, and
not as men would teach them? But it may
be, ô my soule, that the priest his great
God (the Pope I meane) who is clothed
with a threefold diademe, as he who hath
all power in heauen, and in earth, and in
the hels, hath made him conceit that he
hath procured this credit vnto him. Alwayes
I am not ignorant, ô my soule, that
the Papist Seminarie being challenged
of crueltie, and taught cunningly by their
leaders the Iebusites, will alledge and auow
that they giue no counsell against
the life of any, but of those who be the
enemies of Christ, and that they neither
giue counsell to slay any,The lesuits allegation to excuse their crueltie. neither do allow
the slaughter of any, neither do slay any,
but out of that loue which they carrie to
Christ, and so to the end that by cutting
off the enemies of Christ,This allegation is remoued and 
                              •
                           roued they may build
a glorious Church to his Maiestie. What
if these allegations (plausibly to the Papist

God by his owne bloud hath purchased
a Church to himselfe: but Scripture told
me neuer, that God would conquire a
Church vnto himselfe by shedding the
bloud of men and women, of Princes and
subiects, old and yong. I heare our Maister
indeed saying in the Gospell to his

                        The time shall come that whosoeuer
killeth you, shall thinke he doth God good
seruice: But I neuer heard him speake
thus. The time shall come that whosoeuer
killeth you shall do God good seruice:
and knowest thou not, ô my soule,

not that the Iewes thought that they

not an euill doer we would not haue deliuered

cause) that the blind Iesuite either
hath neuer read, or neuer duely considered
that 7. Chapter of the 2. of Samuel:
was not Dauid a man according to the

heart of God? That bloud which he had
shed, was it not shed by him on the speciall
warrant of Gods command? (for as
yet he had not slaine Vriah) and yet because

cannot find libertie so much as to build an

shall that bloudie Burrio the Iesuite alledge,
that he (hauing no warrant to shed

by Matthew in his 26. Chap. there
Peter seeing his Maister apprehended,Mat. 26. 51. 52. out

Alwayes I thinke that his Maister

I heare Iesus commanding Peter to

                        Because they receiued not the loue of

proprium est, coedere autem Christianos, Pilati,

Christians to be slaine, but it is the office of

wonder, if Bernard were liuing now,
how he would take the bloud of the

for writes he not thus to the Pope

Iesuite leaue off to wearie that blessed
holy God of heauen, and to deceiue his
poore babes with that his vnbloudie sacrifice,
neuer knowne to God, neuer commanded
by his Sonne,The sacrifice all Ministers should offer to God. and begin to take
pleasure to sacrifice vnto God, that holy
sacrifice (that Apostle who communicated
not with flesh and bloud) but who

was taught of God what to do, to sacrifice
to his Maiestie? Hearest thou not, ô
my soule, that the Apostle saith to thee?
I haue somwhat boldly after a sort written
vnto you, as one that putteth you in rememberance
through the grace that is giuen me
of God,
                        Rom. 15. 15. 16. 
                        that I should be the Minister of
Iesus Christ towards the Gentiles, ministring
the Gospell of God, that the offering
vp of the Gentiles might be acceptable,

Chrysostome writing vpon these words
will haue the whole Apostolicke priesthood
to consist in preaching, saying in the
person of Paul, Ipsum enim mihi sacerdotitium
est praedicare & Euangelizare, hanc offero
hostiam. My priesthood is to preach
and to sound the euangell; this offering I offer;
And going on in the explication of the
seuerall parts of this metaphor for the
better vnderstanding of this sacrifice offered
vp by the Apostle he tells vs the
sword whereby he did slay the sacrifice
offered vp by him to God was the Euangell;
that the art of sacrificing, was the
preaching of the Euangell; that the fire
whereby the sacrifice was burnt, was the
faith of God; that the sacrifice sacrificed

by him, was the Gentiles; that the Priests
sacrificing this sacrifice, was the Apostles
sent of God to this effect. Had these monsters
sent from Rome these manie yeares
by gaine, bene exercised about the
sacrificing of such sacrifices, drawing of
the sword, and kindling of this fire here
remembred by Paul, ô what a world of
bloud of soules of men, of womē, of yong,

through their default withdrawne
