of the Masse, which can no wayes impaire
but alwayes augment their debt
and dutie. Here leauing their indured
monsters to their owne induring
maisters, and reuerincing the dispensation
of that wise God whose iudgemeuts are
vnsearchable, and his wayes past finding
out,Igna Epist. 6. ad Phil. we must remember that of Ignatius:
Quemadmodum pseudoprophetae & pseudoapostoli
vnum & eundem spiritum fallacem, &
populi seductorem acceperunt; sic prophetae &

Apostoli vnum & eundem spiritum, sanctum,
bonum, eximium, verum, & doctorem rectū
acceperunt à Deo per Iesum Christum. As
the false prophets and apostles receiued anie
euill spirit, to deceiue the people: So the
true Prophets and Apostles receiue from God
through Iesus Christ, and his holy spirit,
the good, excellent, true, teacher of righteousnesse.
                     
                  
                  
                     THE FIFTH ROBBER
is the Popish Seminarie, subtily stealing
from the babes of God that royall,
and sweet smelling garment of
Christ his righteousnesse put on by
faith; and obtruding to them that
rotten ragge of iustification by their
owne workes.
                     EVerie proud man is odious before
God, ô my soule, but specially the
proud hypocrite, who looking vnto man,
his brother, is not ashamed to crie out:
Stand apart,
                        Esay 66. 5. 
                        come not neere me, for I am holier
then thou: O God, I thanke thee that I am
not as other men,
                        Luke 11. 12. 
                        extortioners, vniust, adulterers,
or euen as this Publican; I fast twice in

the weeke, I will giue the tyth of all that euer
I possesse. For is not this testimonie giuen
to the one?Esay. 65. 5. 
                        These are as smokes in my wrath,
and a fire that burneth all day; and this to
the other by our God who knoweth all
Iustifiers of themselues, and abhorres
them:Luk. 18. 14. 
                        but this man went home vniustified.
Could these blinding Robbers, and proud
Pharisees the Papists of this our age see
this, ô my soule, would they not begin
to curse the first inuenters, and venters
of that hellish doctrine of Iustification by
workes and aduancing of mans merits?The inuē
                           ters of Iustification by workes are to be cursed. To
my iudgment, there is not a Papist liuing
this day, yea, that there was neuer a Papist,
who liued before these our dayes,
who is or was sanctified in a higher measure,
or made instruments of such good
workes, as Moses that faithfull seruant of
God was, louing his God with a zelous
loue, louing Gods people with a laborious
loue; yea, what Papist could euer haue
alledged, or can this day alledge, that he
was or is more crucified to the world; or
had, or hath the world more crucified
to him, then Moses had it? for cannot
Moses (through the grace of God)
renounce all the honours, riches, and

pleasures of the land of Egypt, and content
(esteeming the rebuke of Christ, his
onely riches, honour, and pleasure) to
affliction
                           •
                        , yea most sharpe long affliction,
with, and for Gods people. And yet when
this great God drawes neare this same
Moses, Moses must be content to heare
this said to him:Exod. 3. 5. 
                        Come not hither, put thy
shoes off thy feete, for the place where thou
standest is holy ground. What Papist can
with a conscience, or countenance aduance
himselfe aboue Ioshua, that faithfull
seruant of God? and yet when that mightie
holy God draweth neare to him, Ioshua
must heare that said to him which was
said to Moses before him:Iosua 5. 15. 
                        Lose thy shoes
off thy feete, for the place where thou standest
is holy. What if the Papist could compare
that which he may reade by Moses in
the 34. of Exodus, and by Paul in the
4. of the Romanes, with that (a alas) he
hath brought to his eares by the smooth
flattering tongues of his lying Seminaries
and to his eyes by the poysoning volums
of his deceiuing teachers? would he not
be ashamed before God to alledge anie
Iustification by workes, or to obtrude vnto
his Maiesties owne merites? When I

reade the 34. of Exodus, I first see Moses
comming downe from the mount Sinai
where he had stayed 40. dayes talking
with his God: Secondly, I see the skum
of Moses face shining so brightly after
that God had talked with him, that not
the children of Israel only, but Aaron also
is affrayed to come neare him; whereupon
Moses was compelled to couer his face
with a vaile when he spake to them, albeit
when Moses came before the Lord
to speake to his Maiestie,Exod. 34. 29. 31. 32. 33. 34. 35. he tooke off the
couering from his face. When I reade the
4. to the Romanes, I heare Paul confessing
that Abraham looking vnto man
might haue maintained Iustification by
workes, but that he looking vnto God,
behoued to renounce all such Iustification,
fleeing by faith to the free mercie
of God onely, remitting him all his
sinnes to his euerlasting blessednesse in
his blessed Sonne: one man compared
with another man, and comparing before
him, may appeare to shine gloriously; but
if a man could bring himselfe before his
God, all his shining glorie should proue
obscure vanitie, yea blacke like the
tent of Kedar. What wonder that the

Papist hath not learned this, for will he
search Scripture? dare he attempt to
search Scripture, albeit that Scripture be
that onely true looking-glasse in the
which he may see his God, he may see
himselfe? And which is to be lamented, ô
my soule, can he ceasse to lend his eare,
yea wholely to sell himselfe ouer to lying
mans vaine traditions, which makes
white appeare to be blacke, and blacke
appeare to be white; which makes good
appeare to be euill, and euill appeare to
be good.1. Cor. 4. 4. Shall Paul say I know nothing
by my selfe,Iob 39. 37. 38. & 42. 5. 6. 
                        Yet I am not thereby iustified?
yea, shall Iob who could talke freely and
largely before his friends, lay his hand
vpon his mouth, repent in dust and ashes
when he is drawne before his God? And
dare the Papist comming before God
boast himselfe, or dreame that he shineth
in Gods eyes to the Iustification of himselfe?
Bernard reprouing the dead blindnesse
of his time could say: Nec talia sunt
hominum merita, vt propter ea vita aeterna
debeatur ex iure, vt Deus aliquam iniuriam
faceret nisi eam donaret. Nam vt taceā quod
merita omnia dona Dei sunt, & it a homo
propter ipsa Deo debitor est, magis quā Deus

homini. Quid sunt merita omnia ad tantam
gloriam? denique quis melior est Propheta, cui
Dominus ipse tam insigne testimoniū perhibet
dicens, virum inueni secundum cor meum?
Veruntamen ipse Propheta necesse habuit dicere
ne intres in iudicium cum seruo tuo Domine.
The merites of men be not such that by
anie law euerlasting life can be due vnto them
or as if God should do any wrong vnlesse he recompensed
them with eternall life: for besides
this which I will passe with silence, that all
merites of man are the gifts of God, so that a
man for them is rather a debtor to God, then
God a debtor to him; what proportion possibly
can there be betwixt mans merits and that
great weight of glorie which is layed vp in
heauen? And to conclude, what is man better
then that Prophet, to whō God gaue so notable
a testimonie saying: I haue found a man according
to my owne heart,
                        Psal 143. 12 
                        & yet this same Prophet
behoued to say: O Lord enter not into
iudgement with thy seruant, for in thy sight
shall none that liueth be iustified.
                        No works can iustifie. Must thou
not know, ô my soule, y• all workes which
be done by man here, be either euill
workes repugnant to Gods Law, and forbidden
of God; or good workes agreeable
to his Law and commandement, yea,

commanded by him. Euery man of himselfe
can easily do euill workes, which be
condemned and forbidden of God: (for
Man drinketh iniquitie like water;
                        Iob 15. 16. 
                        yea euen
the iust man falleth seuen times a day) and do
grosly infect and defile man.Pro. 64. 12. Good works
againe commanded and commended by
God can no man of himselfe possibly do;
for hearest thou not, ô my soule, the Spirit
speaking thus to thee: We are dead in
sinnes and trespasses:
                        Ephes. 2. 1. 
                        Of our selues we are not
sufficient to thinke any thing as of our selues,
                        2. Cor. 3. 5.
                        but our sufficiencie is of God. Hearest thou
not thy Sauiour (who can deceiue none)
saying to thee:Ioh. 15. 5. 
                        Without me ye can do nothing.
Yea speakes not Paul thus: We are
Gods workmanship created in Christ Iesus
vnto good workes,
                        Ephes. 2. 10 
                        which God hath ordained
that we should walke in them. And will he
not resolue the Philippians thus? It is God
which worketh in you both the will and the
deed of his good pleasure.
                        Phil. 2. 13. Now I must tell
thee, ô my soule, that all men, euen the
dearest Saints and seruants of God, are so
defiled with sinne, that whensoeuer our
God by his Spirit worketh any good
worke in them, and by them, they cannot
but (by that sea of filth which alwayes remaines

in them) defile that good worke
of God, and make it abhominable in his
eyes, if in iustice he would looke vpon it.
And therfore euen the Saints and seruants
of God knowing this, when they are
made instruments of good workes, can
crie out:Iob 14. 4. 
                        Who can bring a cleane thing out
of vncleannesse? there is not one. Yea treading
the pathes of that Euangelicall royall
Prophet Isaiah, they will not be ashamed
thus to blesse themselues, to the end
they may honour their God:Isa 64. 6. 
                        We haue all
bene as an vncleane thing, and all our righteousnesse
as filthie clouts. This moued Augustine
to say:Aug. ep. 106 
                        Opera ex gratia, non ex operibus
gratia; quoniam fides quae per dilectionem
operatur, nihil operatur, nisi ipsa dilectio Dei
diffundatur in cordibus nostris per spiritum
sanctum, qui datus est nobis; nec ipsa fides esset
in nobis, nisi Deus vnicuique partiretur mensuram
fidei. Good workes are of grace, and not
grace of good workes; because faith which
worketh by charitie, could worke nothing vnlesse
the loue of God were shed abroad in our
hearts, by the holy Ghost which is giuen to vs;
yea faith could not be wrought in vs, vnlesse
our God imparted to euery one of vs a measure
of faith. Yea, this moued him to say:

                        Cum malus sum, nihil aliud est confiteri tibi
quam displiceri mihi; cum vero pius, nihil
aliud est confiteritibi quam hoc non tribuere
mihi quoniam tu Domine benedicis iustum,
sed prius cum iustificas impium. When I am
wicked, offending thee, I cannot otherwayes
confesse my selfe to thee, but being displeased
with my selfe for grieuing of thee: when I am
vpright, doing good, I cannot better confesse
my selfe to thee, then by not challenging the
doing of that good to my selfe, because thou, O
Lord, doest blesse the iust man, and yet before
that, thou iustifiest him being vniust and without
God. This moued him also to hold this
for a firme ground: Cum Deus remunerat
opera nostra, coronat in nobis dona sua. While
our God rewards our workes, he crownes in
vs his owne gifts. For as Bernard, who liued
in a corrupt time long after Augustine,
saith, Gratia non solum peccata lauat, sed
etiam merita donat. The grace of God not
onely washeth vs from sinne, but gifteth vs
also with merit.
                        Iustifiers of themselues are no sons to God but mercenary slaues. Alwayes here led by Scripture
I must say more to thee, ô my soule,
whosoeuer dare attempt to thinke or alledge,
that he should onely refraine his
hands from euill, walking before God
and among men holily, to the end that

thereby he may merit eternall life at the
hands of God, cannot possibly carrie the
honest heart of a louing sonne, nor the
cleane hand of an vpright seruant, but
doth prooue himselfe to be a very mercenarie
slaue worthie to be put out of Gods
doores; for as God loued vs freely, so he
will be freely loued of vs. This moued our
wisest Maister, whose words neuer sauored
Popish doctrine, thus to direct his disciples:Luk. 17. 10.
                        When ye haue done all these things
which are commanded you, say we are vnprofitable
seruants, we haue done that which was
our dutie to do. The sense hereof moued
Augustine sweetly to say: Hoc affectu & desiderio
colendus est Deus, vt sui cultus ipse sit
merces.
                        August. ep. 120. 
                        Nam qui Deum ideo colit, vt aliud
magis quam ipsum promereatur, non Deum
colit, sed illud quod assequi concupscit. Our
God is with this affection and earnest desire of
heart to be worshipped by vs, that he himselfe
may be the reward of that worship wherewith
we worship him: For whosoeuer worships God,
to the effect that thereby he may merit to
himselfe some other thing beside God, worships
not God, but that other thing which he desires
to obtaine at his hands. The sense whereof
moued him, toning his sweete song with

a loud voice, to crie out: Tunc enim recte,
tunc iuste, tunc pie fit; cum opus bonum in eius
laudem fit, cuius gratia donatur vt fiat. Then
a good worke is done rightly, iustly, and holily;
when it is done for the glorie and praise of his
name, whose fauour and grace made the doer
of it able to do it.
                        In Ioan. tract. 3. And againe. Si gratiam
ideo Deus tibi dedit quia gratis dedit, gratis
ama; noli ad praemium diligere Deum, ipse sit
praemium tibi. If God hath giuen grace to
thee because he hath giuen it freely, see that
thou loue thy God freely, loue not thy God for
any reward, let God himselfe be thy reward
to thee. It was holily and couragiously said
by the three children vnto Nebuchadnezzar,
ô my soule, We are not carefull to answer
thee in this matter;
                        Dan. 3. 16. 17. 18. 
                        behold our God
whom we serue is able to deliuer vs from the
hote fierie fornace, and he will deliuer vs out
of thy hands ô King. But if not (marke this
my soule, I pray thee) be it knowne to thee,
ô King, that we will not serue thy gods, nor
worship the golden image which thou hast set
vp. Resoluing hereby Nebuchadnezzar, albeit
they should be left by their blessed
onely true God to be deuoured by the
burning flames of his fornace, yet they
would not ceasse to worship God, or appeare

to regard his idoll. O when shall
the selfe iustifying Papist begin to take
some paines to know God, and his owne
heart? for could he know these two, he
would seeke for some secret place with
Peter, there to weepe bitterly that euer he
inuented or vented, or professed and
maintained, that damnable poysoning
leauen of iustification by workes, considering
that great and onely true teacher of
our soules hath said:Luk. 16. 15. 
                        Ye are they which iustifie
your selues before men, but God knoweth
your hearts, for that which is highly esteemed
among men is an abhomination in the sight of
God.
                        Ignorance the mother of the vile doctrine of humane merit. Ignorance then, ô my soule, yea,
most grosse ignorance (as thou mayest
see) hath rikled vp that sandie bray of the
Romane synagogue, now running speedily
by its owne force to a decay; and
fearefull vncouth ignorance hath made
the blind Papist to inuent, and vent that
mischieuous doctrine of mans merits.He who would merit must do 3. things. For
must not euen the simplest man confesse,
that whosoeuer would merit any thing
by his working at the hands of God must
do three things: for first, that which he 
doeth, he must do it of himselfe, and by
himselfe; for if he do it by the grace and

strength of another, that other merits and
not he.Ioh. 15. Now if Christ be true, no man can
do any thing which is good but him. And
if Paul be not deceiued, no man doing
any thing by the grace of God can but
with shame boast himselfe of y• which h
                           •
                        
doeth.1. Cor. 4. Secondly, that which the meriting
 man doth, must be done of meere good
will, and not of dutie; for if it be done by
the force of any obligation binding him
thereunto, the doer cannot possibly merit
any thing by the doing of it: and yet I
hope the Papist (if he haue not both cauterised
his conscience, and seared his face
with a brasen countenance) will blush to
alledge that he is not bound to do all, and
more then possibly he can do, and when
he hath done it, that he cannot merit
thereby, if he could heare the voice of
God and beleeue it, as the voice of him
who would be his Father and shepheard:
Ishow mercie vnto thousands of them that
loue me,
                        Ezod. 26. 
                        and keepe my Commandements.
                         Thirdly, that worke which is done by a
man to the end that he may merit by it,
must be proportionable, and answerable
to that reward a man expects for the doing
of it. Now what man liuing here can

possibly do or suffer that which can be answerable
to the worth and excellent valew
of that eternall life layed vp in heauen?
Paul saw that it was a greater gift to
suffer for Christ, then to beleeue in Christ:
and therefore could speake touching the
Philippians thus:Phil. 1. 29. 
                        Vnto you it is giuen for
Christ, that not onely ye should beleeue in him,
but also suffer for his sake. And yet that
same Paul writing to the Romanes can
say:Rom. 8. 18. 
                        I account that the afflictions of this present
time are not worthie of the glorie that
shall be shewed vnto vs. And so from my
heart I pray God make the hautie Papist
at length subscribe from his heart and
with his hand vnto that heauenly poesie:

                           Datua, sed quae non debes, proportio constet,
                           Haud aliter meritum dixeris esse tuum.
                        
Giue those things which be thine owne,
but which thou art no wayes bound to
giue; let there be a proportion betwixt the
gift and the reward, otherwise alledge
not that thou hast any merit. Conclude
then, ô my soule, if thou wouldst appeare
iust before that onely iust Iudge, as I saiah
concludeth: We haue all bene as an vncleane
thing,
                        Isa. 64. 6. 
                        and all our righteousnesse as filthie
clouts; as Paul concludeth: I know nothing

by my selfe,
                        1. Cor. 4. 1. 
                        yet I am not thereby iustified. As
Bernard concludeth, taught by the Spirit,
and led by the Scripture long ago. Sufficit
mihi ad omnem iustitiam,
                        Ber. serm. Cant. 23. 
                        solum habere propitium
eum, cui soli peccaus; non peccare Dei
iustitia est, hominis iustitia Dei indulgentia.
It suffices me for my whole and perfect righteousnesse,
to haue him mercifull vnto me, against
whom I haue sinned. Gods righteousnesse
is not to sinne, mans righteousnesse is Gods
indulgence and free pardon. And therefore
ô how neatly, how truly, how pretily was
it said: Dare non dignis res mage digna Deo
est. It is a thing most worthie of our God,
who is goodnesse, mercie, liberalitie it
selfe, to giue euer grace and glorie vnto
those who being vnworthy of themselues
merit confusion and eternall death.
                  
                  
                     THE SIXTH ROBBER IS
the Popish Seminarie, with a shamelesse
face and bloudie hand, stealing
from the child of God the mediation
and intercession of that sole Mediator
God and man, euen the Man
Christ Iesus, & putting in his hands
the intercession of Saints.
                     
                        
TRue sauing prayer,Sauing prayer is a royall wise ambassadour. ô my soule, may
iustly be styled, that royall ambassadour,
prudent and couragious, who lodging
alwayes in a cleane cabinate, is directed
from that greatest king, towards that
greatest monarch, and who can no wayes
vpon anie condition be moued to stay
from iourneying forwards till he come
before him, to whom he was sent; discharging
that commission which he carrieth
in his bosome: and besides him neither
to minion, nor courtiour, nor anie of
his subiects whatsoeuer. Tell me, ô my
soule, can anie in heauen, anie vnder heauen,
teach thee to pray for thy saluation,
besides that great King, euen the spirit of
the Father, and of his dearest Sonne? and
therefore that great teacher of the Gentiles,Rom. 8. 26.
can resolue thee thus: The spirit helpeth
our infirmities, for we know not what to
pray as we ought, but the spirit it selfe makes
requests for vs with sighes that cannot be expressed.
This ambassadour of prayer comming
from the spirit, cannot lodge but in
the quickned soule, and reneued heart of
Gods child. Reprobates I confesse may
possesse manie delicates, but this delicate
of sauing prayer they cannot haue, and

therefore the said great teacher of the
Gentiles, can marrie, as it were, Prayer
& Saluation, after an inseperable manner,
together saying:Rom. 10. 13. 
                        Whosoeuer calleth vpon
the name of the Lord (to wit, being led by
the spirit of adoption, the onely author
of heauenly supplication) shall be saued.
Sauing prayer besides this is so prudent,
and couragious that being sent by the spirit,
from the honest heart of Gods renued
child, towards that onely superexcellent
monarch God his Father, it will not giue
so much as a looke, let by a God-speed
(as it were) to anie Angel, to anie Saint
in heauen, vnto anie man in earth, (being
so directed by that spirit by whom it was
sent) till it come before that great Maiestie
of the God of heauen, with whom
onely it hath bene, & there in his bosome
poured forth it selfe. O my soule, art thou
not thus charged by God the Father,
Call vpon me in the day of thy trouble.
                        Psal. 50 15. Art
thou not thus charged by God thy Sauiour?Mat. 6. 9.
                        when ye pray pray thus. Our father
which art in heauen? art thou not thus
charged by God thy comforter, and keeper.Iames 1. 5.
                        If anie aske wisedome, let him aske it of
God. Search, search, ô my soule, the whole

old Testament, the whole new Testament
and trie if thou there mayest gather,
either with a precept directing thee to
pray to any in heauen, or vnder heauen,
besides thy God? or with anie, promise
that if thou prayest vnto anie beside his
Maiestie, thou shalt speed? or lastly,
with any practise, shewing thee that euer
any of Gods children euer sent vp their
prayers to any, beside that blessed God in
whom they beleeued.Popish superstitious bablings be no prayers. Vnderstand, vnderstand,
ô my soule, that the ignorant profane
bablings of the blind superstious Papists,
can be no prayers indited by the
blessed Spirit of God; but windie, foolish,
effectlesse words, comming from their
owne deceiued braines and fond imaginations;
for if they come from Gods Spirit,
they would be directed vnto God
onely.The Papist police in aduancing his lying doctrine of inuocation of Saints. But since they be drawne vp vnto
creatures, they cannot come from the
true Spirit of that creator blessed for euermore,
but from the lying spirit of base
cursed creatures. The blind bloudie restlesse
Seminarie compassing the earth to
and fro with Satan, shewing alwayes
where he commeth (any occasion being
offered to him) he is poysoned, and poysoning

people, either to impede the receiuing,
or to hinder the grouth of the
good wheate of Gods word; to the end
that he may perswade men and women of
all rankes, euen with greedinesse, to embrace
his lying doctrine, touching the inuocation
of Saints: hath verie highly heretofore,
and doth still, verie farre aduance
that foolish comparison taken from the
courts of earthly Princes; and this comparison
he hath hatched, to the end he may
the more subtily aduance the grandour
& wealth of that vile court of Rome and
with this draw away, not onely poore
simple people from being truly courteours,
with that King of glorie blessed for
euer; but also to stirre them vp (albeit he
abhorreth to confesse this) to make themselues
grosse and auowed traitors against
his Maiestie.While the Papist cō
                           pares Gods kingdome vnto a court, they trauell to m
                              •
                           ke vs traitors to the king of that court. O shamelesse Papist is not
this thy fond allegance! As subiects (considering
the grandor of their Princes, and
their owne basenesse) are accustomed to
go to their kings by courteours and noble
men. So the children of God, considering
the excellencie of that Maiestie wherewith
their God is clothed, being sensible
in the meane time of their owne vilenesse

by reason of these sinnes wherewith they
are clogged, should not attempt to go to
their God, but by these Saints which are
in heauen. Hadst thou, ô effronted Papist,
hearkened vnto yt answer, (now neare by
twelfe hundred yeares ago) giuen to this
purpose,Ambr. on Rom. 8. by that famous Bishop of worthie
memorie, Ambrose: thou wouldest
haue bene affrayed from receiuing gredily
without any shew or reason, that effectlesse
comparison; and from keeping it so
pertenatiously, euen to this day, without
any kind of shame? for this cause men and
women are moued to go to kings, by noble
men and courteours; because kings be
but men, and know not to whom they
should commit the gouernment of their
countrey: but while a man hath to do
with his God, from whom nothing can
be hidde (for all men are knowne by him)
we haue neede of no such mediator, but
of a deuout humble holy heart: for whensoeuer
such an heart shall speake, God
shall louingly answer it. But deceiued, and
deceiuing Seminarie! to what purpose
will this thy comparison serue thee in that
countrey where the king with whom
thou hast to do, hath by a speciall Edict,

vnder his great seale and publicke proclamation
raised thereupon, authorised his
eldest Sonne, to be the onely mediator,
by whom his subiects great and small,
any wayes offending him, or standing in
neede of any thing at his hands, should
haue recourse vnto him; discharging
them herewith vnder the highest paine, to
make any suite by the mediation of any
other whatsoeuer? Secondly, if the Prince
the Kings eldest sonne, being thus authorised
by his father, haue by his publicke
proclamation (hauing receiued from his
father speciall warrant so to do) certified
all his fathers subiects, that none of them
possibly can come to him but by him?
Thlrdly, if the Lords of the Kings secret
counsell, being certified of the truth hereof,
would beside this (being commanded
by the King and his sonne) charge all
the subiects to come to the Kings sonne,
yea, to his sonne onely, whensoeuer they
haue to do with the King his father.
Now, ô blind bold Seminarie, I appeale
thy conscience, vnlesse thou hast layed aside
all conscience, and made that whore
of Babell thy God, if thou be acquainted
with that voyce which was sounded from

the heauens, that day in the which that
blessed sole Sauiour of the world was
baptized?Mat. 3. 17. 
                        This is my welbeloued Sonne in
whom I am well pleased. Yea, hearest thou
not this voyce sounded ouer againe with
an addition, that day in the which that
holy one was transfigured:Mat. 17. 6. 
                        This is my welbeloued
Sonne in whom I am well pleased
heare him. O Seminarie, wilt thou not
heare the sonne saying to thee?Iohn 14. 6. 
                        I am the
way, the verity, & the life, no man comes to the
Father, but by me. Hearest thou him not
thus secretly inuiting thee to come directly
to him?Mat. 11. 28. 
                        Come vnto me all ye which are
wearie and laden, and I will ease you. Yea, ô
Seminarie possessed with a deafe diuell,
when God speaketh to thee by his word:
wilt thou not heare that great Apostle
Paul, who was well acquainted with the
whole counsell of God saving vnto thee?
There is one God and one Mediator betwixt
God and man, euen the man Christ Iesus.
Bernard from his heart, subioyning with
his hand vnto this sounded by Saint Paul,
could say:1. Tim. 2. 5 Ber. ser. in cant. 48. 
                        Vnus est vitae dator, vnus mediator
Dei & hominum, homo Christus Iesus,
qui dicit sponsae suae: Salus tua ego sum. There
is one giuer of life, and one mediator betwixt

God and man, the man Christ Iesus: who
saith vnto his spouse, I am thy saluation. Sure
I am, were old Christome aliue, he would
as farre condemne the auowed profane
mad folly of the superstitious Papist in
this point, as he commanded the holy
wisedome of that sincere woman, whose
daughter was possessed with a diuell: for
speakes he not thus touching her? Behold
the wisedome of the woman,
                        Chrysost de Cana. 
                        saith he, she prayeth
not to Iames, she maketh not her supplication
to Iohn, she goeth not to Peter, neither
respecteth she the companie of the Apostles,
requiring helpe of any of them, but in stead of
them all, (taking happily vnfained repentance
for her companion,) she goeth directly
forward to blessed Iesus, that onely well
which was able to yeeld out that sweet water
which she thristed for.
                        Amb. in lib. Isak. 
                        Ambrose saw this
while he could say: Christus est os nostrum,
per quod patri loquimur; oculus noster, per
quem patrem videmus; dextra nostra, per
quam patri nos offerimus; quo nisi intercedente,
nec nobis nec sanctis omnibus quicquam
cum Deo est. Christ is our mouth by the
which we speake to the father; our eyes by
the which we see the father; our right hand,
by the which we offer our selues to the father:

without whose intercession, neither we, nor any
of the Saints haue any interesse in, or accesse
to, God. And therefore what wonder that
Irenaeus before Ambrose writeth thus:Iren. lib. 2. cap. 57. 
                        Non
rationibus angelicis fiat aliquid, nec aliqua
praua curiositate; sed mundae & purae orationes
dirigantur ad Dominum, quia omnia fecit,
& nomen Domini nostri Iesu Christi, cuius
nomen omnia praestat, & curat, non autem
alterius cuiusquam. Let nothing be done by
the counsels of Angels, or through any wicked
curiositie; but let our cleane and pure prayers
be directed to that God who made all things,
and to the name of our Lord Iesus Christ,
whose name helpes and cures all things, and
not to the name of any other whatsoeuer. But
will the restlesse Seminarie rest, ô my
soule, when these things are brought from
the very mouth of God vnto his eares?
no, no, for the tricking Seminarie who
can cunningly catch simple soules by his
entrapping subtilties, will confesse, that
blessed Iesus that onely Son of that great
King, is the onely Mediator of reconciliation
betwixt God and man; but with this
he will maintaine, that there be other Mediatours
of intercession besides him, who
may make and do make request vnto God

for vs. Spare not, spare not, ô my soule,
to say vnto the shamelesse pert Seminarie
when he speaketh thus, Auoide Satan:
as one sent ou
                           •
                         by that craftie foxe, and
cruell dragon, first by his subtiltie to snare
thee, and then by his crueltie to slay thee;
demanding him euen from a strong heart
and with a good countenance thus: O Seminarie,
out of what booke, out of whose
mouth, learnedst thou to put a difference
betwixt the Mediatour of reconciliation
and intercession?None can be the Mediatour of intercessiō but who is the Mediatour of reconciliatiō. for out of Gods Booke,
out of Gods mouth, speaking to thee by
Scripture, thou learnedst it neuer; albeit no
booke besides Gods booke, no mouth
besides Gods mouth, must in this point
informe thee: for telleth not Gods booke
me, and so Gods mouth, first, that we haue
no mediatour who can possibly intercede
for vs at the hands of our God, but that
mediatour who hath reconciled vs to our
God, for be not these the words of Paul:
There is one God and one Mediatour betwixt
God and man, the man Christ Iesus. If Paul
had spoken thus, There is one mediatour
betwixt God and man, the man Christ Iesus;
he had spoken enough to conuince
the lying Seminarie, but he will say more,

euen this: There is one God and one Mediator
betwixt God and man, the man Christ
Iesus, to make the Seminarie ashamed (if
he could be) of his subtiltie; for hereby
he would tell thee, ô my soule, that as
there is one onely true God, and no waies
in any respect another, euen the Father,
Sonne, and holy Ghost; so there is onely
one true Mediator, and in no respect another.
Secondly, telleth not Gods booke,
and so Gods mouth me, that this Iesus
Christ could not possibly haue bene a Mediatour
of intercession for vs, praying to
God for vs, vnlesse he had bene a Mediatour
of reconciliation for vs, by his bloudie
sacrifice, satisfying his Fathers iustice
for our sinnes. O vile Seminarie, darest
thou giue that great disciple (whom Iesus
loued, and who lay in Iesus bosome) the
lye? for speakes he not thus. If anie
man sinne,
                        1. Ioh. 2. 1. 2 
                        we haue an Aduocate with the
Father, Iesus Christ the Iust, and he is the
reconciliation for our sinnes. Thus ioyntly
ioyning Christs intercession and reconciliation
together; and from his reconciliation
of vs, proouing that he hath
onely right to intercede for vs; for if he
had not reconciled vs, he could no wayes

haue any right to pray for vs, neither durst
we haue attempted to haue had any recourse
to him as to our Mediatour; yea,
which is more ô my soule, if he had not
bene our onely Reconciler, he could not
haue bene our Mediatour at all. Augustine
writing vpon this place out of the sense
hereof speaketh thus: Ioannes non dixit aduocatum
habetis sed habemus,
                        August. 
                        nec me habetis
(dixit) sed Christum posuit nonse, maluit se
ponere in numero peccatorum, vt haberet Aduocatum
Christum, quam ponere se pro
Christo aduocatum, & inueniri inter damnandos
superbos fratres. Iesum Christum ipsum
habemus aduocatum ad patrem, ipse est
propitiatio peccatorum nostrorum; hoc qui
tenuit, haeresin non facit. Inde enim facta sunt
schismata, cum dicunt homines nos iusti sumus,
nos sanctificamus immundos, nos iusti ficamus
impios, nos petimus, nos impetramus.
Iohn said not ye haue an Aduocate, but we;
neither said he, ye haue me, but putting Christ
for our aduocate not himself; for he had rather
haue put himselfe amongst the number of sinners,
to the end he might haue Christ for his
Aduocate, then to make himselfe aduocate in
Christs stead, and so in the end to be found among
those proud brethren who shall be damned.

We haue Iesus Christ the iust himselfe
for our Aduocate with the Father, he is a
propitiation for our sinnes, whosoeuer holds
this maintaines no heresie, makes no schisme;
for schismes proceed of this, when men say, we
are iust, we sanctifie the vncleane, we iustifie
the wicked, we pray, we obtaine. O when
shall the blind Popish Seminarie thinke
and write as honorably of that excellent
worke of mediation, as Tertullian thought
and wrote of it, for sees he it not to be so
excellent, that he can find neither Angell
nor man any wayes fit for it? yea, that he
must affirme that none can be mediatour
betwixt God and man but he who was
God. And therefore prouing Christ to be
God amongst other arguments he vseth
this:Tert. in lib. de Trin. 
                        Cur homo in orationibus inuocatur,
cum inuocatio hominis ad praestandam salutem
inefficax iudicetur? cur spes in illo ponitur
cum spes in homine maledicta referatur?
Wherefore is man called vpon in our prayers,
seeing the calling vpon man for the obtaining
of saluation must be thought altogether ineffectuall?
Wherefore do men trust in him, seeing
the confidence which is put in man is cursed?
Augustine after Tertullian saw this also,
when he said: Quem i
                              •
                           uenirem qui me

reconciliaret tibi?Aug lib. 10. conf. cap. 42. an eundem fuit mihi ad
Angelos, qua prece, quibus sacramentis? multi
conantes ad teredire, neque per seipsos valentes
sicut audio, tentauerunt hos, & inciderunt
in desiderium curiosarum visionum, &
digni habiti sunt illusionibus. Mediator autem
inter Deum & homines, oporteret vt
haberet aliquid simile Deo, aliqu
                              •
                           d simile hominibus;
ne in vtroque similis hominibus, longe
esset à Deo, aut in vtroque similis Deo, longe
esset ab hominibus. Whom could I finde who
was able to reconcile me to thee? should I haue
gone to the Angels, by what prayer, by what
allegation? many pressing to returne to thee,
and not being able by themselues, as I heare,
haue assayed to do this, and haue fallen headlong
in the loue of curious visions, and haue
bene thought worthie of mocking and scorning:
for it behoued that he who should be
Mediatour betwixt God and man, should
haue some thing like vnto God, and some
thing like vnto man; lest being in euery thing
like vnto man, he should haue bene farre from
God, or lest being in euery thing like vnto
God he should haue bene farre from man: and
so be no mediatour. I wonder if euer the
Papist Seminarie read that ancient Father
Epiphanius in his 74. heresie, where by

nine strong arguments he proues that the
Virgin Marie should haue no prayer
made to her, and so be vsed as a mediatrix
by any. O how sweetly brings Augustine
in the Christian soule, when death is
drawing neare it, speaking thus touching
the onely Mediatour Iesus, and to the
onely Mediatour Iesus:August. 
                        Tutius & incundius
loquor ad meū Iesum, quam ad aliquem
sanctorum spirituum Dei; plus debet mihi
Christus quam alicui caelestium spirituum:
Quod ego sum, fieri dignatus est Deus, non factus
est quod est Angelus; ad curiam Dei sui,
Dei tui, praecess
                              •
                            Deus tuus, homo tuus, tunica

interpellat. Quem igitur habes intercessorem,
habes Mediatorem, constituet ibi propitium
adiutorem; & si Deus prote, quis contrate.
I speake more surely, more ioyfully vnto
my Iesus, then I can speake vnto any of the
holy spirits of God: Christ is all and more vnto
me then vnto any of those heauenly spirits. God
dained himselfe to be that which I am: he was
not made that which the Angels is. Thy God,
thy man, clothed with thy particoloured coate
hath gone before thee into the court and hall
of this God, of thy God. There he doth alwayes
intercede and make request for thee;

and therefore make him to be thy gracious
helper, whom thou hast for thy Intercessour
and Mediatour: and if God be with thee who
can be against thee. When I consider this, ô
my soule, I shall neuer wonder that Bernard
knowing with Peter and Iohn, That
among men there is giuen no name vnder the
heauen whereby a man can be saued beside the
name of Iesus, spake thus of the name of
Iesus.Bernard. 
                        Nomen Iesus est mel in ore, melos in
aure, iubilis in corde; nomen quod instar olei
lucet praedicatum, pascit recogitatum, lenit
& vngit inuocatum. The name of Iesus is
honie in the mouth, pleasant melodie in the
eare, aiubile and exultation in the heart. The
name of Iesus is a name which being preached
shines like oyle, being meditate vpon feedes,
and which being called vpon comforts and annoints.
O when shall the Papist be moued
to see and confesse that to be true, which
Augustine confesseth both truly & chearfully?Aug. ep. 49.
                        Quanto magis pia est creatura, & subdita
Deo, tanto minus se tali honore dignatur,

The more religious and subiect vnto God a
creature is, it accounts it selfe to be lesse worthie
of that honour which it knowes belongs
to God. These holy Angels allowes no sacrifice,
but that which according to the doctrine of
true wisedome and religion is offered vp to
that onely one true God. Therfore as the wicked
pride, either of men or of Angels, commands
or desires these honours to be giuen to
them which be due to God; so the religious
and holy humilitie either of men or of Angels,
haue forsaken these things, and haue shewed
men vnto whom they be due. And so holy Angels,
holy men, true worshippers of the
true God, do alwayes crie with that
Angell which was sent to

                  THREE MOST
FEAREFVLL ROCKES
layed in the way of Gods
babes, iourneying towards heauen:
threatning their present ouerthrow, if
they be not escheued by the light of the
Spirit, their leader; and of the word their
lanterne; holden forth by the man
of God their watchman.
                  
                     
                        2. TIM. 2. 19.The foundation of God remaineth sure, and
hath this seale: The Lord knoweth who
are his, and let euerie one that calleth vpon
the name of the Lord depart frō iniquitie.
                  
                  
                     
                        PSAL. 130. 4.Mercie or forgiuenesse is with thee that thou
maiest be feared.
                  
                  
                     
                        ROM. 6. 15.Shall we sinne because we are not vnder the
Law but vnder grace? God forbid.
                  
                  
                     
                        MAT. 7. 22.Not euerie one that saith vnto me Lord, shall enter into
the kingdome of heauen, but he that doth the will of
my father which is in heauen.
                  
                  
                     
                        TIT. 1. 16.They professe that they know God, but by their workes
they denie him, and are abominable, and disobedient,
and to euerie good worke reprobate.
                  
               
               
                  
                  
                  TO THE VERY
SINCERELY RELIGIous,
and truly Noble Lord;
DAVID, Lord CARNEGY of Kinnard;
Lord of his Maiesties priuie
Counsell, and Senator of the honorable
Colledge of Iustice.
                  
                     IF anie thing could
come from my hands,
my verie religious,
Noble good Lord,
worthie your Lordships
fauorable countenance (vnlesse
I would be accused by that twilight
of nature, and condemned by that
cleare light of grace, my God hath
not altogether denied vnto me; blessed
be his name) I am most strictly
obliged, were I as swift of foote as

                     Hazael was, to runne with my whole
strength to present it; both heartily,
and humbly vnto your Lordship.
Was I not so farre honoured of God
being yet a babe? that from my infancie,
I had your Lordships sincerely
and truly religious father of
most rare worthy memorie, for my
louing, and kindest father? and since
his Lordships death to this day, haue
I not alwayes had your Lordship for
my constant patrone, and louing
fosterer? It hath pleased my good
God to bring to my hands a subiect,
not vnworthie your Lordships consideration;
and which hath refused to
go forth to the world vpon any condition,
till it was couered vnder your
Lordships nourishing, and protecting
winges.
                  I haue reincountered with these
cruell cunning Robbers, layed by
Satan that Dragon and foxe in the
way of the babes of God, to cut them
off, lest they should in the end attaine

vnto that home of heauen they
looke for: and discouered these
Robbers to the sight of a valorous
Dauid, who will proue readie, and
able to apprehend and ouerthrow
them.
                  I am now to meete (my worthy
good Lord) with those fearefull
Rockes, subtile Satan (abusing alas
the foolish minds and foule hearts of
manie professors) hath euen with
their owne consent and applause,
layed in their way to their wrack.
                  I am to come to that more then
glorious Inne, towards the which the
babes of God do iourney, and within
the which they are to rest for euer.
Yea, I am to intreate of the Guestes
for whom that endlesse rest, which is
to be found within the golden gates
of this Inne, is prepared. Now to
whom possibly could I haue presented
these Rockes, to be considered
and discouered vnto the babes of
God, to the end that they might

eschue them beside your Lordship?
who being taught of God, hath happily
learned to adore Gods holy oracles,
and to abhorre all hellish conclusions;
and who is a Pilot ledde by
the Spirit and lanterne of his word, is
not onely able to shew the babes of
God where these Rockes do lie, but
by your Lorships wholesome counsell,
and holy carriage, to stirre
them vp to take their course by
them.
                  Who so fit to allure men towards
that Inne of heauen, as your Lordship?
who liuing among men for
some yeares, hath alwayes bene walking
with God with Enoch, and before
God with Abraham; hauing
your conuersation in the heauens,
setting your affections on things
which are aboue, and not which are
on the earth; and so able out of a
sense of these things which God hath
prepared for those who loue him, to
exhort all men, casting away euerie

thing that presseth downe,
                     Heb. 12. 12. 
                     and the
sinne that hangeth so fast on, to runne
with patience the race which is set
before them, looking vnto Iesus, the
author and finisher of their faith. To
whom could I offer the consideration
of the condition of these guests,
for whom that Inne of heauen is prepared,
omitting your Lordship? who
being taught of God knowes, that
not all those who crie:Mat. 7. 21. 
                     Lord, Lord, shall
enter in the kingdome of heauen, but
those who do the will of that father
which is in heauen;
                     1. Ioh. 3. 2. 3 
                     that whosoeuer hath
this hope in him, that when Christ shall
appeare he shall be like him, seeing
him as he is; purgeth himselfe as he is
pure. Alwaies (in respect of these large
promises made vnto him by God)
cleansing himselfe from all filthinesse
of the flesh,
                     2. Cor. 71. 1 
                     and spirit; and growing vp
in full holinesse in the feare of God.
From my soule, beseeching my good
God for the sonne of his loues sake, so
to sanctifie, and to guard your Lordships,

with your Lordships present,
and future Noble posteritie that your
Lordship with them, happily declining
these fearefull Rockes, and pleasantly
iourneying towards that heauenly
Inne, may at length, as guests
fitted of God for it, be receiued to
lodge within it, possessing in Gods
presence, fulnesse of ioy, and at his
right hand, pleasures for euermore.
                  
                     Your Lordships most
humble deuoted:
D. L.
                  
               
            
            
               
                  
                     
                     THE FIRST ROCKE
is a grosse abuse of Gods holy Predestination,
and Election; which men of
corrupt mindes, vnchast eares, blasphemous
mouthes, and vile liues,
peruert as they do other Scriptures, to
their owne destruction.
                     
                        WOe is me, woe is me, ô my
soule, that that bold vncleane
spirit, should find (euen
vnder this great and
cleare light of the Gospell)
not a few men, not onely mocke that
comfortable doctrine of Gods eternall
Predestination and Election; but tred it vnder
foote, as the verie foundation of all
securitie, and debaucherie; opening their
foule mouthes, and spewing fotth like
most vncleane dogges these vil
                           •
                         speeches:
If I be appointed to heauen, let me wallow
euen with pleasure in all kind of filthinesse, yet
I shall be saued. Tremble, tremble, ô thou

blasphemer of the blessed word of the
most high God, and repenting thy selfe
of this thy wickednesse, pray God, that
if it be possible, this hellish thought of
thy diuellish heart and abhominable
speech of thy vncleane lips, may be forgiuen
thee: for beleeue me, the child of
God appointed and looking for saluation,
thought neuer thus, speakes neuer
thus. Well is Gods child acquainted with
the nature of Gods elect, and therefore
he abhorres some, and loathes himselfe,
onely for sinne; he smiles alwayes
vpon holinesse, and loues himselfe onely
in so farre as he finds himselfe endued
with grace to loue and practise holinesse.
True it is, ô my soule, that the elected
child of God knowes that God his father
did make choise of him in his Sonne Iesus
before the foundation of the world. But
with this he knowes that this was done
not to the end that he should thinke, that
he should speake, so loosely, so abhominably
as the vile blasphemer of God, and
the reprobate doth, but to the end, that he
should be holy, and without blame before
him in loue who did chuse him.Eph. 1. 4. Well
is Gods elect child acquainted with

that great seale engrauen on both sides,
and not on the one side alone, wherewith
our God sealeth those he hath appointed
to be heires of his euerlasting inheritance.
Hauing on the one side this heauenly
Motto: The foundation of God remaineth
sure; and The Lord knoweth who is his owne.
And here behold, ô my soule, beside this
Motto, as it were ye pleasant pourtraicture
of Gods free election drawne. And on
the other side, hauing this for an inscription:2. Tim. 2. 19.
                        Let euery one who calleth vpon the name
of the Lord depart from iniquitie. And here
behold, ô my soule, beside that inscription,
y• shining pourtraicture of true sanctification,
which Angels, which diuels, which
men shall not be able to separate from
Gods election. But which is more, ô my
soule, the wise, humble, and holy elect
child of God, well instructed out of the
word of God his Fathers booke, out of
the which he learnes all these lessons,
whereby to gouerne himselfe: while he
knowes that the election of God his Father
stands euer most sure and stable, in respect
of his God who changeth not; yet,
feeling himselfe to be subiect to a verie
world of tentations and crosses, he cannot

ceasse in the feare and reuerence of his
God, whiles he liues here, to make his election
more and more sure to h
                           •
                        mselfe, and
that by eschewing all euill; the loue and
practise whereof he knowes cannot stand
with the election of God; and by louing
and doing good, yea by ioyning goodnesse
vnto goodnesse vncessantly: for he
dare not attempt to thinke that his God
hath drawne him toward his Maiestie by
the soft and strong co
                           •
                        d of his eternall election,
while Satan is pulling him backe,
and he is willingly following after him,
ledde in that blacke and vile halter of
sinne. Thou must not wonder, ô my soule,
that the elected child of God carrieth
himselfe so, for are we not Gods children,
thus charged by the Spirit? Giue diligence
to make your calling and election sure,
                        1. Pet. 1. 5. 6 7. 8. 
                        ioyning
vertue with your faith; and with vertue,
knowledge; and with knowledge, temperance;
and with temperance, patience; and with patience,
godlinesse; and with godlinesse, brotherly
kindnesse; and with brotherly kindnesse, loue:
for if these things be amongst you, and abound,
they will make you that ye neither shall
be idle, nor vnfruitfull in the knowledge of our
Lord Iesus Christ.
                     
                  
                  
                     
                     THE SECOND ROCKE
is a foule abuse of the grace of God,
which vncleane men turne into vncleane
wantonnesse; delighting, alas,
to commit sinne, because that good
God delighteth to forgiue sinne.
                     MAny wayes, alas, ô my soule, doth
miserable man wrong God his gracious
maker: yea, many men called Christians,
do grosly grieue that holy one Iesus,
who hath called them to that high
dignitie to be called the sonnes of God:
but in this specially, that they take occasion
to commit sinne, yea to continue in
sinne, with some pleasure and contentment,
because God the Father out of his
vndeserued loue, borne freely to man, hath
giuen his Sonne to dye for man, because
his blessed Sonne out of this same loue
hath humbled himselfe willingly, yea,
chearfully to the death for man; so that
blind nature, common ciuilitie, Gods
truth, their owne consciences, Angels,
and well informed, or any waies, reformed
men, cannot but condemne them, yea
pronounce them to be execrable. Woe is
me, ô my soule, that euer subtle and strong

Satan should haue preuailed so ouer man,
that man now can be content to abuse
that salue which is onely able to cure him,
yea that he doth runne headlong vpon
that sharpe slaying sword of sinne, because
he heareth that salue is prepared for the
curing of him. All men confesse, ô my
soule, that that second couenant of grace
made betwixt God and man in his blessed
Sonne Iesus, that second Adam (who neuer
fell nor can fall) is of greater moment,
and alwayes more glorious then that first
couenant of workes, which was made in
that first Adam who stood not long, but
fell fearefully. And canst thou deny but as
our God hath obliged himselfe more
strictly to man by this second couenant of
grace, then he was by that first of works:
so man is become nearer, yea sibber to
God by the last then he was by the first;
and in that respect obliged to worship and
attend his Maiestie, so much the more diligently,
faithfully, and constantly? findest
thou, ô my soule, when thou readest and
cōsiderest Scripture, but God thy maker,
perceiuing that first couenant of workes
made betwixt him and man, broken by
man, prooued iust; and so adiudged man

with all his posteritie vnto that death
threatned against him and them, in case
that couenant should be violated by
them? And shall not our God, hauing giuen
his owne Sonne for man, proue much
more iust in condemning all such who
dare attempt to despise that bloud shed
by him for sinne, by selling themselues ouer
to sinne, because his bloud was shed
for buying them from sinne? If a Iew hauing
the Law of God put in his hand by
Moses,
                        Leuit. 18. 5. hearing Moses sound this in his
eares:Deut. 27. 26. 
                        Do this and liue: Cursed be he that
confirmeth not all the words of this Law to do
them: could with Abraham see by faith
the day of the blessed Messias a farre off,
and reioyce in it, he were easily freed from
that curse: for blessed Iesus (who was
made a curse for vs) blesseth all those
whom Moses curseth, prouiding they can
repent and beleeue in him. But ô Gentile,
liuing now not vnder the Law, but vnder
the Gospell, not hauing Moses, the seruant
of God for thy doctor, but Iesus, the Son
of God for thy Maister: what if thou shalt
take vpon thee not to abuse that Law giuen
by Moses, but that grace dearely cost
and louingly brought to thee by Iesus?

                        
                           〈1 page duplicate〉
                        
                        
                        
                           〈1 page duplicate〉
                        
                        
where shalt thou finde salue to cure thy
sore, and medicine to heale thy disease?
Let me anger Moses through breaking
of the Law: let Moses threaten me for
breaking of the Law: If I can but touch
with a liuely faith the hemme of Iesus
garment, I shall find peace with God, and
health with life to my selfe. But if I shall
anger Iesus, who shall pacifie him? where
shall I find a sacrificer, to satisfie him; hauing
despised that bloud shed by him for
me? Oh, ô my soule, when shall that sentence,
yea, that byting sentence be hearkened
vnto, by the monstrous, vile, loose
gospellers of this profane, licentious, leacherous
time, He that despised Moses, died
without mercie, vnder two or three witnesses.
Of how much sorer punishments suppose
ye, shall he be worthy which treadeth
vnder foote the Sonne of God, and
counteth the bloud of the Testament as
an vnholy thing, wherewith he was sanctified,
and doth despise the Spirit of grace.
That patient who among men doth despise
the kindest wisest,Heb. 10. 28. 29. the painefullest,
and best approued Physician, is thought
to be desperately diseased? And shall not
that man, ô my soule, who dare (taking

himselfe to sinne, Christs onely enemie)
neglect Iesus, renounce Iesus medicine,
die for euermore? for can Angels, can
Saints, triumphing in heauen, can Saints
fighting on earth, yea, can diuels euer
dying in hell cure him, whō Iesus will not
cure, who dare refuse to be cured by Iesus?
Yea, who is not affrayed to cast that cup
(euen the blessed word of God, and Sacraments
annexed thereto, in the which
the wholesome potions of saluation are
kept, and by the which they are conueyed
to the sicke soules of Gods children)
vnder his feete? Do not Peter and Iohn
triumphantly crie.Act. 4. 12. 
                        There is no name vnder
the heauen by the which a man can be saued,
but by the name of Iesus. Yea, doth not
Augustine,
                        August. who was no Papist, taught of
God and ledde by Scripture, maintaine
that which Peter and Iohn did proclaime:
for he doth see no Sauiour, but one; euen
sweet Iesus: Nemo liberat à vulneribus
illius trucidatores, nisi gratia saluatoris; nemo
liberat venundatos sub peccato, à vinculis
captiuitatis, nisi gratia redimentis. None freeeth
man from the wounds of that murtherer,
but the grace of that Sauiour: none deliuereth
those who be sold vnder sinne, from the bonds

of spirituall captiuitie and thraldome, but his
grace who redeemeth them. Sure I am, ô my
soule, were Iude, that blessed Apostle of
Iesus, liuing this day, he would change his
tune, if he were writing either to vs, or
of vs, (who liues now vnder such a dispised,
abused, great light) writing to those
of his time,Iude 4. he was content to say: There
are certaine men crept in, which were before
of old ordained to this condemnation; vngodly
men there are which turne the grace of our
God into wantonnesse, and denie God the onely
Lord, and our Lord Iesus Christ. But were
Iude liuing now among vs, he could not
but say, and write thus: There be manie
men, who do resort to the house of God, who
call vpon the name of God, who daily in
troopes runne on foote, ride on horsebacke,
keeping their solemne meetings in citie and
countrey, who turne the sauing grace of God
into damnable wantonnesse, denying (albeit
not with their foule mouthes, yet by their
vile deeds) that God and Lord who would
haue saued them. Oh, ô my soule, when
shall that golden sentence written by
Augustine be heard of vs,August. who liues now?
be honoured and embraced by vs as a
wholesome medicine able to cure vs? as a

precious Iewell able to honour vs? Quid
nobis gratia Dei vtilius confert in hoc praesenti seculo
maligno,
                        Aug. Epist. 47. 
                        nisi vt moriamur peccato?
ac per hoc ipsi gratiae inuenietur ingratus,
qui propter illam vult viuere peccato, per
quam morimur peccato.
                        Iude 4. 
                        What more profitable
thing doth the grace of God in this present
wicked world bring to vs, then that by it
we are made to do the same? so that, that man
must by this be found vnthankefull to the
grace of God, who because of it, will liue in
sinne, by the which we are made able to die to
sinne? Oh when shall the loose gospellers
hearken to Irenaeus saying to them? Vt
aucta est gratia sub nouo Testamento, ita &
poena eorum qui non credunt. As grace is
augmented now vnder the Gospell, so the
punishmēt of those, who beleeue not, is encreased
also. And no wonder that he write so,
considering that his Maister writ before
him touching Chorasin, Bethsaida, and
Capernaum: Wo be to thee Chorasin, wo be
to thee Bethsaida, for if the great workes,
which were done in you, had bene done in Tirus,
and Sidon, they had repented long ago in
sackcloath and ashes.
                        Mat. 11. 21. 23. 24. 
                        Therefore I say vnto you,
it shall be easier for Tirus, and Sidon, at the
day of Iudgement then for you. And thou

Capernaum which are lifted vp vnto the heauen,
shall be brought downe to hell, for if the
great workes which haue bene done in thee,
had bene done among them in Sodome, they
had remained to this day. But I say vnto you
it shall be easier for them of the land of Sodom
at the day at Iudgement then for thee. Giue
no place to sinne, ô my soule, because
Christ died for sinne, and by his death
hath purchased remission of sins to thee,
not forgetting thee: which the Apostle
saith to thee.2. Cor. 15. 14. 17. 
                        If one be dead for all, then were
all dead: and be died for all, that they which
liue should not hence forth liue vnto themselues,
but vnto him which died for them, and
rose againe. Therefore if any man be in Christ
let him be a new creature.
                     
                  
                  
                     THE THIRD ROCRE IS
A foolish leaning (without anie
ground) to a naked profession of God,
with the mouth, without any practise
of godlinesse in thy life.
                     COmparing the protestation of our
professors, with their conuersation,
I haue for some bygone yeares lamented

(before my God in secret,) ô my soule,
the desperate estate of this our deaddest
age. Our professors do protest that they
do know and worship that God who
made not only the heauens and the earth,
but who made that booke which is onely
worthy the stile of a booke, to wit, the
Bible, and that they hold this booke, for
the booke of this God; indited by his
Spirit, and put in register by his pen-men,
ledde by this same spirit: yet our professors
so liue, as all who do looke on
them, and heare them (being truly sensible
of the true God, and truly instructed
by the Spirit of truth out of his word)
must euen solemnely sweare, that the effects
of a great manie of them, do either
denie this God who made the Bible, to
be that God whom they worship; or the
Bible to be Gods booke. Offend not
rashly, ô my soule, that I speake so to
thee: for after triall (alas) this will proue
to be most true. If our professors did hold
that God who made that booke which
we call the Bible for their God, would
they not striue to worship him, and to
liue with men, and among men, as God
by this his booke hath appointed them to

do? Againe, if our professors, ô my soule,
held the Bible for Gods booke, indited
by his Spirit who cannot lye, calling
nothing good but that which is good
before God, and which leadeth man toward
the narrow way of saluation, calling
nothing euill but that which is euill before
God, and which draweth man towards
the broad way of perdition, could
they be so easily induced to transgresse
those lessons our God by this booke teacheth
them, and vnder no lesse paine then
of remedilesse, endlesse, condemnation
commands them to obey? yea, durst they
for ten thousand worlds attempt to do
this? I wonder, ô my soule, if our gallants
(whom nothing can tame) do hold that
speech for the speech of God (who cannot
lye of faine)?Eccles. 11. 9 
                        Reioyce ô yong man in thy
youth, and let thy heart cheare thee in the
dayes of thy youth, and walke in the wayes of
thine heart, and in the sight of thine eyes, but
know that for all these things God will bring
thee to iudgement.
                        Eccl. 12. 14. 
                        God will bring euery worke
vnto iudgement with euery secret thing whether
it be good or euill. I wonder if our mad
whoremaisters and whoores, if our abhominable
blasphemers, if our brutish drunkards,

if our filthie speakers, do hold these
speeches for the speeches of the great
God, before whom they must one day appeare,
and giue an account of their whole
carriage here, publicke in the streets and
priuate in chamber, by night and by day?
Men do not despise a thiefe when he stealeth
to satisfie his soule,
                        Prou. 6. 30. 31. 32. 33. 34. 35. 
                        because he is hungrie; but
if he be found he shall restore to seuen fold, or
he shall giue all his substance of his house: but
he that committeth adulterie with a woman
is destitute of vnderstanding he that doth it,
destroyeth his owne soule, he shall find a wound
and dishonour, and his reproach shall neuer be
taken away. For iealousie is as the rage of
man, therefore he will not spare in the day of
vengeance, he cannot heare the sight of anie
ransome, neither will be consent though thou
augment the price.
                        1. Cor. 6. 9. 10. 
                        Know ye not that the vnrighteous
shall not inherit the kingdome of
God? Be not deceiued, neither fornicators,
nor idolaters,
                        Ephes. 5. 3. 4. 5. 6. 
                        nor adulterers, nor wantons,
nor buggerers, nor theeues, nor couetous, nor
drunkards, nor raylers, nor extortioners, shall
inherit the kingdome of God. But fornication
and all vncleanenesse, or couetousnesse, let it
not be once named among you, as it becometh
Saints; neither filthinesse, neither foolish talking,

neither iesting, which are things not
comely, but rather giuing of thankes. For
this ye know, that no whooremonger, neither
vncleane person, nor couetous person, which is
an idolater, hath any inheritance in the kingdome
of Christ and of God. Let no man deceiue
you with vaine words; for, for such
things commeth the wrath of God vpon the
children of disobedience: be not therefore
companions with them.
                        Reu. 21. 8. 
                        But the fearefull and
vnbeleeuing, and the abhominable, and murtherers,
and whooremongers, and sorcerers,
and idolaters, and all lyers, shall haue their
part in the lake, which burneth with fire and
brimstone, which is the second death. Yea, I
wonder, ô my soule, if the Kings and Princes,
and mightie men of this world do
hold that speech for the speech of God:
And the kings of the earth, and the great men,
and the rich men,
                        Reu. 6. 15. 16. 17. 
                        and the chiefe captaines, the
mightie men, and euery bondman, and euery
free man hid themselues in dennes, and among
the rockes of the mountaines, and said to the
mountaines and rockes fall on vs, and hide vs
from the presence of him that sitteth vpon
the throne, and from the wrath of the Lambe;
for the great day of his wrath is come, and
who can stand? Our professors then, ô my

soule, for the most part can neither hold
that God who made the Bible for their
God, neither the Bible for his booke, considering
that sensible, hard, and seene exposition,
may easily be found to be betwixt
their liues and Gods lessons taught
in this Bible. And therefore without
doubt, they haue madly (miscarried by
that vncleane spirit) set vp to themselues
their owne hearts lustes, to be both their
God, whom they will serue, and that onely
booke which they will learne and follow.
I know one Scripture, ô my soule,
which shall condemne thousands, who
heare and reade Scripture (alledging
they hold it for Gods word) vnlesse
they repent speedily.Iam. 2. 12. 
                        Thou beleeuest that
there is a God, thou doest well. The diuels also
beleeue and trembleth. Oh, ô my soule,
when shall a great many amongst vs, and
professing with vs, learne to do that
which the diuell doth; well knowes he,
that the onely true God who made the
heauen, and the earth, made the Bible also;
and that this Bible is the booke of that
God, who is the onely true God, yea, that
all things contained in it be most true: albeit,
alas, many men neglect and contemne

that which they heare out of the
Bible, that which they reade in the Bible,
while the diuel knowing these things can
tremble, assured that he is adiudged by
that most great and most iust Iudge of the
world vnto eternall condemnation, as the
Bible speaketh. Shall Satan who doth beleeue
Gods word to be true, and who can
tremble at the sound of it be condemned?
and shall he escape the feare 
                           •
                        ullest damnation
which shall be found in hell, who is
so far from trembling at the iudgements
of God, brought to his eares out of Gods
word, that he makes but a mocke of
them? It were good they were thinking
vpon that, spoken by our God touching
the old foolish vncleane Iewes: Will ye
steale,
                        Ier. 7. 9. 10. 
                        and murther, and commit adulterie,
and sweare falsly, and burne incense vnto
Baal, and walke after other gods whom ye
know not, and come and stand before me in this
house whereupon my name is called, and say
we are deliuered, though we haue done all
these abhominations? Were Paul liuing, sure
I am, no sooner would he lend his eares
vnto a great many of our professours, but
he would say ouer againe: They professe
that they know God,
                        Tit. 1. 16. 
                        but by their workes they

denie him, and are abhominable and disobedient,
and to euery good worke reprobate.
And no wonder, for the voice of our blind
sensuall professours is this, ô my soule: I
loue God, and cursed be he who loues not God.
But, ô blind foole, when shalt thou begin
from an heart sensible of God, and with a
cleane mouth honouring God, to say, I
loue godlinesse, and cursed shall he proue at
length who loues not godlinesse. The voice of
our blind sensuall professors is this, I hate
the diuell, I defie the diuell, and all his works.
But when shall they begin from an honest
heart, and with true lips to say, I hate sin,
and cursed shall he proue at length who hates
not sinne. O when shall that of Augustine
be taken to heart by our vncleane professours?Ep. 171.
                        Christianos vos dicitis & Christo contradicitis.
Ye call your selues Christians, and
you contradict Christ alwayes. Open our
professours eyes ô Lord by thy Spirit, to
the end that they may once happily see
that which Bernard brought to the eares
of the loose professours of his time: Vnde
tibi gloria putide puluis? de vitae sanctitate,
quid tibi prodest pium Saluatoris nomen lectitare
in libris: nec habere pietatem in moribus.
Whence commeth glorie and honour
                        
vnto thee, ô stinking dust, from the holinesse
of thy life I thinke it commeth onely? for what
can it profit thee to reade the holy name of thy
Sauiour in bookes, while that thou hast not
holinesse in thy manners. And againe. Is
Scripturas recte legit, qui verba vertit in
opera. That man readeth holy Scripture
aright, who turneth words
into workes; doth that in his
life which he reades in
the Scripture.
                  
               
            
         
         
            
               
                  
                  THAT ONELY
GLORIOVS INNE,
AND BRIGHTLY SHIning
palace, filled with all pleasures
and ioyes, towards the which the
Babes of God do iourney in time laboriously:
and in the which they
shall liue eternally, with the nature
and condition of those
babes who shall possesse it.
                  IOH. 14. 2.
                  In my Fathers house are many dwelling
places, if it were not so, I would haue told you:
I go to prepare a place for you.
                  IOH. 17. 24.
                  Father, I will that these whom thou hast
giuen me be with me where I am; that they
may behold the glorie which thou hast giuen
me, for thou louest me before the foundation
of the world.
                  REVEL. 20. 6.
                  Blessed and holy is he, who hath part in the
first resurrection, for on such the second death
hath no power: but they shall be the Priests
of God, and of Christ, and shall reigne with
him a thousand yeare.
               
            
            
               
                  
                  
                  THE INNE WITHIN
THE WHICH THE BABES
of God carried in this heauenly Chariot,
lookes to lodge and alwayes to rest;
is that new Ierusalem which is aboue,
where there is fulnesse of ioy to be found
in Gods presence, and pleasures
lasting for euermore at his
right hand.
                  
                     THat Inne towards the
which this heauenly golden
Chariot drawne by
these heauenly white horfes,
carries these babes of
God, (happily ledde and directed by the
Spirit, and enlightned by the lanterne of
the word, held in the hand of the Preachers
thereof) free of the foresaid Robbers,
and Rockes; is that new Ierusalem
which is aboue, made vp of pure gold,
like cleare glasse; whose wall, ô my soule,
is of lasper, founded vpon twelue precious

stones: euen vpon a Iasper, a Saphire, a
Chalcedome, an Emeraud, a Sardonix, a
Sardin, a Chrysolite, a Berill, a Topaz, a
Chrysophrasus, a Iacinth, a Amathist: whose
twelue gates, are twelue pearles also,
whose streetes are pure gold shining like
glasse, whose temple the Lord God almightie
and the Lambe is, which hath
neither Sunne, nor Moone, beside the glorie
of God, and of the Lambe. In the
light whereof the people that are saued
do walke, and to the which the kings of
the earth shall bring their glorie, and honour;
whose gates are neuer shut, which
is inriched with a pure riuer of water of
life, cleare as cristall, springing out of the
Throne of God, and of the Lambe; hauing
in the midst of the streete of it, and
on the other side of the riuer that tree of
life which beareth twelue manner of
fruites, and giueth fruite euerie moneth,
the leaues whereof do heale the nations,
where Gods seruants being free from all
curse, (for no curse can possibly enter
there) shall serue him, seeing alwayes his
face, and hauing his name written in their
foreheads, reigning with him for euer.
But canst thou tell me, ô my soule, what

shall be the estate and condition of those
who shall be admitted to be citizens
within this new Ierusalem, and Inne of
heauen, they being once happily possessed
of it? To handle this matter to the full,
and so to lay open to thee, ô my soule,
the nature of this Inne as it deserueth, and
as it is in it selfe; it is not in the power of
Angels, or of men: for heare I note first
that royall,Esay 64. 4. Euangelicke, Prophet Isaiah,
and then that great Apostle Paul crying
out:1. Cor. 2. 9. 
                     The eye hath not seene, the eare hath
not heard, neither came it to mans heart, to
thinke of these things which God prepareth
for them that loue him?
                     2. Cor. 12. 4 Yea, Paul who
had a greater proofe of the beautie, glory,
aand superabundant riches of the things
which are to be found in this Inne, being
rauished vp towards it, confesseth that he
saw things there not to be vttered. Hearken,
hearken therefore, ô my soule, I pray
thee, for heare I must tell thee that the
skilfulnesse of Arithmeticke can not number
out these good things which are to
be found there. That the deepenesse of
Geometrie, cannot measure the length,
and breadth, the higth, and the depth of
those good things which be layed vp

there: Yea, that the swiftest and sweetest
tongue of the most rarely eloquent Orator,
is not sufficient to expresse the worthie,
and excellencie of them: for when
this Citie, and Inne is looked vpon by him
whose eyes be enlightened from aboue
by the Lord of it. The Arithmetician, the
Geomerticiā the Orator must stand amazed
and crie out. Neuer saw I an Inne before,
ye pleasures, the plenishing, the beautie
whereof I was not able to reckon, to
measure, and to declare. But behold here
an Inne, filling my eares so, my eyes so, my
smelling so, my tasting so, my touching
so, yea, my heart aboue all things so; that
I am like (through the superabundance of
passing excellent things, may delight my
hearing my seeing, my tasting, my touching,
and if I were not sustained by a
stronger, euen by that blessed, yea, onely
Lord and Ma
                        •
                     ster of this Inne) to
loose my hearing by hearing, my sight by
beholding, my smelling by smelling, my
tasting by tasting, my touching by touching;
those things which be there to be
heard, seene, smelled, tasted, and touched.
Yea, I would loose my verie heart and life.
And no wonder, ô my soule, yt it be so, for

in that Inne of heauen, thy God shall be
a bright shining looking glasse to thy
sight, a sweetly sounding Fluit, & Cimball
to thy hearing, a delicious honie combe
to thy tast, odoriferous balme to thy
smelling, and a passing wonderfull soft
pleasant rose to thy touching: What man
of sharpest sight can behold this outward
Sunne which God himselfe hath appointed
to enlighten this world, which is the
common Inne of the elect, and reprobate,
in his full brightnesse and glorie, and not
haue his eyes hurt thereby? And shalt
thou, ô my soule, behold that supreamest
Maiestie of the Father, and of the Lambe,
that onely Sonne which doth enlighten
this Inne, (within the which no reprobate
can enter) vnlesse thou be fortified by one
stronger then thy selfe, and blessed with
a more strong, quicke sight then thou
canst here beneath attaine vnto? what
mans eares are not transported, when he
heares a number of sweete voyces, singing
artificiall musicke in diuerse parts formerly
and melodiously. And shalt thou not
find thy selfe wonderfully transported, ô
my soule, when thou shalt be brought
within thy Inne, to be a hearer, not onely

of the sweetest musicke of the glorified
Saints; but of these celestiall Spirits the
Angels, there inioying the pleasures of the
spring, the glorie of the Summer, the
plentie of the haruest, and the sweet rest
of the Winter? But no wayes hearing, or
seeing, or feeling any hurt which euer
came to man by any of these. This moued
Bernard meditating vpon the estate of
Gods glorified children in heauen,Ber. Ser. 33. in cant. to
burst forth in these words, not without a
speciall exclamation, and admiration: O
perenne Solstitium, quando iam non inclinabitur
dies! ô lumen meridianum! ô vernalis
temperies! ô aestiua venustas! ô autumnalis
vbertas! ô quies & feriatio hiemalis! O euerduring
stay of the Sunne, (for that Sunne
which shineth in this Inne, neuer goeth
downe, but alwayes shineth in his hight)
when the day shall not incline to the end! (for
the day which riseth in this Inne shall last
for euer) O noone-tide light! ô the sweetest
temperance of the spring! ô the pleasantnesse of
the Summer! ô the plentie and abundance of
the haruest! ô the rest and refreshing vacants
of the Winter! If this low house of the
world, be so richly furnished with a verie
world of diuerse pleasant, profitable, and

glorious things, (being the lodging not
onely of the children of God, but of the
children of wrath) ô how rich must that
house of God be furnished with pleasure,
profit, and glorie; within the which none
can dwell, beside that blessed great Gods
elect Angels, and dearest sonnes, and
daughters! Augustine finding himselfe ouercome
by the consideration of the glorie
of this Inne of heauen, could say: Si
id quod ex parte est non valuit eloqui ne
                           •
                         expertus,
quid de perfectione inexpertus balbutire
conatur. Oculus non viditò Deus absque
te, quae praeparasti diligentibus; pax super
pacem, indeficiens exultatio, torrens voluptatis
diuinae, flumen laetitiae, gaudium plenum;
cogita quicquid vis, quicquid potes exopta,
excedit cogitationem omnem, desiderium
omne exuperat illa felicitas, aeternitas illa,
beatitudo illa. If that which is but in a part
could not be expressed by him who had proofe
thereof, wherefore should he who is inexpert,
attempt to babble about it. The eye sees not ô
God without thee the things which thou hast
prepared for those that loue thee: peace aboue
peace, triumphant indeficient ioy, a peale
of heauenly pleasure, a floud of gladnesse, full
ioy: thinke vpon any thing thou pleasest, wish

after what thou may; that happinesse, that
eternitie, that blessednesse, surmounteth all a
man can thinke, and sensibly ouercomes all a
man can desire. Augustine pressing to make
this his assertion cleere vnto vs, can crie
out.Aug. de doc. Chrsti. lib. 1. cap. 15.
