                     Quibus verbis dici, aut qua cogitatione
capi potest, praemiū quod Christus in vita futura
daturus est? quando ad consolationem
huius itineris tantum dedit de suo spiritu, vt
quod faciendum est, non solum sine murmure
sed etiam cum dilectione, & delectatione faceamus,
in aduersis etiam gaudentes, & fiduciam
in eum, quem non videmus, ponentes: By
what words can that reward be expressed, or
by what thought can that reward be apprehended,
which Christ shall giue to his owne in
the life to come? seeing for the consolation,
and sweetning of this their iourney, he
hath giuen them such a measure of his owne
Spirit, that we are made to do that which we
should do, not onely without murmuring, but
also out of loue, and with pleasure, reioycing
euen in tribulations, and putting our confidence
in him, whom as yet we see not. O what
happinesse, what honour, what glorie,
what peace, what charitie? yea, what incomparable
plentie of all things, shall the
glorified Saints inioy there? Shall not that

happinesse be wonderfull excellent there,
where no euill can be found, where no
good thing can be wanting? What a glorie
shall be there, where none who is praised
can be praised, either by the error, or
the flatterie of those who do praise them?
What honour shall be there, when honors
shall not be refused to any who is worthy
of honour, neither can be giuen to anie
who is vnworthie; yea, where none vnworthie
of honour shall presse for honour,
and where none can come but those
who be worthie of it? what peace shall be
there, where none can possibly suffer any
hurt or wrong, either from themselues or
from any other? O what loue shall be
there, where no inferiour shall enuie the
superiour, nor any superiour contemne the
inferiour! O how excellent shall the free-will
of man be there, ô my soule! When
God made Adam to his owne Image, he
beautified him with that free-will, whereby
he might haue not sinned. But in that
Inne of heauen this shall be mans happie
freewill, and mans happinesse, because of
this his free-will that he shall not be able
to sinne. O what plentie shall be there
possessed by man, when he shall haue nothing

which he would want, and when
he shall want nothing which he would
haue? Augustine saw this when he said: In
ciuitate superna,
                     Aug ep. 3. 
                     atque diuina, iam non est
molestè toleranda calamitas, nec laboriosè
fraenanda cupiditas, sed sola sine vlla difficultate,
& perfecta libertate retinenda, Dei &
proximi, charitas. In that heauenly Citie
which is aboue, there shall be no calamitie
with trouble to be suffered, neither any concupiscence
or lust with paine to be bridled: but
there the onely loue of our God and of our
neighbour to be retained and kept without
any difficultie and paine, and with perfect libertie
and freedome. The sense hereof moued
Bernard to say:Bern. 
                     In coelis erit securitas
libera, & libertas secura, neque aduertendi
erunt de caetero oculi ne videant vanitatem;
quia purissimam videbunt venustatem, quae
est ista copia, vbi nihil quod nolis sit, vbi totum
sit quod velis. In the heauens there shall be
free securitie, and secure freedome, for there
the children of God shall not haue occasion
any more to aduert to their eyes, that they behold
not vanitie, because they shall alwayes
see most pure and pleasant comelinesse: ô what
abundance is this, where there is nothing
which thou wouldst not haue, and where all

that is which thou wouldst haue. And thus
thou mayst see, ô my soule, that the glorie
and happinesse of this Inne of heauen consisteth
in two things: to wit, in the absolute
necessarie presence of all good, and in
the absolute necessarie want of all euill
things: for in it there is such abundant
beautie of euerlasting righteousnesse,
such an inexpressible pleasant world of
shining, quickening, and refreshing light,
that howbeit it were not lawful for a man
to stay there, but for the space of a short
day; yet for a very short dayes abiding
there, he would heartily content himselfe
to despise and depriue himselfe of all the
pleasures, honour, and wealth can be
found here, and with ioy vndergo and vnderlye
all those euils he can suffer here,
to the end he might but liue there but for
the space of a short day. Had Dauid (out
of the sense of these comforts which were
to be found by the exercise of religion)
the outward tabernacle of God in such
account,Psal. 84. 1
                           •
                        
                      yt he could say: A day in thy courts
is better then a thousand other where: I had
rather be a doore keeper in the house of my
God, then to dwell in the tabernacles of wickednesse.
And shalt thou not find in the end

of thy time, when thou shalt enter within
that Inne of glorie, that it were better to
stay there for one day if it were possible,
then to liue with Methusalah 969. yeares,
adorned with vncertaine, perishing pleasures▪
honours, and riches? Beside this, ô
my soule, knewest thou what a stole thou
shalt weare in this Inne of heauen? yea,
with what a stole this my bodie shall be
clothed there, ô with what earnestnesse
wouldst thou call for the comming of Iesus!
ô with what earnest desire wouldst
thou long for the comming of Iesus! yea,
ô what praises wouldst thou sing to God
thy Father, who hath promised this Inne
to thee, to God thy Sauiour, who hath
conquised this Inne to thee, and to God
the holy Ghost, who assures thee that
this Inne belongs to thee! Thou, ô my
soule, in that Inne of heauen, shalt be richly
and royally decked with a threefold
stole; in beautie, in worth, farre surpassing
all those ornaments and iewels, rich Salomon
was couered with, when he sat in his
royall throne: with the stole of the perfect
knowledge of the blessed and glorious
Trinitie; Father, Sonne, and holy Ghost;
and this perfect knowledge shall fill vp

the roome of that liuely iustifying faith
wherewith on earth here thou art blessed,
and by the which thou apprehendest the
promises of God made to thee in thy Sauiour:
for when thou shalt enter, ô my
soule, within the doores of this Inne of
heauen (all being giuen thee which was
promised to thee, and beleeued by thee)
thy faith shall ceasse, and this perfect
knowledge of God shall meete thee, and
keepe thee for euer. Secondly, thou shalt
be clothed with the stole of the perfect
fruition of inioying of the glorious Trinitie;
the Father, Sonne, and holy Ghost.
And this fruition shall fill vp the roome
of that Hope which now thou hast; for so
soone as thou shalt come to the gates of
this heauenly Inne, in that day of iudgement
that Hope, whereby thou expectest
now those things, thy Father hath promised,
thy Sauiour hath conquised, and the
Spirit assures thee of, shall ceasse also. And
this fruition shall fill the roome of it, thou
being fully possessed with all thou expected.
Thirdly, with the stole of the perfect
loue of the blessed Trinitie, the Father,
Sonne, and holy Ghost; and of the
Saints his children, for then that loue

wherewith thou, ô my soule, now louest
thy Father, thy Sauiour, thy Sanctifier, and
his children shall not then end with thy
faith and hope, when thou shalt enter
within the gates of this Inne; but shall go
in with thee, and being there augmented,
and perfected by a thousand thousand
degrees, shall possesse thee for euermore.
This moued that Apostle who was well
acquainted with these things which be in
heauen to say:1. Cor. 13. 13. 
                     Now abideth faith, hope, and
loue, euen these three; but the chiefest of these
is loue. And therefore Irenaeus taught by
the Spirit, and by Paul, subscribing hereunto
could write thus: Charitas pretiosior
est cognitione, gloriosior prophetia, & omnibus
charismatibus supereminet. Loue is more
pretious then knowledge, more gracious then
prophecie, yea, it surmounts all gifts man
hath. This my bodie againe in that heauenly
Inne, ô my soule, shall be clothed
and adorned with a fourefold stole: first,
with the stole of rare beautie and holinesse,
so that the Sunne in his full brightnesse
did neuer shine so gloriously as my bodie
shall shine in that Inne. Tels not Daniel
me that in the Inne of heauen: The wise
shall shine as the brightnesse of the firmament,
                     Dan. 12. 3.
                     
                     and they that turne many to righteousnesse as
the starres for euer and euer. Yea, are not
these the words of thy Sauiour who cannot
lye:Mat 8. 43. 
                     Then shall the iust men shine as the
Sunne in the kingdome of their Father. Now
thou must not wonder, ô my soule, that
euen the blackest & palest coloured bodie
of the glorified child of God shall thus
shine: for art thou not thus resolued by
the Spirit? We looke from the heauens for the
Sauiour euen the Lord Iesus Christ,
                     Phil. 3 20. 21. 
                     who shall
change our vile bodies that it may be fashioned
like vnto his glorious bodie. Now if Christ
giuing his disciples Peter, Iames, and Iohn,
before Moses and Elias, a little view of
that glorie which is due to him, had his
face shining as the Sunne, and his clothes
white as the light, while he was onely
transfigurate vpon mount Tabur? ô with
what a glorie is he now clothed, in that
mountaine of glorie with his Father! and
and how shall our bodies shine,1. Ioh. 3. 2. who in
heauen shall be like him,1. Cor. 5. 49. bearing there
the image of that heauenly Adam, as here
we beare the image of the earthly? Secondly,
with that singular stole of impossibilitie,
so that howbeit the bodies of the
Saints of God be subiect to a thousand alterations,

and hazards which do manie
wayes trouble and annoy them, yet then
they shall be free of all suspition of alteration,Reuel. 21. 4.
or hazard, all these first things which
here do trouble men being ended. Thirdly,
with that excellent stole of wonderfull
Agilitie, for then our lumpish bodies shall
be freed of that heauinesse which now
doth clogge them, and make vs, that without
great difficultie and paine, we cannot
go from place to place: yea, that without
some outward helpe we cannot vpon a
sudden transport our selues, where we
would fainest be. For now the spirit cannot
go but where the bodie goeth (the
bodie being a burthen to it) but then the
spirit being made the full maister of the
bodie, shall command it to go without
any trouble wheresoeuer it would haue it
to go. And therefore Augustine could say:
Tanta erit tunc corporis agilitas, vt vbi volet
spiritus ibi protinus erit & corpus. Then the
child of God being in heauen, the agilitie and
nimblenesse of the bodie shall be so great, that
where euer the spirit would be, there the bodie
shall be also incontinent. Now thou must
no wayes doubt of this, ô my soule, considering
as thou hast heard that our bodies

in heauen shall be conforme to the
bodie of our blessed Sauiour, and so as
Christs bodie after his resurrection was
adorned with such agilitie, that in a most
short space it could be seene in diuerse
places, now at Ierusalem, now out of Ierusalem,
comming to his disciples vnawares,
& vpon a suddaine departing from
them,Ioh. 20. 19. 26. as Iohn witnesseth: our glorified
bodies shall euen in this be like vnto his.
Yea, what shall I say, shall the bodie of the
Prophet Elias,
                     Luk. 24. 31. and of Philip the Deacon,
soiourning beneath here, be transported
vpon a suddaine from place to place by
the Lord our God:1 King. 18. 12. 46. and shall we doubt
that our bodies being glorified, and made
like to the bodie of Christ shall be inferiour
to them in this point?Acts 8. 9. And ô how
farre shall this augment the ioy of the
glorified Saints, while we liue here: ô
how often do we desire to be with those
who be dearest to vs, and of whom we
are specially loued? yea, is it not a matter
of speciall griefe euen to the dearest
Saints of God, that knowing themselues
to haue deere brethren and sisters, some in
that same kingdome with them, others in
diuerse kingdomes farre remoued from

them, lying vnder sharpe crosses and diuerse
afflictions whom they are not able,
notwithstanding of this, to visite, for imparting
the sweet honie of consolation to
them, being hindered through distance of
place from them. But in heauen, ô how
soone shall we find our selues, not onely
in minde but in bodie also present with
such we do loue, and who do loue vs.
Then Dauid shall haue no cause to crie
from a wounded heart, and with a mourning
tune and countenance:Psal. 42. 1. 2 
                     As the Hart
brayeth for the riuers of water, so panteth my
soule for thee ô God. My soule thirsteth
for God, euen for the liuing God, when shall
I come and appeare before the presence of
God? my teares haue bene my meate day and
night, while they say daily where is thy God?
There Paul shall haue no neede to crie
out:Rom. 7. 14. 24. 
                     What I would that do I not, but what I
hate that do I. O wretched man that I am
who shall deliuer me from the bodie of this
death? If the expectation of these wayes, ô
my soule,Iob. 19. 25. 26. 27. which be in heauen, made Iob
(inuironed with an inward and outward
sea of tentations and crosses) not onely to
digest them, but digesting them to reioyce
in the midst of them: ô what ioy

shall the full fruition of them procure
him? Fourthly, in this Inne of heauen
thou shalt be cloathed, ô my soule, with
the stole of perfect health, and strength;
so that where now the bodie of Gods
child is not onely subiect to great weakenesse,
but to innumerable grieuous, and
most painfull diseases, there it shall be
fully, and finally deliuered from all▪ weaknesse,
or from all feare of any paine or disease
whatsoeuer. This is that whereof
the Spirit would assure thee, when he
saith:Reuel. 21. 4. 5. 6. 
                     Behold the tabernacle of God is with
men, and he will dwell with them: and they
shall be his people, and God himselfe shall be
their God with them, and God shall wipe away
all teares from their eyes, and there shall be no
more death, neither sorrow, neither crying,
neither shall there be any more paine, for the
first things are passed, and he that sate vpon
the throne said: Behold I make all things
new, and he said vnto me, write, for these
words are faithfull and true. Yea, in this
Inne of heauen, one shall be knowne by
euerie one, euerie one by all, embracing
one another, as now the members of one
bodie embrace one another; so that thou
ô my soule, shalt then loue all the children

of God as thou shalt loue thy selfe, and
shalt be loued by him, as thou shalt loue
them: for whosoeuer shall be there, and
all those who shall be there, shall be one
bodie, shall be one Church, shall be one
spouse to blessed Iesus; and therefore the
will of one shall be the will of all: yea,
which is more, ô my soule, there the will
of God shall not differ from thy will, nor
thy will from Gods will; albeit (alas)
while thou shalt soiourne beneath here,
there shall alwayes remaine most grosse,
and fearefull contrarieties, betwixt the
good will of thy good God, and thy peruerse
euill will. Did Adam in his innocencie
know Euah whom he had neuer
seene before, and giue her a fit name so
soone as she was presented before him?
and shalt thou being aduanced to a higher
dignitie in a farre more excellent pallace,
not know all who shall be there? Shall
Peter when our Maister was transfigurate
vpon mount Tabur, know Moses, and
Elias, whom he had neuer seene before?
and shall I not know them when I shall
be glorified by him, and with them in the
mountaine of glorie? I will not denie, ô
my soule, but in this Inne of heauen; there

shall be degrees of glorie,
                     1. Cor. 15. 40. 41. 
                     euen as there is another
glorie of the Sunne, and another glorie of
the Moone, and another glorie of the starres,
for one starre differeth from another in glorie.
This is that the Spirit would cleere vnto
vs,Dan. 12. 3. when he saith: They that be wise shall
shine as the brightnesse of the firmament, and
they that turne manie to righteousnesse shall
shine as the starres for euermore. And we
know that there is difference betwixt the
brightnesse of the firmament, and the
brightnesse of the starres. But I must
tell thee, ô my soule, that this is the priuiledge
of this Inne of heauen, that none
inioying greatest glorie is enuied by him
who inioyes lesse, that none possessing
lesse glorie is condemned by him who
inioyes lesse, that none possessing lesse
glorie is condemned by him who possesseth
more; and therefore out of this
sense I heare Augustine saying:August. 
                     Quòd ibi
futuri sint gradus hominum, nullatenus ambigendum
est, verum beata illa ciuitas magnum
in se bonum videbit; quod nulli superiori
nullus inferior videbitur, tam nollet vnusquisqueesse
quod non accepit. Sic itaque habebit
donum alius alio minus vt hoc quoque donum
habeat quod non volet amplius. That in heauē
                        
there shall be degrees of men we must no wayes
doubt. That blessed Citie shall see that great
good in her, that no inferior shall appeare inferior
to any superiour; so farre shall euerie one
not desire to be that which he hath not receiued
& so one shall haue a gift lesse then another so,
that he shall haue this gift also, that he wisheth
to haue no more then he hath. Now, ô
what ioy shalt thou then, ô my soule, and
enioying be able to expresse when thou
shalt be brought towards this Inne! shall
not thy ioy there breake forth in most
heauenly inexpressible mirth and musicke,
making thee to say to the father! Holy, holy,
is the Lord of Hoastes,
                     
                        
                           •
                        say 6 3. 
                     the whole world is full
of his glorie; stirring thee vpto crie to the
Sonne. Thou art worthie ô Lord to receiue,
glorie, and honour, and power; for thou hast
created all things, and for thy wills sake they
are and haue bene created. This ioy is
compared to the ioy of a marriage,
yea, with the marriage of Kings. Our
minds be now narrower then they can
comprehend this; albeit when the heauens
shall receiue vs, we shall be capable
of it so farre as a glorified creature may
be. Lift vp thy selfe, ô my soule, and proue
holy, wise, when thou hearest these things

if thou wouldst not be condemned in that
great day by one who neuer saw that,
who neuer heard that, which thou seest
and hearest daily. Shall the Queene of the
South hearing the fame of Salomon, and of
the glorie of his court, and kingdome,
long to see that which she heard, yea, vndertake
and vndergo a long wearie iourney,
to the end that she may see? and
shouldst thou not, ô my soule, eate vp they
selfe (as it were) within me, through longing
and earnest desire; sparing neither
for paines, nor expenses, till thou come to
the chamber of that thy bridegroome;
and to that Citie and Inne which is aboue
founded, builded, garnished, and inriched
as thou hast heard? for I assure thee, ô my
soule, as the Queene of Sheba being come
to Ierusalem, and there heard the wisedome,
and seene the glorie of Salomon,
was moued to say:1. King. 10. 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. 
                     It was a true word that
I heard in my owne land of thy sayings, and of
thy wisedome; howbeit I beleeued not this report,
till I came and had seene with my eyes.
But loe the one halfe was not told me, for thou
hast more wisedome and prosperitie then, I
haue heard by report. So thou, ô my soule,
happily by Gods grace being by a liuely

faith ingraft in his Sonne, and without
delay repenting thee of thy sinnes, and
being by death transported to this his
Inne of glorie, to see that with thy eyes,
that which I heare onely with my eares,
shall not onely find all these things to be
there which thy God by his report, speaking
to thee by his written word, shewes
thee to be there; but thou shalt see, and
seeing shalt possesse for euermore, ten
thousand thousand degrees of more glorie,
more ioy, more pleasures, then euer
here thou hardst was there, or sawst here
whilst thou liuest here, to be there. Shall
Peter seeing but a glimps of Christs glory
vpon mount Tabur crie out, (neglecting,
yea, despising all he eue
                        •
                      heard or saw in
Ierusalem, yea in the verie Temple of
God at Ierusalem) Maister it is good to be
here. And shalt thou not, ô my soule,
thinke in a manner euill to be here on
earth, till thou be where thy Iesus is cloathed
with that glorie for euermore, farre
surmounting that transitorie glimpse
which Peter saw beneath here. For wert
thou there, ô my soule, be sure thou
shouldst say, and sing continually, O my
blessed Maister! ô my sole sweetest Redeemer!

It is good to be here, it is onely good to be
here, would to God I had bene here sooner;
for there the Father is, the Sonne is, the
holy Ghost is, his elect Angels, his chosen
sonnes and daughters do liue onely,
free of all feare of euill, possessed with a
very sea of all good. And no wonder it be
so, ô my soule, for here by the word of
God we are onely acquainted (to speake
so with his Maiestie) with the backe parts
of God. But when we shall be transported
to that heauenly Inne, farre remoued from
all euill, and fully possessed with euerie
good thing, as hath bene shewed thee,
We shall see him as he is. The taste of this before
hand moued Bernard to say:Bern. 
                     Infelicit
as media in hoc seculo est pro qua gemimus,
extrema in inferno quam merito formidamus:
felicitas media in paradise vnde
cecidimus, felicitas summa in coelis ad quam
suspiramus. The midde degree of miserie is in
this life, for the which we do sigh; the extremitie
of miserie is in hell, which not without
cause we do feare. The midde degree of happinesse
was in Paradise, from the which we
haue fallen; the onely great and extreame degree
of all true happinesse is in heauen, after
the which with sighing and sobbing we do

                        
                           〈1 page duplicate〉
                        
                        
                        
                           〈1 page duplicate〉
                        
                        
long and hasten vnto. And to conclude this
point: this shall not a little augment the
happinesse of the more then happie estate
of the babes of God, being admitted
within this Inne of glorie, & there admitted
in soule, in bodie, as hath bene said,
that being once possessed with these
things, they shall neuer be depriued of
them againe; but shall vndoubtedly enioy
them for euer and euer. The things of this
world thou knowest, ô my soule, be subiect
to fading, for that shall neuer stand
sure:1. Ioh. 2. 17. 
                     The world passeth away, and the lustes
thereof. But as for these ioyes of heauen,
they do resemble him by whom they be
promised, by whom they be conquised,
and who doth assure vs of them, and so be
no wayes subiect to decay, but do last for
euermore. And therefore Paul doth tell
me that the elect of God in that day of
iudgement (being caught vp in the clouds
to meete our blessed Lord and Sauiour in
the aire) shall after that,1. Thes. 4. 17. euer be with that
our Lord. Wherefore ceasse not, ô my
soule, while I breathe here to crie aloud,
and to sing sweetly with the Psalmist:
Sing ye loud vnto the Lord all the earth,
                     Psal 100. 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. 
                     serue
the Lord with gladnesse, come before him with

ioyfulnesse: know ye that euen the Lord is
God, he hath made vs and not we our selues,
we are his people and the sheepe of his pasture:
enter into his gates with praises, and into his
courts with reioycing, praise him and blesse
his name; for the Lord is good, his mercie is
euerlasting, and his truth is from generation
to generation. Yea, to the end that thou
mayst prooue truly and holily wise, ô my
soule, see that while thou soiourne here,
that thou vse the world circumspectly, as
if thou vsed it not, knowing that the fashion
of this world goeth away;1. Cor. 7. 31 and that
thou rest vpon nothing but vpon that
which is to be found in this Inne of heauen,
euer remembring and neuer forgetting
that of Augustine:
                     August. 
                     Diuitiae si diliguntur
ibi seruentur vbi perire non possunt; honor si
diligatur, ibi habeatur, vbi nemo indignus
honoratur; salus si diligitur, ibi adipiscenda
desideretur, vbi adepta nihil timetur; Vita si
diligitur, ibi acquiratur vbi nulla morte finitur.
If riches be loued, let them be kept there
where they cannot perish; if honour be loued,
let it be had there where no vnworthie person
is honoured; if health be loued, let it be desired
to be found there where being once found
there can be no feare to loose it; if life be loued,

let it be procured and purchased there, where
it can be ended by no death.
                  
               
               
                  THE GHVESTS ADMITted
by our wise God (the sole Lord
of this heauenly Inne) to enter and
to lodge within it; be those alone
who being members of his dearest
Sonne Iesus Christ, be made in time
by him true Christians, and so Prophets,
Priests, and Kings vnto God
their Father.
                  THis Inne of heauen being the verie
paradise and pleasant garden of the
Lord our God, none can possibly be
transported towards it but the trees of
righteousnesse, who being the planting of
God do here on earth glorifie his Maiesty.Esay 61. 3.
This Inne is the sheepfold of that great
Shepheard Iesus, and therefore none can
enter into it but those who be the sheepe
of Iesus,Iohn 10. 7. 14. 27. 28. hearkening to his voice, knowing
his voice,Luk. 12. 32. following his voice, and refusing
to here the voice of a stranger. This
Inne is the wedding chamber of that glorious
Bridgrome Iesus, that eldest Sonne,

and heire of the great King of glorie. And
therefore none can be admitted to enter
within it,Mat. 25. but those who being wise virgins,
haue their lampes alwayes readie,
and their oyle in them, attending in faith,
and yet in feare, his comming. This Inne
is the house of Christs Father, and therefore
none can be suffered to enter within
it, (albeit there be many dwelling places
in it) but those who be the sonnes and
daughters of God the Father,Iohn 14▪ 2. and so the
brethren and sisters of Iesus, carefull to separate
themselues from the wicked, and
not attempting to touch any vncleane
thing. But who contrariwise do cleanse
themselues from all filthinesse of the flesh
and of the spirit,2. Cor. 6▪ 17 18. & 7. 1. growing vp into holinesse
in the feare of God, and alwayes
(out of that hope they haue at length to
lodge in this Inne) purging themselues
more and more,1. Iohn. 3. 3. as God their Father, and
Lord of this Inne is pure; for no vncleane
thing can possibly enter into it, but such
onely who hauing washed their long
robes, haue made their long robes white
in the bloud of the Lambe, and whose
names are written in the Lambes booke
of life.Reuel. 7. 14. 15. And so in a word, this Inne being

the royall palace of Christ that great Prophet,
that high Priest, and that soueraigne
King of Gods elect, none can possibly be
honoured with it: but these who through
this Christ are made Christians,Reuel. 1. 6. by the
vertue of his Spirit, & meanes of his word
and Sacraments: and consequently Prophets,
Priests, and Kings to God the Father.
Would I then, ô my soule, after my
wearie labours here, be possessed with
that worthie rest in heauen? I must studie
necessarily before death to become a Prophet
(for no ignorant shall come there)
acquainted with the knowledge of God
in his Sonne, and of my selfe in nature, and
in grace, and so euery one who lookes for
that Inne of heauen must know themselues
to be miserable because of sinne;
must know God to be mercifull, and readie
to forgiue sinne, in his Sonne Iesus
Christ; and must know that Christ dyed
for them, and that his death became meritorious,
deseruing and procuring remission
of sinnes, and life euerlasting to them
if they can beleeue in him, and repent.
The sense hereof moued Paul to crie out:
This is a true saying,
                     1. Tim. 1. 15 
                     and by all meanes worthy
to be receiued, that Christ came in the world

to saue sinners.
                     2. Cor. 5. 21 And againe: He hath made
him to be sinne for vs, which knew no sinne,
that we should be made the righteousnesse of
God in him. Yea, our Maister in a word
packing vp the whole matter of mans saluation
doth say:Ioh. 17. 3. 
                     This is life eternall, that
they know thee to be the very onely God, and
whom thou hast sent Iesus Christ. Wouldst
thou, ô my soule, after death liue within
this Inne, before death I must be a priest
offering vp to God my Father, Redeemer,
and Sanctifier, not a dead, but a liuing, not
a reasonlesse, but a reasonable sacrifice; yea
not another beside my selfe, but my selfe
vnto his Maiestie, remembring and reuerencing
that holy charge sweetly giuen
to me by that chosen vessell of Christ:Rom. 12. 1. 2. 
                     I
beseech you brethren by the mercies of God,
that ye giue vp your bodies a liuing sacrifice,
holy, acceptable vnto God, which is your reasonable
seruing of God▪ And fashion not your
selues like vnto this world, but be ye changed
by the renewing of your minde, that ye may
proue what is the good will of God, aud acceptable
and perfect. Thirdly, wouldst thou
remouing from thy tent on earth be receiued
within that Inne of heauen, ô my
soule, which is the palace of this great

King, which carries this Motto vpon his
thigh, The King of kings, and Lord of Lords:
I must be a king, for this Inne is for no
men but those who be kings, is for no
women but those who be Queenes, and
so who be true Christians. But what sort
of Kings and Queenes be these, ô my
soule, who shall rest within this Inne?
men & women made kings and Queenes,
not by God the Creator of the world, but
by God that sole Redeemer of mankinde,
and so by Iesus Christ who hath loued
them, and washeth them from their sinnes
in his bloud, and made them kings and
Queenes vnto God,Reuel. 1. 5, 6. euen his Father. And
so I see, ô my soule, that there shall not so
much as one man, as one woman be admitted
within the doores of this Inne of
heauen, but he who is a Christian, but she
who is a Christian, and that not so much
as one true Christian shall be debarred
from it. Thou art a king, but not a Christian,
and therefore thou must stand without,
& haue thy portion in the lake which
burneth with fire and brimstone. Thou art
a Queene, but not a Christian, and therefore
thou must stay without also, to be
tormented with thy king. Thou art a

countrie clowne, and yet a Christian,
and therefore thou must not stay without,
because thou art a clowne but must
go in because thou art a true Christian.
But because in these our dayes there be
such a world of men and women called
Christians, and holding themselues for
good Christians; I would haue thee, ô my
soule, to trie who if these be Kings and
Queenes made by Christ, & so fit ghuests
for this Inne of heauen? Hearken vnto
me speaking with a warrant of Gods
word. None can be such Kings and
Queenes, but those who can be seruants,
and will be seruants; who cannot be seruants,
nor will be seruants; who can be
seruants, and will be seruants to him, who
being the Lord of all, was heartily content
to become a seruant for them; and
so to that blessed and sweete Lord Iesus:
who cannot, nor will not vpon any condition
be seruants to any besides his Maiestie.
Can the true Christian forget
that ransome wherewith he was redeemed,
and can he thinking on it be a
seruant either to diuels or to men? No
no, for he can neuer forget that of Paul.
Ye are bought with a price, be not the seruants

men.
                     1. Cor. 7. 23. 
                     Ye were once darknesse, but now are
light in the Lord,
                     Eph. 5. 8. 
                     walke as the children of
light. And thus the true Christian sees all
these whom he sees in Christ, and cannot
possibly see any out of him; he can honour
and serue his king, his parents, his
neighbours, alwayes in Christ, and for
Christ but no wayes against Christ. And
therefore he can mocke all honour, but
that wherewith Christ is honoured; all
pleasures, but those wherewith Christ is
pleased; and all wealth, whereby his spirituall
treasure is lessened, yea not augmented;
and all life, but that life whereby
his life Iesus Christ is conquised, and
conserued by him: yea, he doth not onely
misknow, but denie all friends and kindred,
but those who in Christ be neare
vnto him: in this resembling his blessed
Maister who did all that he did for him;
who suffered all that which he suffered
for him; holding none for his mother, his
brother,Mat. 22. 50. and sister, but those who do his
Fathers will which is in heauen: and accounting
all such who did this his will,
for his mother, brother, and sister. Could
this be considered, ô what a shame should
couer the face of ye Christians of this age!

ô what a feare should possesse the hearts
of the Christians of this age! O man thou
wilt be a Christian, but not a king ouerruling
the diuell? Thou wilt be a Christian,
yet not a king maistering this wicked
world, either alluring thee to euill by
faire offers, or drawing thee from God,
driuing thee to euill by threatnings, and
punishments, but maistered by it? and that
most willingly not eschuing sinne which
thy Sauiour came to slay, but delighting
in sinne which put thy Sauiour to death.
Were that Marty Blandina
                     Blandina. liuing to this
day, sure I am she would say, albeit there
be many men in the world now, yet there
be wonderous few Christians in the
world now. For in the midst of her torments
she did crie out to the hearing of
her Torturers.Clem. Alex. in orati ad gentes. 
                     Christiana sum, & nihil mali
apud nos geritur: I am a Christian, and
there is no euill thing done against vs. Sure I
am, were Clemens Alexandrinus liuing, he
would subscribe with her: for describeth
he not a Christian thus? Is solus, qui pius
est, ac religiosus, Christianus est: That man
alone who is holy and religious, is a Christian.
Oh, ô my soule, shall not these Christians
who liued in the dayes of Eusebius arise in

iudgement against these of this our time.
These in their liues were so religious,Euseb. Eccles. Hist. lib. 4. cap. 8.
holy, chast, temperate, modest, that the
verie fame of their liues, being brought to
the eares of men, moued all sorts of people,
casting off their natiue superstition, &
forme of liuing, to turne to Christ; yea, the
verie sauage Barbarions, by the report
made vnto them touching the Christians,
layed aside their barbaritie, and fiercenes,
and embracing Iesus Christ, learned of
him to be meeke and lowly in heart. Yea,
what shall I say, ô my soule, if the Christians,
in this our age find not grace in
time to looke about them; the verie ambitious,
curious, auatitious men among
whom they liue, and whose carriage is
knowne to them, shall accuse and condemne
them. What ambitious man can
content himselfe with the honour he hath
gotten, and ceasse to aspire vnto a greater?
what curious man can satisfie his eye with
seeing, or his eare with hearing? Yea,
what couetous man is heard saying, I haue
enough, I will haue no more? And yet alas,
ô how many blind senslesse Christians,
deceiued by Satan and their owne lusts,
and willingly deceiuing thēselues dreame

that they be alreadie sufficiently furnished
with that future Inne, prepared for Gods
children, albeit they haue neither oyle in
their Lamps, nor a Lampe in their hands.
Historie telleth me that Marcus Marcellus
a Romane dedicated a Temple to the
goddesse of Honour, but with all Historie
tels me, that the way to that Temple
of Honour was by the Temple of Vertue;
and canst thou, ô man calling thy selfe a
Christian, looke to be receiued within
that onely honourable Temple, which is
the mansion of that onely Lord, to whom
all honour doth belong, & in whose presence
true honour is onely to be found,
vnlesse thou reserue (treading the way of
vertue and valour here) to fight against
the diuell, and to seeke and to serue thy
God?Hier. part. The sense hereof moued Hierom to
say.3. tract. 4. 
                     Portae duae sunt, porta Paradisi, & porta
Ecclesiae;
                     Epist. 20. 
                     per portam Ecclesiae intramus portam
Paradisi. There be two gates, the gate of
Paradise, and the gate of the Church; by the
gate of the Church we enter into the gate of
Paradise. Yea, this moued Bernard to say.
Non rectised peruersiest animi,
                     Bern. 
                     antea quaerere
gloriam, quam excercere virtutem, & velle
coronari qui legitime non certauerit; virtus

gradus est ad gloriam, verus mater est gloriae.
It is not the nature of an vpright, but of a
froward wicked mind, to seeke glorie before
vertue be exercised, and to heare him desiring
to be crowned, who hath not fought;
vertue is a degree to glorie, yea, vertue is the
mother of glorie.
                     Bern. in Cant. And againe: Quid mihi
cum victoria si non in praelio fui? impudētissimè
mihi arrogo, aut gloriam absque victoria, vel
victoriam sine pugna. What haue I to do with
victorie, if I haue neuer bene in the battell? O
how most impudently do I ascribe to my
selfe, either glorie without vertue, or vertue
without a fight. Learne therefore, ô my
soule, in time to know Christ, in time to
know what it is to be a true Christian, to
the end that I may be perswaded that one
day that onely glorious Inne of heauen
shall receiue me, and receiuing me shall
retaine me for euer; and so see that without
delay thou learne to desire, betwixt
the pretious and the more pretious, and
so betwixt things seene which be temporall,
and betwixt things vnseene which be
eternall. O how manie called Christians
shall be condemned of Iacob in that day
of iudgement, and shut for euer out of the
doores of this Inne of glorie! Iacob being

to receiue his brother Esau, when he
feared, sent first before him his sheepe,
oxen, and camels, after them he placed
both his maides and their children, after
them Leah and her children. But Rachel
and Ioseph (as his most pretious and estimable
treasure) he placed nearest himselfe,
in the safest place: testifying hereby
that he had rather loose all the rest,
before he had loosed them. But alas the
Christians of this our time, ô my soule,
expose the onely best things (that is these
heauenly graces which must leade them
towards that heauenly Inne) vnder danger,
and proue onely curious about the
keeping of the perishing things of this
world nearest them; testifying thereby
that they had rather want Christ, and part
with Christ, then any other thing beside
him. Yea not onely shall they haue Iacob
to condemne them who was the Lords
holy confederate, but the verie brutish
serpent, wanting soule, wanting reason;
for natural prudence teacheth him to hide
his head carefully when he is pursued,
and to yeeld the rest of his whole bodie
to the smiter, to the end that that being
lost which is of smallest weight, he

may happily keepe that which is of greatest
valour. But, alas, ô my soule, our
onely blessed, and glorious head Iesus, is
offered by vs at all times to danger, and
we do keepe these things which cannot
keepe vs, and which we shall not be able
for our verie hearts to keepe long. O
when shall men with Paul learne while
they are here to know none,1. Cor. 1. to know nothing
but Christ, and him crucified; to the
end that in the day of challenge they may
receiue this testimonie of Christ.Luke. 16. 
                     Thou
hast chosen the best part which shall not be
taken from thee.
                     Bern. When shall that of Bernard
written on these words: Behold we
haue forsaken all things and followed thee,
be considered by vs, Nec mutilis commutatio,
pro
                           •
                        eo qui supra omnia est, omnia reliquisse;
nam & simul cum eo donantur omnia,
& vbi apprehenderis eum, erit vnus ipse omnia
in omnibus, qui pro ipso omnia reliquerunt;
omnia sane dixerim, non solum possessionis,
sed etiam cupiditatis. Neither is it an
vnprofitable chance to forsake all things for
him, who is aboue all things, for with him
all things are giuen also, and so soone as thou
apprehendest him, he himselfe alone shall be all
things, to all those who for him hath left all

things; yea, euen all things I say truly, not
onely of possession which a man can haue, but
of desire which a man can wish. Thou seest
then, ô my soule, that thou must seeke thy
God in this wildernesse of thy pilgrimage,
if thou wouldst be found of him in
that wished Inne of his glorie; that thou
must serue him abroad as it were amongst
strangers, yea, amongst sworne enemies,
if thou wouldst reigne with him at home
with his owne onely deare children thy
friends. But here I will haue thee grauely
to consider two things. First how shouldst
thou serue thy God here? Secondly,
wherefore shouldst thou serue him thus?
Thou must serue him, ô my soule, frankly,
and with ioy: and so neither from a grudging
heart, nor with an auerse or froward
countenance. Thou hast, I thinke, long
ago acquainted thy selfe with the third
petition of the Lords Prayer, Thy will be
done in earth euen as it is in heauen: Hereby
first confessing that thy God should be
serued by thee here on earth, as he is by
those celestiall spirits in heauen. Secondly,
earnestly begging grace from his hands
that thou mayst serue him so. Now couldst
thou, ô my soule, learne to consider, and

considering to take to heart three things,
ô how carefull wouldst thou be that thy
God were alwayes serued by thee here on
earth, faithfully, freely, heartily, and diligently,
as he is by his Angels in heauen?
First, couldst thou remember how these
three sacred persons of that glorious
Godhead concurred to make man, saying:
Let vs make man to our owne Image? Secondly,
couldst thou remember how
heartily and gladly, that sweete meeke
Lambe of God Iesus, offered himselfe to
the death for thee, ô how heartily wouldst
thou seek thy God, ô how gladly wouldst
thou serue him? He is without Ierusalem,
and if it had pleased him he might haue
stayed without it: alwayes saith he not
vnto his disciples:Mat. 8. 21. 
                     I must go vnto Ierusalem
and suffer many things of the Elders, and of
the high Priests and Scribes, and be slaine.
And when Peter tooke him aside, and began
to rebuke him saying: Maister pitie thy selfe,
this shall not be vnto thee.
                     Vers 22. Turneth not blessed
Iesus backe this saying vnto Peter: Get
thee behind me Satan, thou art an offence vnto
me, because thou vnder stands not the things
which are of God, but the things which are of
men. Telling vs by these two things: first,

that he knew very well what would befall
him at Ierusalem: Secondly, that he
went vp most willingly thither, to the
end that he might suffer these things
there. Hast thou not, ô my soule, considered
the 15. and 16. verses of the 22. of

desired to eate this Passc
                           •
                        uer with you
before I suffer, for I say vnto you hence forth

some Passeouers before that time with
them, yet he neuer longed to eate any of
those as he longed to eate this immediatly

                     Ioh. 12. 17. 
                     but therefore came I into this
houre. Yea, to close this point, pained it

                     Ioh. 10. 17. 18. 
                     No man taketh
it from me, but I lay it downe of my selfe.
Shouldst thou not then seeke this Iesus,
serue, this Iesus, both of purpose and with
pleasure, who of purpose and with pleasure
came to seeke and to serue thee?
Thirdly, couldst thou consider, ô my
soule, how frankly and willingly wicked
men do serue the diuell, wouldst thou not
be ashamed, yea afraid, if thou finde not
thy selfe seruing thy blessed maker and
sweet Redeemer, as frankly and willingly,
as these do serue that euill one? Hath any
wicked man receiued that, from that euill
one, which thou, ô my soule, hast receiued
from thy good God? Hath that euill one
done or suffered that for any wicked man,
which thy God hath done and suffered
for thee? yea can any wicked man expect
that from the hands of that euill one,
which thou, ô my soule, mayst expect and
must expect from the hands of thy God?
The sense hereof moued Chrisostome to
say: Turpe est impios diabolo tam strenuò seruire;
                     Chrysost.
                     Christianos Christo, pro pretio redemptionis
nihil respondere, It is a shame that wicked
men should so diligently and carefully

serue the diuell, and that Christians should
recompence Christ with no good seruice, for
the price of their redemption. Fourthly,
couldst thou remember, ô my soule, how
willingly, how ioyfully, thou seruedst thy
owne lustes before thy conuersion, and so
before thy God called thee from that
damnable darknesse of ignorance, of infidelitie,
and of impietie (vnder the which
thou layest being in the first Adam) vnto
this marueilous light of knowledge, of
faith, and of begunne holinesse, wherewith
thou art now happily adorned, being
in that second Adam; wouldst thou not be
ashamed not to serue thy good holy God
after thy conuersion, as willingly and readily
as before thy cōuersion thou seruedst
thy wicked and vile flesh? O would to
God that euery man had that grace bestowed
vpon him, wherewith Paul was
happily inriched before his conuersion,
when he knew not Iesus, he ranne on foot
and horse in euery place where he came
like a furious lyon presenting those who
called vpon his name. But after his conuersion
I thinke he was as forward to
preach Iesus for the conuersion and sauing
of Christians; as he was furions before his

conuersion to persecute them for the profession
of his name. Bernard thinking vppon
this point, directs his speech thus to
thee ô my soule: Erubesce anima, conuersa
ad Dominum,
                     Bern. ep. 34. 
                     minori affectu sectari iustitiam,
quam iniquitatem antea sectata es: Causa
enim est valde dissimilis, pudeat proinde negligentius
in vitam, quam prius in mortem ire,
& minori studio salut is acquirere, quam perauionis
aug
                           •
                        mentum. Be ashamed, ô soule
conuerted to the Lord, to follow after righteousnesse
with lesse care and affection then before
thou followedst after wickednesse: for the
cause is verie vnlike, wherefore let it ashame
thee to runne more negligently after life, then
thou walkedst before after death, to seeke the
increase of saluation with lesse care then thou
soughtst before the augmentation of thy owne
perdition. Bernard againe out of the sense
of this doth crie sweetly and chearfully:
Curramus non passibus corporis; sed affectibus,
sed desiderij

                        ,
                     Bern. Med. 
                     sed suspirijs. Quoniam non
solum Angeli,
                     cap. 6. 
                     sed Angelorum Creator, nos
expectat; expectat nos Deus Pater, tanquam
filios, & haeredes, vt constituat nos super omnia
bona sua; expectat nos Deus tanquam fratres
& cohaeredes, vt fructum suae natiuit atis
& pretium sui sanguinis Deo Patri offerat:

expectat nos Spiritus sanctus, cuius templum
sumus. Let vs runne not vpon the feete of our
bodie, but vpon our affections, but vpon our
desires, but vpon our sighes and sobs, because
not onely the Angels, but the great maker of
the Angels expects and awaites for vs. God
the Father expects and waites for vs, as for
his sonnes and heires, to the end he may make
vs maisters of all his goods. The Sonne of God
awaites for vs, as for his brethren and heires
annexed with him, to the end that he may
offer and present vnto God his Father the
fruite of his natiuitie, and the price of his
bloud. The holy Spirit awaites for vs, as
for his temple in the which he dwelleth here.
O when shall the loose Christians of this
our time take that to heart which Bernard
wrote long ago for the wakening of sleeping
Christians, and for the punishing of
such toward that Inne of heauen, who
looking for it step neuer a foote forward
to the end that they may obtaine it? Qui
in schola Christi non profecit,
                     Bern. ep. 34. 
                     eius indignus est
magisterio; praesertim tamen cum simus ibi
vbi nihil in eodem statu permaneat, & non
proficere sine dubio deficere est. Nemo igitur
dicat satis est, sic volo manere; in via residet
qui eiusmodi est, in scala subsistit vbi neminem

Patriarcha vidit, non ascendentem, aut descendentem.
He who profits not in the schoole of
Christ, is vnworthie to haue him for his maister,
but specially seeing we are there, where
nothing remaineth in that same estate: and
where if men profit not by going forward,
they must receiue hurt by falling backward.
Let no man therefore say, it is enough I will
abide as I am; he who is such an one sits still in
the way, and stayes, without any motion on that
ladder, where that Patriarch saw none but
such, who was either going vp or going downe.
Let me be carefull therefore, ô my soule,
to walke with God with Enoch, to walke
before God with Abraham, while I liue
here; denying vngodlinesse and worldly
lusts, and liuing holily, righteously, and
soberly in this present world, not regarding
where I die; not regarding how I
die: for that is a taske almightie God
hath not committed to my consideration
but which he hath absolutely kept in his
owne hands, willing me to be alwayes
carefull to trie how I liue, but no wayes
to be curious where, or after what manner
I shall die. For I assure thee, ô my
soule,August. that that of Augustine shall euer
stand vndoubtedly true. Vndecunque mors

piae, bona est. W
                           •
                        ence so euer death cometh to
the godly soule, his death is good: & therefore
Augustine most wisely and louingly,August. doth
thus strengthen and incourage the honest
heart of the religious Christian walking
with God, before God, against all feare of
all death, and euerie sort of death. Noli
timere, non potest male mori qui bene vixerit.
Feare not ô good Christian he cannot possibly
die euill, who hath liued well.
                  
                  
                     THE CONCLVSION.
                     Let it not grieue thee then, ô my soule, y•
that same day is hid vp from thee; that in
some place vnknowne to thee, thou must
lay downe this dustie tabernacle, wherewith
thou hast for some yeares bene cloathed,
as with a garment. But see that thou
(being now happily ingrafted in Christ
and through his grace dying to sinne daily
for the which he died, and liuing to him
who died for thee and rose againe) euen
with an holy desire (submitting alwayes
thy will to the good will of God) long
for that day with that great Apostle, and
when that day shall draw neere. I charge
thee, ô my soule, that in that day thou
lift vp thy selfe, and reioyce. What wise
man being wearied all the day long with

laboures abroad, will grieue to draw
home at night; first to refresh himselfe
with some entertainement, and therefore
laying aside his garments to go to his
rest; knowing that (so pleasing God)
when the morning shall arise he will find
his garment againe. And darest thou, ô
my soule, be aggrieued when that night of
death shall approach, all thy wearie labours
sustained by thee here being finished,
to lay downe thy clay bodie, and to
haue thy selfe conueyed by those Angels
of God vnto that refreshing palace of
that Paradise which is aboue now, wide
open to receiue and to retaine thee, because
of the obedience of that same Adam
who died for thee? Yea, darest thou, ô
my soule, be grieued in that night of
death, to haue this clay bodie conueyed
to that resting bed of the graue, sweetly
now perfumed by the buriall of the sacred
bodie of thy gracious Sauiour Iesus? for
knowest thou not, when that glorious
bright shining morning of Iudgement
shall approach, in the which that mightie
God thy Sauiour, whom the heauens do
now containe, shall manifest himselfe in
glorie, accompanied with thousands of

his Angels, and of the sound of the last
Trumpet, that thou shalt not onely find
that wanted garment of thy bodie, but
take it vp againe, and put it on againe?
alwayes not as men take vp their garments
here in the morning, after their
rest in the night, but farre otherwise; more
comfortably, ioyfully, and profitably, by
a thousand thousand degrees; as men here
lay aside their garments at night going
to their rest, so they take them vp in the
morning, and taking them vp they go
forth againe, either to their wonted or to
some new labour. But I must tell thee, ô
my soule, to thy great comfort, that thou
shalt take vp this tabernacle of my bodie,
in that shining morning of Iudgement,
in a farre more excellent estate then it
was layed downe in the chamber of the
graue.1. Cor. 15. 42. 43. 44. It was layed downe in corruption,
it shall be taken vp in incorruption: It
was layed downe in dishonour, it shall be
taken vp in glorie: It was layed downe
in weakenesse, it shall be taken vp in
power: It was layed downe naturall, it
shall be taken vp spirituall. Could this be
well considered, ô my soule, would I
cease while I liue here, to employ all the

members of my bodie holily, and when
death should approach me, would I not
be heartily contented with ioy to lay
downe this earthly tabernacle? Againe I
will assure thee, ô my soule, (because so
hath my Lord, and Maister Iesus, by the
sweetest words of his owne sweetest lips
assured me) that thou hauing in that day
of Iudgement taken vp, and put on that
garment of this bodie, shalt neuer go
forth to any old, or new labours againe;
but shalt alwayes rest in endlesse rest for
euermore, free of all suspition of future
griefes, and filled with a verie sea of inexpressible
glorie; for in that day thou being
happily presented a chast virgine,
well decked and trimmed with the ornaments
of thy glorious husband Iesus, before
thy glorious husband Iesus, shalt
haue that marriage now contracted with
him, solemnized and perfectly consummated;
and then thy blessed husband hauing
wiped away all teares from thine
eyes, shall take thee into his most secret
cabinate of glorie,2. Cor 11. 2. there not onely to see
but to possesse for euer, that glorie which
he possessed before the world was made.
Could this be well weighed by thee, ô my

soule,Psal. 42. 1. wouldst thou not crie with Dauid?
As the Hart brayeth for the riuers of waters
so panteth my soule for thee ô God. My soule
thirsteth for God, euen for the liuing God;
when shall I come and appeare before the presence
of God? yea, wouldst thou not crie
with Paul.
                        Rom. 7. 24. 
                        O wretched man that I am who
shall deliuer me from this bodie of death, I
desire to be loosed and to be with Christ, which
is the best of all. Yea, wouldst thou not crie
with Augustine,
                        August. sol. 
                        Eia Domine, moriar vt te
videam,
                        cap. 1. 
                        videam te vt hic moriar; nolo viuere,
volo mori, dissolui cupio & esse cum Christo,
mori desidero vt videam Christum. Viuere
renuo vt viuam cum Christo. God my sweet
Lord, Let me die to the end I may see thee;
let me see thee, to the end I may die here. I
will not liue, I will die here, I desire to be desolued
and to be with Christ. I desire to die to
the end that I may see Christ, I refuse to liue,
to the end that I may liue with Christ. And
to conclude, ô my soule, (praying my
God to blesse thee with the longing and
earnest desire of Dauid, of Paul, & of Augustine)
wouldest thou not crie vncessantly
with the Church, Christs bride,
Come Lord Iesus: Euen so,
come quickly. Amen,
                     FINIS.
